[GITA:2525] 44                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:2526] Attachment Causes Misery
[GITA:2528] _mÌmñnem©ñVw H$m¡ÝVo` erVmoîUgwIXw…IXm… Ÿ&
[GITA:2529] AmJ_mnm{`Zmo@{ZË`mñVm§pñV{Vjñd ^maV Ÿ&& 14Ÿ&&
[GITA:2531] Do sense organs and sensory objects cause one to exper ience cold or
[GITA:2532] heat, happiness, or sadness? No. One experiences temporary happiness or
[GITA:2533] sadness when these are accompanied by attachment. O Bharata! Rid
[GITA:2534] yourself of attachment which is the real reason for happiness or sadness.
[GITA:2535] (2.14)
[GITA:2537] Comments: If Arjuna’s d istress is due to him not being able to
[GITA:2538] interact with his near and dear ones after they die in war, the Lord states
[GITA:2539] that such distress is due to attachment. Interaction of sense organs with
[GITA:2540] sensory objects do es not in itself  cause happiness or sadness. It is only
[GITA:2541] when such interaction is accompanied by attachment to the physical body
[GITA:2542] does one experience happiness or sadness. Krishna uses the example of
[GITA:2543] heat and cold as sensory objects that cause pleasure or misery when they
[GITA:2544] encounter one’s skin (the only se nse organ that covers one’s entire body).
[GITA:2545] A cool breeze in summer may cause pleasure but the same breeze in winter
[GITA:2546] would cause discomfort. The difference is because of one’s attachment to
[GITA:2547] the body. A gain, when one is asleep one does not feel distress in th e
[GITA:2548] presence of an object that would emit an unpleasant sound. However, when
[GITA:2549] that person is awake the same sound would be objectionable. Krishna
[GITA:2550] advises Arjuna to wage the just war and rid himself of attachment to his
[GITA:2551] loved ones which is causing him distress.
[GITA:2553] `§ {h Z ì`W`ÝË`oVo nwéf§ nwéff©^ Ÿ&
[GITA:2554] g_Xw…IgwI§ Yra§ gmo@_¥VËdm` H$ënVo Ÿ&& 15 Ÿ&&
[GITA:2556] O Arjuna, Superior among men! One, who is equipoised in
[GITA:2557] happiness or sadness caused due to attachment to sense organs and sense
[GITA:2558] objects, is indeed eligible for liberation. (2.15)
[GITA:2571] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      45
[GITA:2573] Comments: Arjuna could argue that one way for him to avoid
[GITA:2574] distress would be to avoid waging the war which could result in loss of
[GITA:2575] loved ones. In this case, the issue of attachment does not arise. So, why not
[GITA:2576] avoid the war? Lord Krishna says tha t waging a just war is Arjuna’s duty
[GITA:2577] and the way that Arjuna can avoid distress is by ridding himself of
[GITA:2578] attachment to his near and dear ones. Such an action will also result in
[GITA:2579] Arjuna achieving liberation hereafter.
[GITA:2581] ZmgVmo {dÚVo@^mdmo Zm^mdmo {dÚVo gV… Ÿ&
[GITA:2582] C^`moa{n Ñï>mo@ÝVñËdZ`moñVÎdX{e©{^… Ÿ&& 16 Ÿ&&
[GITA:2584] No good comes out of bad deeds. Also, there are no bad results from
[GITA:2585] good deeds. The learned seers who have realized the Lord Almighty are
[GITA:2586] convinced of these two facts. (2.16)
[GITA:2588] Comments: Arjuna has expressed concern that he will incur sins by
[GITA:2589] killing elders and teachers during the war. However, these elders are on the
[GITA:2590] side of evil and it is Arjuna’s duty to fight for justice. In this verse, Krishna
[GITA:2591] says that no sin is incurred by performing good deeds.
[GITA:2593] There is a second meaning to this verse as stated by Sri Rayaru
[GITA:2594] [GV]- Inert nature is not subject to creation and destruction , and hence is
[GITA:2595] eternal. The Lord Almighty is also eternal and indestructible.  These two
[GITA:2596] concepts have been traditionally taught by knowledgeable seers.
[GITA:2598] How can one say that inert matter and the Lord Almighty are eternal,
[GITA:2599] and not subject to creation and dissolution? Sri Rayaru [GV] provides an
[GITA:2600] answer by referring to the first line of this verse where  - asat refers to
[GITA:2601] prime material natur e, sat refers to the Lord Almighty , abhava refers to
[GITA:2602] prag abhava  and pradhwamsa abhava , and na vidyate  means ‘does not
[GITA:2603] exist’. This means that prime matter and the Lord Almighty do not have the
[GITA:2604] conditions of the above abhava twins. Thus, the two entities a re said to be
[GITA:2605] eternal.
[GITA:2618] 46                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:2619] What are the abhava twins? This can be explained with an example.
[GITA:2620] Before a potter creates a pot out of clay, the pot is said to have the
[GITA:2621] condition of prior non -existence ( prag abhava ). When such a pot is
[GITA:2622] destroyed, the pot is in th e condition of post non -existence ( pradhwamsa
[GITA:2623] abhava). The material cause for the creation of the universe is inert nature.
[GITA:2624] The Lord Almighty is the instrumental cause for the creation of the
[GITA:2625] universe. Inert nature and the Lord Almighty are not subject to the
[GITA:2626] conditions of prior non -existence (prag abhava ) and post non -existence
[GITA:2627] (pradhwamsa abhava), and thus are not subject to creation or destruction.
[GITA:2629] Sri Rayaru [GV] quotes Sri Narahari Teertha [GBBPN] who in his
[GITA:2630] commentary on the  Gita had an additional i nterpretation for the use of the
[GITA:2631] word ‘api’ (meaning ‘also’) in this verse. This word when combined with
[GITA:2632] the phrase ‘learned seers’, implies that the eternality of inert nature and the
[GITA:2633] Lord Almighty is known through the traditional teachings of learned see rs
[GITA:2634] and through scriptural evidence from the epic Vishnu Purana.
[GITA:2636] Sri Vishwesha Teertha in his Gita Saroddhara [GS] provides a third
[GITA:2637] interpretation for the first line in this verse by applying the concept s to
[GITA:2638] living beings – the p hysical body that is subject to birth  is not perishable
[GITA:2639] (as it is perishable) and the unborn soul does not perish.
[GITA:2641] Eternal, Indestructible Soul reflects the Lord
[GITA:2643] A{dZm{e Vw VX²{d{Õ `oZ gd©{_X§ VV_² Ÿ&
[GITA:2644] {dZme_ì``ñ`mñ` Z H${üV² H$Vw©_h©{V Ÿ&& 17 Ÿ&&
[GITA:2646] Know that entities that pervade the universe will not perish . No one
[GITA:2647] can cause destruction to the imperishable. (2.17)
[GITA:2649] Comments: The entities referred to are not subject to decay and
[GITA:2650] hence are imperishable and eternal. These entities include the Lord
[GITA:2651] Almighty, individual souls, space (avyakrita akasha) and the letters ( the 51
[GITA:2652] letters in the Sanskrit alphabet). Space is known as avyakrita akasha as it
[GITA:2664] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      47
[GITA:2666] does not undergo transformation during creation or dissolution. It is single,
[GITA:2667] eternal, and self-supporting.
[GITA:2669] AÝVdÝV B_o Xohm {ZË`ñ`moº$m… ear[aU… Ÿ&
[GITA:2670] AZm{eZmo@à_o`ñ` Vñ_mX² ¶wÜ`ñd ^maV Ÿ&& 18 &&
[GITA:2672] O Bharata! It is said that the eternal soul’s visible physical body is
[GITA:2673] perishable, but the Lord Almighty, the Supreme Soul, is imperishable (not
[GITA:2674] subject to four-way destruction). Hence , fight this war  as worship to the
[GITA:2675] indwelling Lord Aprameya, the one who is not limited by space, time, or
[GITA:2676] attributes. (2.18)
[GITA:2678] Comments: The individual soul is a reflection of the Lord as in a
[GITA:2679] mirror. Some argue that when the mirror which they consider is upadhi (the
[GITA:2680] conditioning medium) is destroyed, the reflection no longer exists. Sri
[GITA:2681] Rayaru [GV] explains that the upadhi in the example of a reflection in the
[GITA:2682] mirror is the intrinsic body of the individual soul and not the physical body.
[GITA:2683] The intrinsic body ( swaroopa deha)  of a soul never perishes. The Lord is
[GITA:2684] eternal, has no blemishes, does not experience decay or destruction of
[GITA:2685] body, as His body is transcendental. The individual soul’s intrinsic body is
[GITA:2686] also indestructible, and  in that sense, the individual soul is deemed  to have
[GITA:2687] some similarity with the Lord. Hence the intrinsic body of the individual
[GITA:2688] soul is the upadhi in the example of comparing the Lord and the individual
[GITA:2689] soul to the original and the mirror reflection. Also, if the Lord Almighty
[GITA:2690] and individual souls ha ve similar attributes such as indestructibility, then
[GITA:2691] why should one perform duties as a worship to the Lord? Firstly, the
[GITA:2692] individual soul is dependent on the Lord and secondly, the Lord has special
[GITA:2693] characteristics far and beyond those of individual souls.  The Lord pervades
[GITA:2694] everywhere. Sri Rayaru also states [GV] that the Lord is not subject to the
[GITA:2695] fourfold destruction – (i) of the body  (as His body is transcendental), (ii) of
[GITA:2696] the soul (as He is eternal), (iii) of attributes (as He is full of infinite
[GITA:2697] auspicious attributes and is devoid of any blemishes) and (iv) of happiness
[GITA:2698] (as He is devoid of misery). He is superior to ind ividual souls and hence is
[GITA:2699] worthy of worship.
[GITA:2711] 48                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:2713] ` EZ§ do{Îm hÝVma§ `ü¡Z§ _Ý`Vo hV_² Ÿ&
[GITA:2714] C^m¡ Vm¡ Z {dOmZrVmo Zm`§ hpÝV Z hÝ`Vo Ÿ&& 19 &&
[GITA:2716] One who thinks that one person has killed another person and the
[GITA:2717] one who thinks that th e second person has been killed - neither ha s true
[GITA:2718] knowledge. No one can kill anyone else, and no one can be killed. (2.19)
[GITA:2720] Comments: Arjuna’s distress is premised o n his assumption that he
[GITA:2721] may kill his elders and teachers in the war. However, no one can
[GITA:2722] independently kill someone or get killed by someone. Further, no one
[GITA:2723] experiences destruction of their soul, and the Lord is the only independent
[GITA:2724] entity. Hence, Arjuna’s grief is misplaced.
[GITA:2726] Z Om`Vo {_«`Vo dm H$Xm{MÞm`§ ^yËdm ^{dVm dm Z ^y`… Ÿ&

[GITA:2734] Comments: This verse has origins in the Katha Upanishat  and

[GITA:2737] A second interpretation of this verse is as follows: The Lord does not
[GITA:2738] experience bodily birth and death. All His incarnations such as Rama  and
[GITA:2739] Krishna are eternal, and from time to time He manifests Himself and makes
[GITA:2740] Himself visible or invisible. The aspect of the Lord manifesting and making
[GITA:2741] Himself visible is generally termed as His birth.
[GITA:2743] Many scriptures have references to the Lord being in the womb of
[GITA:2744] His mother (for example Krishna being in the womb of Devaki) before

[GITA:2757] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      49
[GITA:2759] where the Lord continues to exist with infinite auspicious attributes and His
[GITA:2760] condition is not like that of mortals who suffer in their mother’s womb.
[GITA:2762] doXm{dZm{eZ§ {ZË`§ ` EZ_O_ì``_² Ÿ&

[GITA:2765] O Partha! One who knows that the soul is eternal, that it does not
[GITA:2766] perish, that it has no birth or death; how can that person cause death to
[GITA:2767] someone and/or kill someone. (2.21)
[GITA:2769] Comments: The word ‘vinasha’ also means weakness such as hatred
[GITA:2770] which is caused by attachment. The soul does not have these defects
[GITA:2771] intrinsically, but a person gets them due to attachment. A wise person who
[GITA:2772] does not have such defects ( avinashi) will know the true nature of
[GITA:2773] individual souls and the Supreme Soul and will know that no one can cause
[GITA:2774] death to someone else.

[GITA:2880] O Bharata! Living beings get a body between birth and death from
[GITA:2881] inert, material nature and th e body will merge back with inert nature after

[GITA:2895] 52                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:2896] Comments: While it was made clear that everyone experiences birth
[GITA:2897] and death due to their physical bodies, what causes birth and death? This
[GITA:2898] verse reveals that birth and death are caused by interaction with material
[GITA:2899] nature. The physical body is made up of a certain proportion of the five
[GITA:2900] basic elements of nature. When a soul gets a body from material nature it is
[GITA:2901] termed as birth, and when it loses the body and is back to material nature, it
[GITA:2902] is termed as death. A soul that is dependent on the Lord has no control over
[GITA:2903] the process of birth and death. So, it is not worth grieving over such a
[GITA:2904] temporary body.
[GITA:2906] After conquering the snake Kalinga, Krishna and other yadavas were
[GITA:2907] spending a night in the forest. They were faced with the onset of rapidly
[GITA:2908] approaching forest fire. Lord Krishna extinguishe d this fire by swallowing
[GITA:2909] it. Saint Sri Vadiraja [RV] describes this incident to explain the fact that all
[GITA:2910] elements of nature emanate from the Lord and submerge back into Him.
[GITA:2912] Amü`©dV² ní`{V H$[üXoZ_mü`©dX² dX{V VW¡d MmÝ`… Ÿ&

[GITA:2915] Some look at the Lord in amazement. Some talk about Him in

[GITA:2917] understand Him even after hearing a lot about Him.  (2.29)
[GITA:2919] Comments: While it was made clear previously that individual souls
[GITA:2920] are not independent, one can ask who they are dependent on. This verse
[GITA:2921] explains that the sole indepe ndent entity in the universe is the Lord
[GITA:2922] Almighty. It also answers that there are no other independent entities that
[GITA:2923] can equal the Lord. While many people can claim to know the attributes of
[GITA:2924] the Lord, this verse makes it clear that only some visualize the Lord with
[GITA:2925] amazement. Just as one cannot find any comparison to the sky or the ocean,
[GITA:2926] no one can find any comparison to the Lord. He is truly incomparable. For
[GITA:2927] one to get over grief that may arise from any activity, one must focus on
[GITA:2928] performing one’s duty as an offering to the Lord. So, it is important for one

[GITA:3172] 58                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3174] O Scion of the Kuru Dynasty (Arjuna)! There is only one tea ching
[GITA:3175] that leads to decisive spiritual knowledge. There are endless teachings that
[GITA:3176] lead the undecided ones to diverse, wrong knowledge. (2.41)
[GITA:3178] Comments: There are different teachings (often contradictory) about
[GITA:3179] spiritual knowledge. How then does one know the true path? Krishna in
[GITA:3180] this verse categorically states that only true teaching leads to proper divine
[GITA:3181] and spiritual knowledge. This is based on evidence from revered spiritual
[GITA:3182] texts such as the Vedas and is realized from following the Vaishnava path
[GITA:3183] which enunciates the supremacy of Lord Vishnu as the supreme of all
[GITA:3184] souls. In the next few verses (from 2.41 to 2.46), the Lord clears any doubts
[GITA:3185] about the true purport of the Vedas.
[GITA:3187] It is interesting to note that the Lord refers to Arjuna as
[GITA:3188] Kurunandana, meaning ‘Scion of the Kuru dynasty who would bring joy to
[GITA:3189] his lineage’, probably implying that most of  the descendants of the Kuru
[GITA:3190] dynasty such as Duryodhana and his 99 brothers belong to the type of
[GITA:3191] people who believe in various, wrong teachings . Arjuna is different and can
[GITA:3192] dispel his doubts and regain the spiritual knowledge he had already
[GITA:3193] possessed.

[GITA:3264] 60                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3265] O Arjuna! Peripherally the Vedas appear to describe rituals that
[GITA:3266] result in atta inment of heavenly and worldly fruits made up of the three
[GITA:3267] attributes. Do not aspire for these. Go beyond dualities (such as pleasure
[GITA:3268] and pain). Focus your mind on the Lord Almighty and leave it to the Lord
[GITA:3269] to help you attain your goals and to help you pro tect goals already attained.
[GITA:3270] (2.45)
[GITA:3272] Comments: The Lord continues to teach about the real purport of
[GITA:3273] the Vedas. In this verse, the Lord instructs that one should not focus on the
[GITA:3274] peripheral meaning of the Vedas that appear to provide details of rituals to
[GITA:3275] help achieve worldly fruits. These fruits and even heavens that one may
[GITA:3276] achieve are borne out of material nature which is a mixture of three
[GITA:3277] attributes – sat, rajas and tamas. As such , these are not permanent, and
[GITA:3278] even if one reaches the heavens, one is bound to fall back to earth after
[GITA:3279] expending merits from good deeds. One should detach oneself from yoga
[GITA:3280] (striving for proscribed material entities not already owned) and kshema
[GITA:3281] (protecting proscribed material entities already possessed). The real purport
[GITA:3282] of the Vedas is to describe the nature of the Lord Almighty. One should
[GITA:3283] focus on the Lord who will help one achieve everlasting bliss ( nirvana).
[GITA:3285] `mdmZW© CXnmZo gd©V… gåßbwVmoXHo$ Ÿ&
[GITA:3286] VmdmZ² gd}fw doXofw ~«m÷Uñ` {dOmZV… Ÿ&& 46 &&
[GITA:3288] The benefit derived from a small body of water such as a well is
[GITA:3289] better derived from a sumptuous water body such as an ocean. Likewise,
[GITA:3290] benefits derived from following Vedic rituals with proper meaning are
[GITA:3291] surely available for one with special knowledge who has realized the Lord
[GITA:3292] Almighty. (2.46)
[GITA:3294] Comments: In the previous verses, it was indicated that the real
[GITA:3295] purport of the Vedas is in understanding of the Lord and not in transient
[GITA:3296] material benefits including attaining the heavens. It was made clear that one
[GITA:3297] who goes by the peripheral meaning of the Vedas and performs rituals only
[GITA:3298] to attain transient material benefits will never achieve everlasting bliss. A
[GITA:3310] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      61
[GITA:3312] question arises as to whether the seeker who goes by the inner meaning of
[GITA:3313] the Vedas and realizes the Lord will be eligible for transient fruits such as
[GITA:3314] the heavens. This verse answers that question through an example. Just as
[GITA:3315] the benefits available from well water are available from a larger body of
[GITA:3316] water such as a lake or an ocean, one who has realized the Lord by proper
[GITA:3317] understanding of the Vedas will surely achieve transient benefits such as
[GITA:3318] heavens, even when one is not focused on them.
[GITA:3320] Sri Raghavendra Swamy in his Gita Vivruti [GV] provides an
[GITA:3321] explanation for the words brahmana (one who has realized the Lord) and
[GITA:3322] vijanatha (one who has special knowledge) where both appear to mean the
[GITA:3323] same thing. Sri Rayaru says that vijanatha indicates the one who has
[GITA:3324] paroksha (or indirect) knowledge of the Lord and brahmana indicates one
[GITA:3325] who has gone a step further and has realized aparoksha or direct
[GITA:3326] knowledge of the Lord. In that sense, for one to obtain direct knowledge of
[GITA:3327] the Lord, one must first start by learning the knowledge indirectly (through
[GITA:3328] a qualified teacher, studying Vedic scriptures etc.).
[GITA:3330] Sri Rayaru provides a second meaning for this verse, by interpreting
[GITA:3331] the Sanskrit terms samplutodaka and udapana differently. Earlier
[GITA:3332] samplutodaka referred to a large body of water (ex: an ocean) and udapana
[GITA:3333] referred to a small body of water (ex: well). Sri Rayaru provides a second
[GITA:3334] meaning for these terms. Samplutodaka means the ocean that dissolves the
[GITA:3335] universe during the grand dissolution and udapana refers to the Lord
[GITA:3336] Almighty who protects the eternal entities in the universe such as souls,
[GITA:3337] time etc. With this interpretation, the verse can also be translated to mean
[GITA:3338] as follows: Whatever advantage (such as dharma, moksha etc.) is obtained
[GITA:3339] through the Grace of the Lord Almighty who  protects  everything during
[GITA:3340] the great dissolution of the universe, the same advantage will be accrued by
[GITA:3341] a seeker who has realized the Lord through proper interpretation of the
[GITA:3342] Vedas.
[GITA:3357] 62                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3358] Duty is Worship
[GITA:3360] H$_©Ê`odm{YH$mañVo _m \$bofw H$XmMZ Ÿ&
[GITA:3361] _m H$_©\$bhoVw^y©_m© Vo g“moo@ñËdH$_©{U Ÿ&& 47 &&
[GITA:3363] You only have the right to do your duty, and never to its fruits.
[GITA:3364] Never p erform your duties with expectations o f outcomes. At the same
[GITA:3365] time, never think about relinquishing your duties. (2.47)
[GITA:3367] Comments: This is probably the most commented upon verse in the
[GITA:3368] Gita. It answers the question as to the purpose of performing ones’
[GITA:3369] prescribed duties when there is no guarantee of getting expected results.
[GITA:3370] Even if someone does not see any immediate material benefits from
[GITA:3371] performing ones’ prescribed duties, such actions will please the Lord. They
[GITA:3372] will result in one obtaining true knowledge about the Lord and eventually
[GITA:3373] achieving everlasting bliss. This is implied in the first line of this verse.
[GITA:3374] Another question that one can raise is the purpose of someone performing
[GITA:3375] any action at all, as earlier in verse 2.45, it was stated that one should
[GITA:3376] always focus ones mind on the Lord.  The second line of this verse answers
[GITA:3377] this question by stating that in addition to focusing the mind on the Lord,
[GITA:3378] one must perform prescribed duties; otherwise, one will accrue sins due to
[GITA:3379] relinquishing of duties. In addition to the philosophical reasons, we can all
[GITA:3380] appreciate the fact that for a society to function smoothly, every one of us
[GITA:3381] must play our assigned roles with diligence and sincerity. Such activities,
[GITA:3382] especially when performed as an offering to the Lord, will help us receive
[GITA:3383] the Lord’s grace to help us in our spiritual journey. Lord Krishna is
[GITA:3384] instructing Arjuna here that he should not shirk from his prescribed duty of
[GITA:3385] fighting for a just cause, just because he is uncomfortable with the thought
[GITA:3386] of losing his loved ones.
[GITA:3388] Sri Rayaru [GV] also provides a second meaning for this verse. He
[GITA:3389] translates the phrase ‘karma phala hetu’ (the entity responsible to grant
[GITA:3390] fruits for actions) as the Lord Almighty, as He alone can grant someone the
[GITA:3391] fruits. As per verse 2.45, one should not consider oneself identical to the
[GITA:3403] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      63
[GITA:3405] Lord as the Lord is supreme and He alone can grant one’s wishes. The
[GITA:3406] second interpretation of this verse is as follows: Arjuna! Individual souls
[GITA:3407] can only perform prescribed duties. They do not have the ability to obtain
[GITA:3408] the fruits by themselves. That ability is only with the Lord. Individual souls
[GITA:3409] are quite different and are subservient to the Lord and hence one should
[GITA:3410] never consider oneself as the Lord.
[GITA:3412] Sri Rayaru [GV] also provides convincing responses to many other
[GITA:3413] deep, philosophical questions in his interpretation of this verse. Following
[GITA:3414] is the summary:
[GITA:3416]  Even those who have already realized the Lord have to keep
[GITA:3417] performing duties.
[GITA:3418]  For one who has already realized the Lord, any additional credit
[GITA:3419] from performing duties will result in buoyant happiness in moksha
[GITA:3420] (the level of bliss in moksha is dependent on the innate capabilities
[GITA:3421] of souls, but additional credits will result in  buoyant happiness, just
[GITA:3422] like when milk boils over, the amount of milk does not change but
[GITA:3423] the milk exhibits more buoyancy)
[GITA:3424]  No one is exempt from performing one’s prescribed duties
[GITA:3425]  While this verse indicates that one should not perform duties with an
[GITA:3426] expectation of the outcome, it is not prohibited for someone to
[GITA:3427] perform activities with loftier expectations of spiritual knowledge
[GITA:3428] and the Lord’s Grace. One should avoid expectations of temporary,
[GITA:3429] transient, material fruits.
[GITA:3430]  Although phrases such as ‘swarga kamo yajeta’ prescribe rituals for
[GITA:3431] fulfilment of mundane desires, the scriptures do not mandate such
[GITA:3432] actions for fulfilment of desires.
[GITA:3433]  Major distinction between individual beings and the Lord in the
[GITA:3434] context of duties and fruits:
[GITA:3435] - Individual Beings: Have responsibility to perform duties. Cannot
[GITA:3436] grant wishes.
[GITA:3437] - Lord Almighty: Has no prescribed responsibility. Can grant
[GITA:3438] wishes.
[GITA:3450] 64                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3452] `moJñW… Hw$é H$_m©{U g“§ Ë`³Ëdm YZ§O` Ÿ&
[GITA:3453] {gÕç{gÕçmo… g_mo ^yËdm g_Ëd§ `moJ CÀ`Vo Ÿ&& 48 &&
[GITA:3455] O Dhananjaya! On your spiritual path (yoga), perform duties without
[GITA:3456] attachments and expectations of results. The real yoga is performing one’s
[GITA:3457] duties without expectations and with equanimity. (2.48)
[GITA:3459] Comments: From verses 2.48 onwards, the Lord provides more
[GITA:3460] details on the concept of nishkama karma (performing prescribed duties
[GITA:3461] without expectations).  In the previous verse 2.47, the Lord instructs Arjuna
[GITA:3462] never to think of relinquishing prescribed duties. This verse responds to the
[GITA:3463] question as to how one should perform prescribed duties. Yoga is having no
[GITA:3464] expectations of results from duties performed and being equanimous to
[GITA:3465] positive or negative outcomes. These are not two separate definitions of
[GITA:3466] yoga.
[GITA:3468] Sri Vidyasagara Madhava Teertha has provided a detailed
[GITA:3469] description of a yogi identified in this verse as –
[GITA:3471] (i) one whose mind and intellect are transfixed at the feet of the Lord
[GITA:3472] with the knowledge of the Lord’s omnipresence, omnipotence, and
[GITA:3473] omniscience.
[GITA:3474] (ii) one who engages in actions without attachment to the act itself or
[GITA:3475] the fruits of such actions.
[GITA:3476] (iii) one who engages in all activities only to please the Lord and as a
[GITA:3477] service to the Lord.
[GITA:3478] (iv) one who, knowing fully well that everything is at the will and
[GITA:3479] command of the Lord, accepts success or failure with equanimity.
[GITA:3481] XyaoU øda§ H$_© ~w{Õ`moJmX² YZ§O` Ÿ&

[GITA:3497] O Dhananjaya! Performing duties with expectation of the outcome is
[GITA:3498] very inferior to the task of attaining divine spiritual knowledge. Wretched
[GITA:3499] are those whose motive is fruit of the action. Focus your mind on spiritual
[GITA:3500] knowledge. (2.49)
[GITA:3502] Comments: In 2.46, it was indicated that one should avoid
[GITA:3503] performing Vedic rituals for temporary gains but instead focus on the inner
[GITA:3504] meaning of the Vedas to attain proper spiritual knowledge. In that sense,
[GITA:3505] performing duties with expectation of material outcome is inferior to the
[GITA:3506] task of attaining divine knowledge. This verse answers the question as to
[GITA:3507] the reason for this distinction. One who is focused only on activities
[GITA:3508] yielding temporary gains will realize sooner or later that such gains will not
[GITA:3509] last and will start feeling miserable. Hence there is no point in performing
[GITA:3510] activities with such expectations.
[GITA:3512] Sri Rayaru [GV] also provides an alternate interpretation for the
[GITA:3513] second half of this verse in response to a question as to whether someone
[GITA:3514] who has already attained spiritual knowledge can consider himself as one
[GITA:3515] with the Lord. By interpreting the phrase phala hetava (the one who grants
[GITA:3516] wishes) as referring to the Lord, Sri Rayaru says that even those who have
[GITA:3517] attained spiritual knowledge will not claim identity with the Lord as such a
[GITA:3518] claim would lead to unending misery.

[GITA:3523] One who has realized the Lord Almighty will be rid of the
[GITA:3524] consequences of good or bad deeds. Therefore, focus on performing your
[GITA:3525] duties with the goal of achieving divine, spiritual knowledge. This is the
[GITA:3526] best path. (2.50)
[GITA:3528] Comments: In the previous verse 2.49, it was indicated that
[GITA:3529] activities performed with expectations of material gains are inferior to the
[GITA:3530] activities pursued in attaining divine knowledge.
[GITA:3542] 66                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3544] That technique which steers one clear of worldly entanglement and
[GITA:3545] ushers one towards the transcendental is ‘skill in action’ (karmasu
[GITA:3546] kauśalam). In this verse, some of the special advantages of these superior
[GITA:3547] activities are outlined. It is indicated that one who has realized the Lord
[GITA:3548] will be rid of the consequences of good and bad deeds which is the
[GITA:3549] essential last step in achieving moksha. A question that would arise
[GITA:3550] naturally is about the reason for consequences of even good deeds to be
[GITA:3551] nullified. Sri Rayaru in GV provides an answer. Good deeds are of two
[GITA:3552] kinds – first one that leads to more clarity on divine knowledge and more
[GITA:3553] exuberant happiness in moksha (ishta punya), and second ones (anishta
[GITA:3554] punya) that do not. Credits from good deeds of the second kind must be
[GITA:3555] used up in this world (in current or future births) while credits from the first
[GITA:3556] kind of good deed will be carried forward till one achieves moksha. The
[GITA:3557] Lord categorically states that among all activities, those that lead to
[GITA:3558] attainment of divine knowledge are supreme.
[GITA:3560] Sri Rayaru [GV] provides a second interpretation for the second half
[GITA:3561] of this verse. One can ask the question - If one feels that one can put in all
[GITA:3562] required efforts to attain spiritual knowledge (which is the goal for
[GITA:3563] achieving moksha), why should one perform activities without expectations
[GITA:3564] on material outcomes? Sri Rayaru answers saying that only activities that
[GITA:3565] are performed for the sole purpose of pleasing the Lord and obtaining
[GITA:3566] divine knowledge will lead to moksha.
[GITA:3568] Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha Swamiji in his Gita Saroddhara [BGS]
[GITA:3569] indicates that this verse reflects the summary of entire chapter 2. This is
[GITA:3570] very appropriate as in this chapter Arjuna in verses 2.4 to 2.8 had expressed
[GITA:3571] the conflict in his mind about his course of action and requested Krishna
[GITA:3572] for guidance. Krishna categorically states in this verse that one needs to
[GITA:3573] perform ones prescribed duty with the goal of achieving divine, spiritual
[GITA:3574] knowledge and that Arjuna needs to engage himself in fighting this holy
[GITA:3575] war to protect his citizens.

[GITA:3633] 68                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3634] Once you develop conviction in spiritual teachings, your mind will
[GITA:3635] become steadfast. At that time, you will be able to follow the path of divine
[GITA:3636] knowledge. (2.53)
[GITA:3638] Comments: In 2.52, it was indicated that one must rid oneself of
[GITA:3639] ignorant viewpoints. In this verse, the questions about what ignorant
[GITA:3640] viewpoints really are and how one could be rid of them are answered.
[GITA:3641] Ignorant viewpoints are those that are not supported by authentic scriptures
[GITA:3642] such as the Vedas. Ones who have developed strong conviction about
[GITA:3643] teachings from scriptures such as the Vedas will be able to rid themselves
[GITA:3644] of ignorant viewpoints without any doubt. They will then be ready to focus
[GITA:3645] their minds on the Lord which will lead to eternal bliss through the grace of
[GITA:3646] the Lord.
[GITA:3648] Sri Rayaru [GV] provides a second interpretation of this verse based
[GITA:3649] on Sri Madhwacharya’s commentary in GTN where the phrase ‘shruti
[GITA:3650] vipratipanna’ is interpreted alternately as ‘shruti visheshena pratipanna’ to
[GITA:3651] mean – one with the right viewpoint based on authentic scriptures (shruti).
[GITA:3652] Based on this, the verse can be interpreted to mean the following – The one
[GITA:3653] who has realized the Lord based on proper understanding of the Vedas will
[GITA:3654] have one’s mind firmly placed on the Lord and will eventually attain
[GITA:3655] moksha through the Lord’s grace.

[GITA:3663] Arjuna said: O Keshava! What are the characteristics of a person
[GITA:3664] who has developed unwavering conviction in divine, spiritual knowledge
[GITA:3665] (Stita Prajna)? How does that person talk or sit or walk (in other words,
[GITA:3666] why does that person need to engage in any activity)? (2.54)
[GITA:3679] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      69
[GITA:3681] Comments: This is perhaps one of the most widely quoted verse
[GITA:3682] from the Gita. After listening to the Lord’s teachings about the need for
[GITA:3683] one to perform prescribed duties without expectations, focusing the mind
[GITA:3684] on the Lord and related topics, Arjuna is now curious to know the
[GITA:3685] characteristics of a person who has developed unwavering conviction
[GITA:3686] (tranquil mind) in divine knowledge. It is interesting that he uses the term
[GITA:3687] ‘bhasha’ to mean characteristics instead of the more common word
[GITA:3688] ‘lakshana’. Arjuna, by using the term ‘samadhi’ (state of complete mental
[GITA:3689] concentration on the Lord), has himself defined a characteristic (lakshana)
[GITA:3690] of a person with deep conviction in divine knowledge. By using the word
[GITA:3691] ‘bhasha’, Arjuna is enquiring about the characteristic of such a person
[GITA:3692] when that person is out of samadhi and is engaged in normal day to day
[GITA:3693] activities. References to talking, sitting, walking etc., in this verse here
[GITA:3694] imply normal day today activities. In other words, Arjuna wants to know
[GITA:3695] how the person with firm resolve performs day to day activities (when not
[GITA:3696] in state of samadhi).
[GITA:3698] Sri Rayaru [GV] also provides a second interpretation for this verse
[GITA:3699] as follows: Why does one who has achieved divine knowledge need to
[GITA:3700] perform activities such as talking, sitting, walking etc.? Here the word
[GITA:3701] ‘kim’ is used to mean ‘why’. In that sense it is a rhetorical question. Why
[GITA:3702] should someone who has already achieved the state of samadhi and has
[GITA:3703] developed unwavering conviction in the Lord indulge in any mundane, day
[GITA:3704] to day worldly activities?
[GITA:3706] The Lord responds to Arjuna’s questions in the remaining verses of
[GITA:3707] this chapter which undoubtedly form the core teachings of the Gita.

[GITA:3724] 70                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:3725] The Lord said: O Partha! One who has conquered mental blemishes
[GITA:3726] such as desire and has focused mind on the Lord Almighty will achieve
[GITA:3727] mental tranquility by the grace of the Lord. (2.55)
[GITA:3729] Comments: The Lord answers Arjuna’s question 2.54, from 2.55
[GITA:3730] onwards till the end of this chapter. For the rhetorical question in the
[GITA:3731] second line of 2.54, the Lord answers in verse 2.69. While desire is
[GITA:3732] mentioned as a blemish that one needs to conquer, this also applies to other
[GITA:3733] blemishes such as greed, anger, hatred etc. Note that desire here refers to
[GITA:3734] worldly desires and not lofty desires such as achieving divine knowledge.
[GITA:3735] Sri Rayaru [GV] explains the special reason for the use of the word
[GITA:3736] ‘manogatan’ (mental) in this verse. Blemishes such as desire, greed, anger
[GITA:3737] etc., originate in the mind. That being the case, what is the reason for using
[GITA:3738] the qualifier ‘mental’ in ‘mental blemishes’? The divine knowledge that
[GITA:3739] one would attain by the grace of the Lord also manifests in the same mind.
[GITA:3740] For the same mind to attain divine knowledge, it is necessary to be rid of
[GITA:3741] worldly blemishes. It is to drive home the fact that  divine knowledge also
[GITA:3742] resides in the same mind that the qualifier ‘mental’ is used in this verse.
[GITA:3744] In verse 2.39, the Lord started out saying that He would teach the
[GITA:3745] path (yoga) to obtain divine knowledge. However, in this verse, He is
[GITA:3746] teaching the characteristics of a yogi who has already attained divine
[GITA:3747] knowledge. How can this be reconciled? Sri Rayaru [GV] states that for a
[GITA:3748] seeker interested in traversing the path towards divine knowledge, it is
[GITA:3749] important to learn about the characteristics of yogis who have already
[GITA:3750] successfully traversed that path.

[GITA:3770] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      71

[GITA:3775] extended to include other blemishes such as obsession, fear, and anger.

[GITA:3780] One with deep conviction in divine, spiritual knowledge (aparoksha

[GITA:3784] Comments: The reason for this equanimity in both pleasure and
[GITA:3785] discomfort in such a person is the lack of attachment to worldly issues.
[GITA:3787] The previous verse 2.56 identified the absence of anger as one of the
[GITA:3788] characteristics of a person with mental tranquility and this verse indicates
[GITA:3789] the absence of hatred during distress as another characteristic. Sri Jaya
[GITA:3790] Teertha in his PD clarifies that there is no repetition here as the absence of
[GITA:3791] hatred in 2.57 refers to all situations (due to the use of the word sarvatrāg)
[GITA:3792] including those where there may be reasons for such hatred.

[GITA:3797] A person of steady wisdom can easily withdraw sense organs away

[GITA:3800] Comments: A person with mental tranquility can control sense
[GITA:3801] organs from indulging in objects of sensory pleasures such as sound, touch,
[GITA:3802] form, taste, and smell. The image of the tortoise which withdraws its limbs
[GITA:3803] at will is used to signify the ease with which such a person is able to control
[GITA:3804] sense organs.

[GITA:3821] By fasting, one can reduce the ability of one’s body to consume and
[GITA:3822] digest food, but not the cravings to indulge in tasty food. Those cravings
[GITA:3823] can only be diminished by realizing the Lord Almighty. (2.59)
[GITA:3825] Comments: The next 3 verses are about sense control. By practicing
[GITA:3826] self-discipline such as fasting, one experiences reduced power in the five
[GITA:3827] sense organs of perception such as eyes, ears, nose, tongue, and skin.
[GITA:3828] However, the craving experienced by the mind to indulge in sense
[GITA:3829] pleasures does not diminish. This can only happen when one experiences a
[GITA:3830] vision of Lord Almighty.
[GITA:3832] Sri Rayaru [GV] also provides an alternate meaning to this verse by
[GITA:3833] interpreting the word ‘rasa varjam’ to mean desires in objects of all
[GITA:3834] sensory pleasures except taste. This means that by fasting one may
[GITA:3835] experience loss of desire in the objects of sense pleasures such as sound,
[GITA:3836] form, smell, and touch but not in the sense object of taste. This can only be
[GITA:3837] overcome when one experiences a vision of Lord Almighty. This
[GITA:3838] interpretation is also consistent with practical experience as when one ages
[GITA:3839] and loses power and interest in seeing, listening, hearing etc., the desire to
[GITA:3840] taste good food never goes away.  In summary, a seeker should strive to
[GITA:3841] achieve control over all sense organs and mind.

[GITA:3846] O Son of Kunti! It is the nature of sense organs to get attracted to
[GITA:3847] sense pleasures. Despite many efforts, even learned ones experience their
[GITA:3848] sense organs swaying strongly. (2.60)
[GITA:3850] Comments: If one can understand that one needs to control one’s
[GITA:3851] sense organs from indulging in sense pleasures (discipline in consumption -
[GITA:3863] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      73
[GITA:3865] pratyahara) and focus one’s minds on attaining spiritual knowledge, one
[GITA:3866] may be able to conquer their sense organs. In that case why should one
[GITA:3867] undertake difficult activities such as fasting - nirahara etc.? This verse
[GITA:3868] answers this question by stating that sense organs are extremely strong and
[GITA:3869] can exert control on the minds of even learned ones. It is the nature of sense
[GITA:3870] organs to cause turbulence in one’s mind. Hence, one must undertake
[GITA:3871] difficult rituals such as fasting on special days etc., in addition to spiritual
[GITA:3872] studies and try to overcome the influence of sense organs on one’s mind.
[GITA:3874] The sense organs and the mind are inert objects. A question then
[GITA:3875] arises as to how these inert objects can exert such control over each other.
[GITA:3876] One must remember that the sense organs, while inert, are activated by the
[GITA:3877] Lord resident in every soul based on the innate nature of that soul. So, it is
[GITA:3878] the responsibility of the individual soul to try and control the activities of
[GITA:3879] the sense organs.

[GITA:3884] One should control one’s sense organs from indulgence with a firm

[GITA:3888] Comments: From previous discussions, it appears that one needs to

[GITA:3892] appears to be a circular argument and hence is logically untenable

[GITA:3894] points to this verse for the answer. One must try and control one’s sense

[GITA:3896] allow the mind to move towards concentrated meditation (dhyana) which
[GITA:3897] allows one to undertake difficult sense control tasks such as strict fasting,
[GITA:3909] 74                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita

[GITA:3911] absorb divine, spiritual knowledge paving the way for moksha.
[GITA:3913] Sri Rayaru [GV] clarifies that for one to achieve divine, spiritual

[GITA:3915] sense organs, a seeker also needs to conquer emotions such as desire,
[GITA:3916] hatred etc., as described later in verse 2.64.
[GITA:3918] Dangers in Sensual Indulgence
[GITA:3920] Ü`m`Vmo {df`mZ² nw§g… g“ñVofynOm`Vo Ÿ&

[GITA:3926] One who keeps contemplating on sense pleasures develops an
[GITA:3927] attachment and obsession with them, which leads to desire in experiencing
[GITA:3928] such pleasures. This desire in turn leads to anger in the event of not being
[GITA:3929] able to satisfy these desires. Anger leads to delusion and clouds one’s mind
[GITA:3930] about right and wrong. This delusion leads one to forget injunctions against
[GITA:3931] forbidden activities. This forgetfulness in turn leads to failure in intellectual
[GITA:3932] judgement. Loss of intellect results in one’s downfall. (2.62) (2.63)
[GITA:3934] Comments: In verse 2.63, it was stated that one should focus ones
[GITA:3935] mind on the Lord while striving to achieve self-control to conquer the sense
[GITA:3936] organs. In verses 2.62, 2.63, 2.64, the Lord outlines the chain reaction that
[GITA:3937] would ensue from loss of self-control and the emotional impact of
[GITA:3938] attachment/aversion or likes/dislikes (raga/dvesha) leading to ones
[GITA:3939] downfall (and eventual fall into hell). Understanding of this chain reaction
[GITA:3940] will help one to develop equanimity in likes and dislikes.
[GITA:3942] The chain reaction is as follows: contemplation on sense pleasures ->
[GITA:3943] obsession -> desire -> anger -> delusion -> forgetfulness -> loss of
[GITA:3955] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      75
[GITA:3957] intellect -> destruction. Forgetfulness could be of two types. One would be
[GITA:3958] forgetting knowledge about avoiding activities prohibited in the scriptures
[GITA:3959] and the other would be to forget societal norms such as not usurping
[GITA:3960] properties owned by others. As indicated in 2.56, one who has realized the
[GITA:3961] Lord will have conquered these emotions, but a seeker on the spiritual path
[GITA:3962] will have to strive to control these emotions, or else he/she will experience
[GITA:3963] the state indicated in the chain reaction. The primary cause of the chain
[GITA:3964] reaction is the inability to manage raga, and dvesha. This aspect is further
[GITA:3965] explained in the next verse.

[GITA:4001] 76                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:4002] manner. It is also clarified that one who has achieved control over sense

[GITA:4005] difficult tasks such as fasting to achieve self-control. Here it is clarified that
[GITA:4006] one does not need to completely avoid consuming foods as one has to
[GITA:4007] ensure physical wellbeing. It is possible to indulge in activities such as
[GITA:4008] consuming minimum amount of required food while still exerting control
[GITA:4009] over the sense organs.
[GITA:4011] In summary, the sequence of events that would unfold from

[GITA:4013] mental peace -> concentrated meditation -> divine knowledge ->
[GITA:4014] elimination of sadness (due to evisceration of sins) -> liberation.

[GITA:4019] One who does not have control over the mind cannot absorb spiritual

[GITA:4053] The mind which follows sense organs that go after sense pleasures
[GITA:4054] will be swayed just like a ship gets swayed in an ocean by strong winds.
[GITA:4055] This leads to loss of intellectual judgement and also knowledge derived
[GITA:4056] through studies. (2.67)
[GITA:4058] Comments: This verse makes it very clear that even one who has
[GITA:4059] learnt a lot through study of scriptures and contemplation of scriptural
[GITA:4060] concepts will not be able to benefit from such knowledge if one is unable to
[GITA:4061] control the mind and the sense organs. Mere acquisition of scriptural
[GITA:4062] knowledge without exercising control over the senses and the mind
[GITA:4063] amounts to just book knowledge.The mind is easily swayed. If sense organs
[GITA:4064] pursue sense pleasures, the mind will follow them and will sway just like a
[GITA:4065] boat in an ocean and loses direction when faced with strong winds.
[GITA:4067] The example of a ship getting swayed by strong winds brings to
[GITA:4068] memory an episode in the life of Sri Madhwacharya. Acharya was once
[GITA:4069] meditating on the seashore near Udupi when he saw a ship caught in a
[GITA:4070] violent storm. The people on the ship were crying for help. Acharya waved
[GITA:4071] his holy fabric (kavi shati) towards the ship, at which the ship immediately
[GITA:4072] stabilized on the waters and came safely ashore. The travelers on the ship
[GITA:4073] who were  rescued by Acharya were very grateful and offered him precious
[GITA:4074] gems on board the ship, but Acharya was content with just a lump of
[GITA:4075] sandstone (gopi chandana) that was used to tie the ship’s mast. Inside the
[GITA:4076] sandstone was a beautiful idol of Sri Krishna which was worshipped by
[GITA:4077] Goddess Rukmini and Lord Brahma. Sri Madhwacharya carried that idol
[GITA:4078] and installed it in Udupi where it can be seen even today! We can see the
[GITA:4079] relevance of using the example of a ship swaying in the ocean in this verse
[GITA:4080] considering this episode. Our body is like a ship that we are using to cross
[GITA:4081] the ocean of samsara. Inside our body, Lord Krishna resides in our hearts
[GITA:4082] just like the idol of Sri Krishna was inside the sandstone. Just as the
[GITA:4094] 78                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:4095] travelers on the ship did not know the value of the sandstone piece which
[GITA:4096] had the idol of Sri Krishna in it, we too do not appreciate the presence of
[GITA:4097] the Lord in our hearts. Just as the travelers on the ship faced violent
[GITA:4098] turbulence due to strong winds, we also feel great perturbance in our minds
[GITA:4099] due to strong swaying of our sense organs. The travelers saw Sri
[GITA:4100] Madhwacharya and cried for help. Acharya rescued them immediately.
[GITA:4101] Similarly, if we turn to Sri Madhwacharya (an incarnation of Sri Vayudeva)
[GITA:4102] asking for help in traversing this ocean of samsara, he will rescue us and
[GITA:4103] land us safely in moksha.

[GITA:4138] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      79
[GITA:4140] Comments: In this verse the Lord is comparing the i nterests and
[GITA:4141] knowledge of a normal worldly person and a realized person. Most people

[GITA:4143] interest in learning about the attributes of the Lord, whereas a realized soul

[GITA:4146] sense pleasure, a realized person stays in the dark (has no interest in such
[GITA:4147] matters).
[GITA:4149] A realized soul is completely immersed in the Lord and has no
[GITA:4150] interest at all in worldly matters. A question then arises about deities such
[GITA:4151] as Indra, Surya, Agni etc ., who are realized souls but have an active role in
[GITA:4152] worldly matters as they activate the sense organs of living beings. If, as
[GITA:4153] realized souls, they avoid taking interest in worldly matters, how can the
[GITA:4154] world function? Sri Rayaru [GV] answers this question by stating that the
[GITA:4155] nature of a realized soul referred to in this verse does not apply to deities. It
[GITA:4156] applies to souls who have achi eved self -realization but are not part of the
[GITA:4157] group of deities who have specific roles.

[GITA:4216] Summary of Chapter 2
[GITA:4218] With the context for the teachings in the Gita established in Chapter
[GITA:4219] 1, the actual sermon of Lord Krishna to Arjuna (and through Arjuna to the
[GITA:4231] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      81
[GITA:4233] rest of humanity) begins in Chapter 2. Seeing Arjuna in  a pitiable condition
[GITA:4234] not wanting to wage the war, Krishna asks Arjuna why he wants to avoid
[GITA:4235] performing his prescribed duties and thereby risk losing respect in society.
[GITA:4236] Such an abdication of responsibility is not worthy of a great prince like
[GITA:4237] Arjuna who had a stellar reputation for fighting for justice all his life
[GITA:4238] (2.2-2.3). Arjuna, who so far wanted to avoid war out of compassion and
[GITA:4239] attachment to his kith and kin, now reasons that Bheeshma, Drona and
[GITA:4240] others are not mere family members and teachers  whom he holds in very
[GITA:4241] high esteem . T hey are also worthy of worship . However, Krishna’s
[GITA:4242] questioning opens some doubts in his mind, and he informs Krishna that his
[GITA:4243] mind is conflicted, and he is unsure about the path forward. He surrenders
[GITA:4244] to Krishna, requests to be considered as a student and  given guidance
[GITA:4245] (2.4-2.8). Given that Arjuna’s doubts are deep rooted, Lord Krishna
[GITA:4246] proceeds to deliver a very detailed sermon to him covering all aspects of
[GITA:4247] life such as the relationship between the Lord and individual souls,
[GITA:4248] responsibilities of everyone in society, concept of devotion to the Lord,
[GITA:4249] transient nature o f life, cycle of births and deaths and many more topics
[GITA:4250] which prove to be a summary of critical teachings from all scriptures such
[GITA:4251] as the Vedas and great epics such as the Ramayana, the Mahabharata etc
[GITA:4252] (2.11-2.71).
[GITA:4253] At this stage, one can expect several qu estions as to the context and
[GITA:4254] content of the Gita. Firstly, why would Krishna get into great details about
[GITA:4255] life, the universe, the relationship between the Lord and individual souls
[GITA:4256] and such spiritual issues when all that was needed was some timely,
[GITA:4257] practical advice to Arjuna to get on with fighting the war. The reason
[GITA:4258] Krishna had to get into such great details is that Arjuna had developed deep
[GITA:4259] rooted doubts about his duties and responsibilities , and he had to be
[GITA:4260] convinced about the need to perform his duti es without getting excessively
[GITA:4261] attached to his near and dear ones. Secondly, one would wonder if the
[GITA:4262] battlefield was the right venue for such heavy philosophical discourse
[GITA:4263] which should normally occur in a serene, quiet environment. Again, it is
[GITA:4264] normal for many to seek guidance when they come to a crossroad and are
[GITA:4265] about to implement actions with grave repercussions. These are the very
[GITA:4266] times when one needs proper spiritual guidance. Some would question as to
[GITA:4278] 82                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:4279] how such a lengthy sermon can be delivered when mi llions of soldiers are
[GITA:4280] about to  start a war. Krishna’s conversation with Arjuna ru ns quickly as
[GITA:4281] Arjuna is an evolved soul and absorbs the concepts very quickly. Finally,
[GITA:4282] some wonder how Arjuna who is known as an incarnation of deity Indra
[GITA:4283] could be ignorant  and develop such fundamental doubts about his duties
[GITA:4284] and responsibilities. At the end of Krishna’s teachings, Arjuna responds
[GITA:4285] saying that by Krishna’s grace, his doubts have been cleared, his memory is
[GITA:4286] back, and he is clear about his duties and responsibi lities (18.73). The fact
[GITA:4287] that his memory was back, implies that Arjuna had proper knowledge about
[GITA:4288] his duties earlier but for some reason his mind was covered with delusion.
[GITA:4289] It was the Lord’s Divine Will that Arjuna would undergo temporary loss of
[GITA:4290] memory to set the stage for his doubts and questions , which then gave Him
[GITA:4291] an opportunity to use Arjuna as an instrument to teach the Gita to all of the
[GITA:4292] mankind. Lord Krishna then advances many powerful reasons for Arjuna to
[GITA:4293] stop worrying about the h arm the war could cause  to his loved ones.
[GITA:4294] Firstly, his elders and teachers such as Bheeshma and Drona were  not
[GITA:4295] worthy of grieving for as they had supported Duryodhana, the evil king ,
[GITA:4296] whose army had to be  destroyed to establish order and righteousness.
[GITA:4297] Despite their good  nature, these elders were blind to Duryodhana’s evil
[GITA:4298] intentions and hence were not deserving of sympathy (2.11). Secondly, if
[GITA:4299] Arjuna was  worried that these elders would be  permanently destroyed,
[GITA:4300] Krishna reminds him that the body and the soul are separate , and that their
[GITA:4301] souls would live on. Further, based on the good deeds they had performed,
[GITA:4302] they would achieve  heaven. So, it was unnecessary  to grieve over them
[GITA:4303] (2.12). Thirdly, just as a body undergoes various stages in life such as
[GITA:4304] childhood, youth, old a ge etc, death is also a natural stage for everybody.
[GITA:4305] As such, these elders would die one day or the other , and no amount of
[GITA:4306] grieving could prevent  that (2.13). Fourthly, just as one does not grieve
[GITA:4307] about throwing out old, worn-out clothes as they are replaced by new, good
[GITA:4308] clothes, one should not grieve over a worn-out body that will eventually be
[GITA:4309] replaced by a new one (2.22). Basically, Krishna teaches Arjuna  that he
[GITA:4310] must perform his rightful duties and any excuses coming in the way are
[GITA:4311] untenable.
[GITA:4324] Chapter 2                                                                                                                                      83
[GITA:4326] Verses 2.20 to 2.24  give us a description of the nature of individual
[GITA:4327] souls which are indestructible, and have no beginning or end etc. As
[GITA:4328] opposed to individual souls, the nature of the Supreme Soul (Lord
[GITA:4329] Almighty) is briefly described in verses 2.17 , 2.25 and 2.29. The Lord who
[GITA:4330] pervades everywhere, is eternal, and does not experience destruction of the
[GITA:4331] body (as His body is transcendental), and is full of auspicious attributes and
[GITA:4332] is devoid of any blemishes. He is superior to individual souls and hence is
[GITA:4333] worthy of  worship. One should perform one s prescribed duties as an
[GITA:4334] offering to the Lord without expectations. This paves the way for one’s
[GITA:4335] liberation. Coming to the practical aspects of Arjuna’s decision to
[GITA:4336] relinquish arms, the Lord e mphasizes the need for Arjuna t o perform his
[GITA:4337] prescribed duties, as for a kshatriya, there is no loftier duty than waging a
[GITA:4338] just war. Arjuna has been handed a great opportunity to perform his duty
[GITA:4339] and he should not waste this chance. If he were to withdraw from war,
[GITA:4340] purely out of compass ion to near and dear ones, nothing would prevent his
[GITA:4341] enemies from concluding that Arjuna was afraid to fight, and they could
[GITA:4342] question his valor. Finally, Krishna tells Arjuna that he has nothing to lose
[GITA:4343] by waging the war. If he wins, he gets to rule the ki ngdom and eventually
[GITA:4344] goes to heaven hereafter for diligently performing his duty. If he loses and
[GITA:4345] dies, he will attain heavens for his conviction and efforts (2.31 -2.37). From
[GITA:4346] verses 2.12 to 2.38, Krishna imparts Arjuna knowledge (sankhya) about the
[GITA:4347] Lord and individual souls. From verse 2.39  onwards, He teaches Arjuna the
[GITA:4348] methods and procedure (yoga) for acquiring such knowledge after which
[GITA:4349] Arjuna would be able to perform his prescribed duties with conviction,
[GITA:4350] realize the Lord, get over worldly bondage and achieve the state of eternal
[GITA:4351] bliss ( moksha). In verses 2.42 -2.45, the Lord teaches Arjuna the real
[GITA:4352] purport of the Vedas - that one should focus on the deeper meanings and
[GITA:4353] not get carried away by peripheral meanings. The real purport of the Vedas
[GITA:4354] is divine, spiritual knowledge of Lord Almighty. In verses 2.45 -2.51, the
[GITA:4355] Lord discusses the concept of nishkama karma , that is performing
[GITA:4356] prescribed duties without expectations. Specifically, in verse 2.50 , the Lord
[GITA:4357] categorically states that the best path for one to achieve divine, spiritual
[GITA:4358] knowledge is for one to focus on performing one’s assigned duties as an
[GITA:4359] offering to the Lord without expectations on the outcome ( nishkama
[GITA:4371] 84                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:4372] karma). Such a realized soul  would be rid of the consequences of good and
[GITA:4373] bad deeds and would be eligible for liberation. Among all activities, those
[GITA:4374] that lead to attainment of divine knowledge is supreme. In verses 2.52 and
[GITA:4375] 2.53, it is stated that in order to absorb proper teachings, one needs to
[GITA:4376] cleanse one’s mind of conflicting, ignorant, and inconsistent viewpoints not
[GITA:4377] based on scriptural truths. In verse 2.54, Arjuna asks Krishna about the
[GITA:4378] characteristics of a person with such a tranquil mind. In the 4 verses,
[GITA:4379] starting from verse 2.55 to 2.58 , the Lord describes the characteristics of a
[GITA:4380] person with mental tranquility. In the 9 verses from 2.59 to 2.67 , questions
[GITA:4381] about the nature of such a person are answered. The Lord concludes the
[GITA:4382] sermon in Chapter 2 by stating in 2.72  that such a person will not
[GITA:4383] experience worldly miseries and in due course will reach His abode.

[GITA:4402] Chapter 3 – The Path of Action
[GITA:4404] Chapter Introduction:  This Chapter of 43 verses is termed Karma
[GITA:4405] Yoga (The Path of Action). In this chapter , t he Lord answers Arju na’s
[GITA:4406] questions regarding the paths of duty ( karma) and knowledge ( jnana).
[GITA:4407] Arjuna wonders if there was a way, he could focus on acquiring knowledge
[GITA:4408] (jnana) and avoid participating in the  war. The Lord answers all Arjuna’s
[GITA:4409] doubts logically to convince him that everyone has an obligation to perform
[GITA:4410] his duties to society , and as a kshatriya prince it was Arjuna’s
[GITA:4411] responsibility to fight the just war to protect his citizens. To perform one’s
[GITA:4412] duty, one also needs to be equipped with knowledge and in that sense, one
[GITA:4413] needs to incorporate both karma and jnana in their spiritual journey. Based
[GITA:4414] on ones innate nature, some may be prescribed a path that is dominant in
[GITA:4415] action and others may be prescribed a path dominant in knowledge. This
[GITA:4416] chapter also has an excellent di scussion on the Cyclic Order of the
[GITA:4417] Universe. In the previous chapter, in verses 2.12 to 2.30, the Lord lectured
[GITA:4418] on the nature of individual souls and the Supreme Soul (Lord Almighty). In
[GITA:4419] verse 2.39, the Lord tells Arjuna how to acquire spiritual knowledge which
[GITA:4420] would guide one to perform right actions. In the verses 2.45 to 2.51, the
[GITA:4421] Lord discusses the concept of nishkama karma  (performing prescribed
[GITA:4422] duties without expectations ) which w ould liberate one from bondage. In
[GITA:4423] this chapter, that concept is expanded in response to Arjuna’s questions that
[GITA:4424] appear in verses 3.1 and 3.2 . Thus, chapter 3 is an appropriate follow up to
[GITA:4425] chapter 2.

[GITA:4444] 86                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita

[GITA:4448] Arjuna said: O Janardana! O Keshava! If you opine that knowledge
[GITA:4449] is superior to action, then why are you pushing me to wage this dreadful
[GITA:4450] war?  (3.1)
[GITA:4452] My mind is confused with this dual talk of superiority between
[GITA:4453] knowledge and action. Please tell me with certainty the correct way which
[GITA:4454] will lead me to the right path. (3.2)
[GITA:4456] Comments: Sri Rayaru in GV makes a reference to verse 2.49 which

[GITA:4458] action. Ho wever, in other verses such as 2.37 , Krishna ex horts Arjuna to
[GITA:4459] follow the path of action by waging the just wa r as that was Arjuna’s
[GITA:4460] prescribed duty. Arjuna is now questioning as to which  is the superior path.
[GITA:4461] He wonders whether he should renounce everything, become an ascetic and
[GITA:4462] follow the path of knowledge which would lead him to liberation.
[GITA:4464] Jnana Yogis and Karma Yogis
[GITA:4466] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:4467] bmoHo$@pñ_Z² {Û{dYm {Zð>m nwam àmoº$m _`m@ZK Ÿ&
[GITA:4468] kmZ`moJoZ gm§»`mZm§ H$_©`moJoZ `mo{JZm_² Ÿ&& 3 Ÿ&&
[GITA:4470] The Lord said:  O Anagha (Arjuna, the one without sins)! As
[GITA:4471] explained before, in this world there are two paths towards liberation
[GITA:4472] depending on one ’s innate nature, talent, and situation. Kings such as
[GITA:4473] Janaka (karma yogi) achieved liberation by sincerely ruling their kingdoms
[GITA:4474] (path of action), and sages such as Sanaka ( jnana yogi) achieved liberation
[GITA:4475] by learning, teaching, and spreading spiritual knowledge to others (path of
[GITA:4476] knowledge). (3.3)
[GITA:4489] Chapter 3                                                                                                                                         87
[GITA:4491] Comments: Lord Krishna clarifies that there are two main paths to
[GITA:4492] liberation, based on one’s innate nature, ability, and eligibility. Arjuna, as a
[GITA:4493] ruler, belongs to the karma yogi  class and hence he should perform his
[GITA:4494] prescribed duty of waging th is war to protect his ci tizens. Thi s answers
[GITA:4495] Arjuna’s question in 3.1. It is further clarified in GV  that everyone must
[GITA:4496] follow both the path of knowledge and the path of action. However, in
[GITA:4497] jnana yogis , knowledge is predominant and hence they should follow the
[GITA:4498] path of knowledge a nd in the process also follow necessary activities (path
[GITA:4499] of action). Likewise, for karma yogis  such as Arjuna, the path of action
[GITA:4500] (war, in this case) is the superior path and traversing that path also requires
[GITA:4501] a certain amount of knowledge (path of knowled ge). As such, karma yoga
[GITA:4502] and jnana yoga  refer to the aspect of action or knowledge that is
[GITA:4503] predominant in a person’s nature. This also means that everyone of us
[GITA:4504] should introspect within ourselves as to the proper path for us to follow ,
[GITA:4505] depending on our inn ate nature, talent, interest, and ability. For one who
[GITA:4506] sincerely prays to the Lord, the path will become clear.
[GITA:4508] Action (Karma) is Mandatory for Everyone
[GITA:4510] Z H$_©Um_Zmaå^mÞ¡îH$å`ª nwéfmo@íZwVo Ÿ&
[GITA:4511] Z M g§Ý`gZmXod {gqÕ g_{YJÀN>{V Ÿ&& 4 Ÿ&&
[GITA:4513] One cannot escape b ondage from actions just by relinquishing
[GITA:4514] actions. Also, one cannot directly achieve liberation only by performing
[GITA:4515] duties without expectations (nishkama karma). (3.4)
[GITA:4517] Comments: Krishna instructs Arjuna not to avoid performing
[GITA:4518] prescribed duties. There are three reasons that Arjuna could have for
[GITA:4519] avoiding duties: (a) Once liberated (in moksha), there are no compulsions
[GITA:4520] on duties, so in preparation , it may be best to avoid actions (and focus on
[GITA:4521] knowledge) in this world itself; (b) focus on activities might bi nd one in
[GITA:4522] worldly life and lead to expectations;  and, (c) some scriptures say that
[GITA:4523] action comes in the way of attaining moksha, based on the phrase –
[GITA:4535] 88                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:4536] ‘karmana badhyate jantuhu’ (one gets bound by activity – in other words,
[GITA:4537] actions come in the way of liberation).
[GITA:4539] Lord Krishn a responds to the reasoning in ‘a’ by using the word
[GITA:4540] purusha in this verse which stands for one with a physical body (gross or
[GITA:4541] subtle). The physical body is designed for performing actions. Hence, the
[GITA:4542] existence of the body contradicts t he reasoning in ‘a’. The use of the word
[GITA:4543] purusha also implies that one has gone through many births. Just because,
[GITA:4544] one decides not to perform any actions in this birth, it does not mean that
[GITA:4545] they did not perform activities in prior births. So, does it mean  that one can
[GITA:4546] never achieve liberation? This a rgument makes the reasoning in ‘b’
[GITA:4547] untenable. Actions performed with expectations on outcome s do come in
[GITA:4548] the way of moksha. This does not apply to all actions, especially actions
[GITA:4549] performed without expectations.  Hence, reasoning in ‘c’ is also invalid.
[GITA:4550] Even nishkama karma does not, by itself directly lead to moksha. This type
[GITA:4551] of action leads to purity in mind which allows one to absorb spiritual
[GITA:4552] studies, eventually paving the way for liberation.
[GITA:4554] So, the path to liberation is to avoid activities with expectations and
[GITA:4555] perform prescribed activities -> mental peace -> detachment from worldly
[GITA:4556] objects -> concentrated listening, reflection, meditation on  the Lord
[GITA:4557] Almighty -> divine knowledge -> liberation. The process i nvolved in these
[GITA:4558] steps are clarified in the following verses.

[GITA:4767] Comments: These 2 verses describe the Cyclic Order of the

[GITA:4771] imbalances. Living beings come into physical existence through the food
[GITA:4772] chain, which is represented by rice. Rain (governed by the deity Parjanya –
[GITA:4773] Sun) causes rice to grow.  P arjanya, when pleased by the yagna performed
[GITA:4774] by the citizenry causes rain. Human beings invoke  the Lord Almighty
[GITA:4775] through Vedic hymns (as the Lord is known through the Vedas) and the
[GITA:4776] Lord powers humans to perform their prescribed duties ( karma) and
[GITA:4777] propitiate the deities through yagna. This cycle is represented as follows:
[GITA:4778] Rice -> Humans -> Vedic Prayers - > Lord’s Grace -> Prescribed duties ->
[GITA:4779] Ritual sacrifices -> Offering to Deities (Parjanya) -> Rain -> Rice.
[GITA:4781] Yagna, the concept of offering to deities thr ough ritual sacrifices is
[GITA:4782] an especially important aspect of Hindu philosophy and its meaning is
[GITA:4783] described in later verses.
[GITA:4785] Ed§ àd{V©V§ MH«§$ ZmZwdV©`Vrh `… Ÿ&
[GITA:4786] AKm`w[apÝÐ`mam_mo _moK§ nmW© g Ord{V Ÿ&& 16 &&
[GITA:4788] One who does not respect and follow this cycle of life is leading a
[GITA:4789] wasteful life. Such people are interested only in pursuing sense pleasures,
[GITA:4790] and they lead a sinful life. (3.16)
[GITA:4792] Comments: The Lord teaches that everyone must play his role  in the
[GITA:4793] circle of life to ensure proper functioning of the cycl ic order of the
[GITA:4794] universe. This order is an intera ction amongst its constituent parts  namely,
[GITA:4795] the individual souls, the inert matter (material nature) and the Lord
[GITA:4796] Almighty. Even from practical experience , we all know that there is a
[GITA:4797] specific order in natur e that one must follow. We witness every day  the
[GITA:4798] perils of deviating from this order in terms of global warming, excessive
[GITA:4799] rains, floods, earthquakes, pandemics etc. The Gita teaches that everyone
[GITA:4800] must understand their role in the univer se and not waste th eir lifetime  by
[GITA:4812] 94                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:4813] senselessly pursuing sense pleasures constantly. Some can point out to the
[GITA:4814] instances where even after performing the stipulated yagna, one does not
[GITA:4815] see the effects such as rains, sumptuo us harvest etc., and question  the
[GITA:4816] validity of these cl aims. One must note that mechanically performing these
[GITA:4817] rituals will not yield results and they must be accompanied with sincerity in
[GITA:4818] purpose and most importantly, as an offering to the Supreme Lord.
[GITA:4820] At this stage, one may ask a question as to the applicab ility of these
[GITA:4821] rituals to the population other than married householders, such as students
[GITA:4822] (brahmachari), those who have retired from active life ( vanprasthi) and
[GITA:4823] ascetics ( sanyasis). After all, not everyone w ould have access to all
[GITA:4824] material utilities that would be required to perform these rituals. Sri Rayaru
[GITA:4825] [GV] clarifies that yagna has different meanings based on one s stage in
[GITA:4826] life. For example, for brahmcharis, serving their teachers ( guru) is the
[GITA:4827] stipulated yagna. For ascetics who have renounced all m aterial utilities,
[GITA:4828] yagna refers to mental ( manasika) and vocal (vachaka) sacrifices.
[GITA:4829] Studying, teaching, and lecturing about the scriptures is the stipulated
[GITA:4830] yagna for ascetics. For vanaprasthis, performing activities without hurting
[GITA:4831] any living organism co nstitutes yagna. In other words, yagna is mandatory
[GITA:4832] for everyone, but the sti pulated activity depends on one ’s stage in life. Sri
[GITA:4833] Vidyasagara Madhava Teertha indicated the example of s ome saints who,
[GITA:4834] in addition to jnana yagna (sacrifice through knowledge) , dhyana yagna
[GITA:4835] (sacrifice through meditation), etc.,  practice the yagna of writing poetry on
[GITA:4836] the greatness of the Lord Almighty. For them, poetry (kavana) and singing
[GITA:4837] in praise of the Lord is savana (yagna).

[GITA:5007] agent that causes changes in other objects but itself does not undergo
[GITA:5008] changes. If the Lord stops performing ac tivities, there is a danger that
[GITA:5009] everyone in society, devoid of examples , may also stop performing their
[GITA:5010] prescribed activities, interrupting the cycle of the universe, resulting in

[GITA:5061] Ignorant ones, unaware that the Lord Almighty activates everyone’s

[GITA:5065] Comments: This verse provides further  explanations on verses 3.25
[GITA:5066] and 3.26. Sri Rayaru in GV  provides an excellent explanation on the inner
[GITA:5067] meanings of the terms prakriti and guna appearing in this verse which carry
[GITA:5068] 3 sets of meanings. Firstly, prakriti and guna refer to the Lord Almighty
[GITA:5069] and His 3 attributes, namely, will, knowledge, and attempt. Secondly, the
[GITA:5070] terms prakriti and guna refer to the three types of individual souls
[GITA:5071] (superior, ordinary, and inferior) and their 3 attributes of knowledge,
[GITA:5072] namely, correct knowledge, mixed knowledge, and false knowledge.
[GITA:5073] Thirdly, the terms prakriti and guna, refer to inert nature and its 3
[GITA:5074] attributes, namely sat (piety), rajas (passion) and tamas (ignorance). With
[GITA:5075] these interpretations, this verse can be expanded to mean as follows -Lord
[GITA:5076] Almighty is ind ependent and is the instrumental cause for activities
[GITA:5077] performed by everyone based on their innate attributes using  inert nature as
[GITA:5089] 100                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:5090] the material cause and their sense organs as the instrument s. The attributes
[GITA:5091] of inert nature impact the actions performed by the sense organs. Ignorant
[GITA:5092] ones think that they are performing the actions on their own using their
[GITA:5093] sense organs of action.

[GITA:5098] O Arjuna, The one with strong arms! Learned one s, aware of the
[GITA:5099] distinction in the attributes and activities between the Lord and ordinary
[GITA:5100] souls, know that their sense organs perform their activities as willed by the
[GITA:5101] Lord. Such people will not get entangled in worldly life. (3.28)
[GITA:5103] Comments: The previous verse stated that ignorant ones believe that
[GITA:5104] they act independently, and this verse describes the views of learned ones.
[GITA:5105] The learned ones are aware that the Lord Almighty is independent and
[GITA:5106] causes activity in individual souls based on their innate nature . They have a
[GITA:5107] good understanding of the divisions among attributes ( guna) and action
[GITA:5108] (karma). Attributes here have different meanings depending on the entity.
[GITA:5109] The attributes of the Lord are will, knowledge, and attempt. For the
[GITA:5110] individual souls they are th e innate nature of being superior, ordinary, and
[GITA:5111] inferior. The attributes of inert nature are sat(piety), rajas(passion), and
[GITA:5112] tamas(ignorance). Likewise, the actions of the 3 entities are also dif ferent.
[GITA:5113] The Lord is independent. Individual souls which are dependent on the Lord
[GITA:5114] act according to their innate nature, and inert nature which is also
[GITA:5115] dependent on the Lord undergoes transformation based on its 3 attributes of
[GITA:5116] sat, rajas and tamas. Sri Rayaru in GV  provides two equally meaningful
[GITA:5117] interpretations for the first half of the second line ( guna guneshu vartanta).
[GITA:5118] First interpretation – The Lord’s attributes (guna) initiate actions (guneshu)
[GITA:5119] in individual souls based on their innate nature. The second interpretation –
[GITA:5120] Individual soul’s sense organs (guna) act on sense objects ( guneshu) based
[GITA:5121] on the Lord’s will and the individual’s innate nature. In summary, the
[GITA:5122] learned ones understand that they are not independent and with proper
[GITA:5134] Chapter 3                                                                                                                                         101
[GITA:5136] conviction they avoid getting entangled in worldly activities as they are
[GITA:5137] focused on the Lord Almighty.

[GITA:5374] Fire, Mirror, and Fetus

[GITA:5379] Just as smoke hides fire, just as dust covers a mirror and just as a
