[GITA:5383] Comments: While the previous verse 3.37  identified desire or lust as
[GITA:5384] the root cause of evil, this verse explains the strength of this emotion
[GITA:5385] through three different examples. Sri Rayaru in GV  explains the reason for
[GITA:5386] using these three different examples. These are related respectively to the
[GITA:5387] three classes of beings, namely pious, passionate, and ignorant. Pious souls
[GITA:5388] can also get enveloped by lust just as smoke covers a fire. However, just as
[GITA:5389] one can see and feel t he fire to some extent even when covered by smoke,
[GITA:5390] pious beings can visualize the Lord even when influenced by desire . So
[GITA:5391] they have the most to gain by controlling desire. Passionate souls are
[GITA:5392] covered by desire just as dirt covers a mirror. With some effor t, one can
[GITA:5393] wipe the mirror clean and likewise passionate souls with effort can
[GITA:5394] overcome the influence of desire. Ignorant souls are under the tight grip of
[GITA:5395] desire just like a womb covers a fetus strongly. Such souls who are under
[GITA:5396] the constant influence of lust can never overcome this emotion and fail to
[GITA:5397] realize the Lord.

[GITA:5420] spiritual knowledge.

[GITA:5476] Comments: The Lord continues to provide answers to Arjuna’s
[GITA:5477] question in a logical manner . If desire has its home in one ’s sense organs
[GITA:5478] (including mind) and intellect, how does one control desire? The Lord
[GITA:5479] answers by stating that one needs to control the sense organs to be able to
[GITA:5480] control desire. Desire is a strong force that can shroud both ordinary and
[GITA:5481] special knowledge ( jnana and vijnana). Ordinary knowledge refers to
[GITA:5482] knowledge th at one acquires through study and through teachers. Special
[GITA:5483] knowledge refers to the deep knowledge that one acquires by study,
[GITA:5484] meditation, and contemplation of scriptural texts such as the Vedas,
[GITA:5485] Puranas etc.
[GITA:5487] In the current context, Arjuna’s knowledge is shrouded by his mental
[GITA:5488] weakness due to the fear of losing his near and dear ones in the war. The
[GITA:5500] Chapter 3                                                                                                                                         109
[GITA:5502] Lord ex horts him to conquer his mind and focus on performing his
[GITA:5503] prescribed duty.
[GITA:5505] At this stage, it is useful to understand the concept of desire.
[GITA:5506] Scriptures state tha t there are four aspects to one ’s activities – dharma
[GITA:5507] (right conduct), artha (material riches), kama (desire) and moksha
[GITA:5508] (liberation). There is a discussion in the Mahabharata regarding the
[GITA:5509] relative importance of these four aspects. Vidura states  that moksha is the
[GITA:5510] most important one as that is everyone’s goal. Bh eema states that kama is
[GITA:5511] the most important. Naturally, everyone is curious to find out more.
[GITA:5512] Bheema states that desire can be either lofty (positive) or primal (negative).
[GITA:5513] After all, one  would work towards moksha only when one has the desire
[GITA:5514] (kama) to achieve moksha. So, lofty desires are not prohibited. It is primal
[GITA:5515] desire or lust that entangles living beings.
[GITA:5517] Know Thy Lord and Overcome Desires

[GITA:5522] It is said that the sense organs are superior, and the mind is more
[GITA:5523] superior to them. Intellect is superior to the mind and the ultimate
[GITA:5524] consciousness (the Supreme Lord) is even more superior to the intellect.
[GITA:5525] (3.42)
[GITA:5527] Comments: After describing the impact that desire/lust has on a
[GITA:5528] seeker’s spiritual journey and stating that desire is rooted in the sense
[GITA:5529] organs, it was concluded that one must exert control over the sense organs
[GITA:5530] in order to conquer desire. It was al so indicated that desire is an immensely
[GITA:5531] powerful emotion and even learned ones fall prey to it. A natural question
[GITA:5532] that one would have at this stage is as follows – how can one control the
[GITA:5533] sense organs (including the mind)? This verse answers by indicatin g that
[GITA:5534] the weapon to conquer desire is knowledge. As the enemy resides in an
[GITA:5535] individual’s faculties , one must understand the relative importance of
[GITA:5547] 110                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:5548] various faculties. Only then can one conquer desire. To contr ol desire, one
[GITA:5549] must control one ’s sense organs.  To control the sense organs, one must
[GITA:5550] conquer obsession with objects of sensory perception and to do this one
[GITA:5551] must control the mind. To control  the mind, one must be able to control the
[GITA:5552] intellect. But these are all inert entities. How can they help one co ntrol
[GITA:5553] desire? Sri Rayaru [GV] explains the inner meaning of this verse by
[GITA:5554] explaining that the faculties indicated here imply the respective controlling
[GITA:5555] deities who activate the faculties. The relative gradation among the
[GITA:5556] faculties and their controlling dei ties implied in this verse is as follows.
[GITA:5557] Sense organs (and their controlling deities such as Indra) are superior to
[GITA:5558] other organs in the body (and their controlling deities such as Prithvi).
[GITA:5559] Objects of sensory perception (and their controlling deities such  as Parvati)
[GITA:5560] are superior to the sense organs (and their controlling deities).  The Mind
[GITA:5561] (and its controlling deit y such as Rudra) is superior to objects of sensory
[GITA:5562] perception (and their controlling deities). The Intellect (and controlling
[GITA:5563] deity such as Saraswati) is superior to the mind (and its controlling deities).
[GITA:5564] The principle of consciousness (and its controlling deities such as Brahma)
[GITA:5565] is superior to intellect (and its controlling deities). The unmanifest principle
[GITA:5566] (the inert nature and its controllin g deity Mahalakshmi) is superior to the
[GITA:5567] principle of consciousness.  The supreme Lord Almighty is superior to the
[GITA:5568] unmanifest principle (and to all controlling deities). The Lord has indicated
[GITA:5569] many times that one must perform one ’s prescribed duties without
[GITA:5570] expectations, as an offering to Him. This verse gives everyone an assurance
[GITA:5571] that we are not alone in this universe and the various angelic forces that
[GITA:5572] control all activities in this universe,  and indeed in our bodies can help us
[GITA:5573] in conquering desire if we approach our prescribed duties with sincerity
[GITA:5574] and as an offering to the Lord.

[GITA:5600] Summary of Chapter 3
[GITA:5602] This chapter is a continuation of chapter 2, where the Lord provides
[GITA:5603] more details on the concept of duties without expectations. In the first 2
[GITA:5604] verses, Arjuna expresses confusion about the superiority between the paths
[GITA:5605] of knowledge and action. In verses 3.3 -3.9, the Lord teaches that both these
[GITA:5606] paths lead to liberation and the choice of path depends  on one ’s innate
[GITA:5607] nature, talent, and background. The Lord also c autions Arjuna against
[GITA:5608] avoiding all actions as no one can survive without performing some action.
[GITA:5609] The Lord also provides clarification on the nature of duties that are
[GITA:5610] prescribed to living bei ngs. In verses 3.10 -3.13, the Lord introduces the
[GITA:5611] concept of yagna (ritual sacrifice) and the need for one to perform them to
[GITA:5612] propitiate the deities who govern the various entities essential for the
[GITA:5613] functioning of this universe. The Lord explains the Cyclic O rder o f the
[GITA:5614] Universe in verses 3.14 -3.16 where the interrelat ionships among the
[GITA:5615] various constituents of the universe, namely – the individual souls, the
[GITA:5616] deities, inert nature, and the supreme Lord are briefly presented. For the
[GITA:5617] universe to function, everyone must play their designated role in  the circle
[GITA:5618] of life. In verses 3.17-3.21, the Lord teaches that those who have achieved
[GITA:5619] the state of ultimate consciousness  and have realized the Lord have no
[GITA:5620] obligation to perform  duties. Likewise, souls that are liberated have no
[GITA:5621] obligation to perform  any activities. However, t hey continue to perform
[GITA:5622] activities to set an example to the masses. Such souls do enjoy deeper
[GITA:5623] levels of bliss in moksha. In verses 3.22-3.24, the Lord clarifies that He has
[GITA:5624] no obligation to perform any activit y but does so out of pure compassion to
[GITA:5625] set an example to others and to e nsure order in society. Verses 3.25 -3.29
[GITA:5626] describe the manner of activities performed by the ignorant ones and the
[GITA:5627] learned ones. It also briefly describes the divisions and distinctions among
[GITA:5628] the three constituents of the universe  (the Lord Almighty, individual souls,
[GITA:5640] 112                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:5641] and inert nature) in terms of their attributes and actions. Learned ones
[GITA:5642] understand these divisions and are aware that they do not act
[GITA:5643] independently.  In verse 3.30, the Lord summarizes the previous verses and
[GITA:5644] instructs Arjuna to overcome ego  and attachment and  wage the war as an
[GITA:5645] offering to Him. In verses 3.33 to 3.35 , the Lord speaks ab out the strong
[GITA:5646] influence of one ’s innate nature on one’s activities. In verse 3.36 , Arjuna
[GITA:5647] asks Krishna why  one indulges in  sinful ac tivities even when one is not
[GITA:5648] inclined to do so. The Lord provides a detailed response to Arjuna in a
[GITA:5649] logical, sequential manner in verses 3.37 to 3.43 . To conquer des ire, one
[GITA:5650] must control one ’s sense organs, mind, and intellect. These are controlled
[GITA:5651] by an gelic forces with relative gradation  which are working under the
[GITA:5652] control of the supreme Lord. One must focus on performing one ’s
[GITA:5653] prescribed duties as an offering to the Lord and , by His grace , conquer
[GITA:5654] desire.

[GITA:5673] Chapter 4 - Wisdom in Action
[GITA:5675] Chapter Introduction: This chapter of 42 verses is known as Jnana
[GITA:5676] Yoga (The Path of Knowledge) . It is predominantly about the spiritual
[GITA:5677] knowledge that a seeker  needs to perform prescribed action ( karma).
[GITA:5678] Knowledge regarding the individual souls, various deities and the attributes
[GITA:5679] of the Lord Almighty are explained to instill devotion in a seeker. The Lord
[GITA:5680] explains that He incarnates in this world from time to time to establish
[GITA:5681] virtue and to vanquish immorality. K nowledge about the various types of
[GITA:5682] actions – right action, wrong action and inaction are also covered here.   In
[GITA:5683] the previous chapter, in verse 3.8, the Lord ta ught that one must perform
[GITA:5684] one’s prescribed duties without expectations ( nishkama karma ). In thi s
[GITA:5685] chapter, till verse 4.15, some important attributes of the Lord  Almighty are
[GITA:5686] described. Verses 4.16 to 4.23 provide a comparison of nishkama karma to
[GITA:5687] other types of activities with details of the types of nishkama karma such as
[GITA:5688] worship and sacrifice. A central feature of this chapter is the classification
[GITA:5689] and description of the different types of sacrifices  (yagna) or austerities that
[GITA:5690] yogis perform. These are described in verses 4.25 to 4.30.

[GITA:5782] Arjuna said: Krishna! You r birth is in recent times. Surya (the Sun
[GITA:5783] deity) was born a long time ago. How am I to understand that you taught
[GITA:5784] this knowledge to Surya? (4.4)
[GITA:5786] Comments: In verse 3.30 , the Lord stated that to achieve liberation
[GITA:5787] one must perform one ’s prescribed duties without expectation , as an
[GITA:5788] offering to Him. This implies that the Lord is supreme and worthy of
[GITA:5789] worship. In other verses such as 2.12 , the Lord clarified that He does not
[GITA:5790] experience births and deaths like individual souls.  Sri Rayaru  in GV
[GITA:5791] explains that Arjuna (a jnani himself who had already listened to Krishna’s
[GITA:5792] teachings in Chapter 2 and 3) was not asking about the Lord’s birt h (or
[GITA:5793] manifestations), but about the evidence to prove the difference between the

[GITA:5814] The Lord sai d: O Arjuna! Many manifestations of Mine and many
[GITA:5815] births of yours have come and gone. O! Parantapa! I know them all clearly,
[GITA:5816] but you do not. (4.5)
[GITA:5818] Comments: By stating that He always has many manifestations, the
[GITA:5819] Lord answers Arjuna’s question in 4.4  as to how He taught the knowledge
[GITA:5820] to Surya who has been in existence for a long time. The Lord manifests
[GITA:5821] (appears) at different time s which are loosely termed as  the Lord’s births.
[GITA:5822] This is quite different from individual souls such as Arjuna who experience
[GITA:5823] many births and deaths. Further, the Lord clarifies that He is aware of all
[GITA:5824] His incarnations and all births of others, but the individual souls are not
[GITA:5825] aware of their many births. Hence this verse draws out the superiority and
[GITA:5826] omniscient nature of the Lord as distinct from individual souls.
[GITA:5828] AOmo@{n gÞì``mË_m ^yVmZm_rœamo@{n gZ² Ÿ&

[GITA:5831] I am not born like everyone; My body does not perish, and I am the
[GITA:5832] controller of all beings. Through the entities of material nature creat ed by
[GITA:5833] Me, I manifest Myself in My transcendental form based on My own free
[GITA:5834] will. (4.6)
[GITA:5836] Comments: The Lord seemed to indi cate in verse 4.5  that He appears
[GITA:5837] and disappears many times. But in verse 2.17 , the Lord stated that He does
[GITA:5838] not cease to exist. How ca n thus be reconciled? The next few verses detail
[GITA:5839] the concept of manifestation as it relates to the Lord. The Lord does not
[GITA:5840] experience physical births as experienced by individual souls. The term
[GITA:5852] Chapter 4                                                                                                                                           117
[GITA:5854] birth (janma) when used in the context of Lord, relates to Hi s manifestation
[GITA:5855] which He does at His own free will using the entities of material nature that
[GITA:5856] He Himself created. This is explained in the phrase prakritim swam
[GITA:5857] adhishtaya. Sri Rayaru in GV interprets this phrase in three different ways:
[GITA:5859]  The Lord, in an incarnation such as Krishna manifests Himself
[GITA:5860] through the bodies of Vasudeva and Devaki which He Himself ha d
[GITA:5861] created.
[GITA:5862]  The Lord utilizes Goddess Durga  (governor of tamasic nature) who
[GITA:5863] is under His control , to cause  ignorant souls to consider His
[GITA:5864] manifestation as an ordinary birth.
[GITA:5865]  The Lord performs the above two actions of His own free will.
[GITA:5866] These 3 interpretations provide answers to the three questions that arise
[GITA:5867] here.
[GITA:5868] Question 1 : What does  the statement that the Lord takes birth at a
[GITA:5869] specific time and place  when His body and soul are eternal  mean? For
[GITA:5870] example, the birth of Krishna to Vasudeva and Devaki.
[GITA:5871] Answer 1 : Inert nature is under the control of the Lord Almighty. The
[GITA:5872] Lord gives physical bodies comprised of material nature to Vasudeva and
[GITA:5873] Devaki and ent ers their bodies in His transcendental form and manifests
[GITA:5874] Himself.
[GITA:5875] Question 2: What makes some think of the Lord as having a birth like
[GITA:5876] everyone else?
[GITA:5877] Answer 2: The Lord causes ignorance in some through Goddess Durga
[GITA:5878] who acts under His control.
[GITA:5879] Question 3 : What benefit does the Lord get by manifesting Himself
[GITA:5880] through Vasudeva and Devaki (and indeed other manifestations)?
[GITA:5881] Answer 3 : The Lord’s actions are due to His free will which is His
[GITA:5882] innate nature and not for any benefit.

[GITA:5911] the Lord incarnates purely out of His free will and out of pure compassion

[GITA:5913] specific time or place, generally He incarnates from time to time, to protect

[GITA:5992] Rewards are Based on Devoted Efforts
[GITA:5994] `o `Wm _m§ ànÚÝVo Vm§ñVW¡d ^Omå`h_² Ÿ&
[GITA:5995] __ dË_m©ZwdV©ÝVo _Zwî`m… nmW© gd©e… Ÿ&& 11 &&
[GITA:5997] O Partha! Whoever worships Me with devotion, in whatever way, I
[GITA:5998] reward them accordingly. Everyone follows the example that I set. (4.11)
[GITA:6000] Comments: In the previous verses it was stated that one who
[GITA:6001] worships the Lord will achieve liberation. Will all who worship the Lord
[GITA:6002] achieve liberation equally? If yes, how can one account for the difference
[GITA:6003] in efforts and approach? If no, isn’t there partialit y in result? This verse
[GITA:6004] answers these questions stating that among those who worship the Lord,
[GITA:6005] there are broadly two categories. The first one includes  learned ones who
[GITA:6006] perform activities without expectations and  surrender completely to the
[GITA:6007] Lord. These see kers are destined for liberation. The second category
[GITA:6008] includes those who, while aware of the supremacy of  the Lord, perform
[GITA:6009] rituals worshipping other deities such as Brahma, Rudra, Indra etc., seeking
[GITA:6010] temporary fruits such as progeny, wealth etc.  Even though this category of
[GITA:6011] people performs rituals to propitiate other deities, the fact that the Lord  is
[GITA:6012] the ultimate destination for their efforts results in them receiving temporary
[GITA:6013] rewards.
[GITA:6015] In the second half of this verse, the Lord clarifies that even offer ings
[GITA:6016] made by the second category of people will eventually reach  Him, but they
[GITA:6017] will not be aware of this fact. The learned ones who act without any
[GITA:6018] expectation are fully aware of this. Thus, the Lord rewards seekers based
[GITA:6019] on their effort, conviction, and a ttitude, purely based on merit. So, there is
[GITA:6020] no question of partiality.

[GITA:6042] Comments: This verse provides the reasoning behind the

[GITA:6049] Categories of Beings
[GITA:6051] MmVwd©Ê`ª _`m g¥ï>§ JwUH$_©{d^mJe… Ÿ&
[GITA:6052] Vñ` H$Vm©a_{n _m§ {dÕçH$Vm©a_ì``_² Ÿ&& 13 &&
[GITA:6054] I created the four categories (varnas) of beings based on their nature
[GITA:6055] and activities. Though I created them, I do not have a creator. I also do not
[GITA:6056] have any obligation to act, and I am eternal. (4.13)
[GITA:6058] Comments: It was stated previously that it is essential for one to
[GITA:6059] surrender to  the Lord to achieve divine, spiritual knowledge and attain
[GITA:6060] liberation. This verse explains the reason why one should surrender to
[GITA:6061] Lord. The Lord is like a  father, and children are expected to worship their
[GITA:6062] father. The Lord, who gave physical bodies to individual entities, provides
[GITA:6063] details of the categories of people He creates.
[GITA:6065] This is probably the most controversial and least understood verse in
[GITA:6066] the Gita as many people associate this verse with the caste system in
[GITA:6067] society. The four categories here are based on the proportion of the three
[GITA:6068] innate attributes ( sattv, rajas and tamas) of beings. How can there be four
[GITA:6080] 122                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:6081] categories if there are three innate attribu tes? The four categories are based
[GITA:6082] on the varying proportions of these  three innate attributes. Sri
[GITA:6083] Madhwacharya provides detailed explanations of the categories ( varnas)
[GITA:6084] and attributes ( gunas) in GB and GTN .  Individual souls are basically of
[GITA:6085] three types – angels (deities), humans, and demons. Angels have the quality
[GITA:6086] of pure sattv and are destined for liberation. Demons have pure tamas and
[GITA:6087] are destined for hell. Humans have rajas mixed with varying proportions of
[GITA:6088] sattv, rajas and tamas resulting in satvika rajasas, rajasa rajasas  and
[GITA:6089] rajasa tamasas . Those with a satvik rajasa  quality are destined for
[GITA:6090] liberation and among them are the se four categories . As explained by Sri
[GITA:6091] Jaya Teertha [ND]  – these categories are characterized by the following -
[GITA:6092] (i) sattv is much greater than rajas  (sattv >> rajas), (ii) sattv is somewhat
[GITA:6093] greater than rajas (sattv > rajas), (iii) sattv and rajas are in equal
[GITA:6094] proportion but greater than tamas (rajas = sattv > tamas) and, (iv) sattv is
[GITA:6095] greater than tamas which is greater than rajas (sattv > tamas > rajas) . As
[GITA:6096] stated by Sri Madhwacharya in GB , the qualities of sattv, rajas and tamas
[GITA:6097] are based on  the level of one ’s devotion to Lord Almighty Vishnu. One
[GITA:6098] cannot conclude one ’s innate nature just by one’s family of  birth. The
[GITA:6099] categorization of beings based on one ’s profession or vocation  (karma) is
[GITA:6100] covered in detail in Chapter 18.
[GITA:6102] The four categories of people indicated here are generally known as
[GITA:6103] brahmanas, kshatriyas, vaishyas, and shudras, which also nominally
[GITA:6104] indicates the profess ion that they undertake, namely, scholastic pursuits,
[GITA:6105] administration, commerce, and service industry. All of them are eligible for
[GITA:6106] liberation. Sri Jaya Teertha in his ND  clarifies this concept by stating that
[GITA:6107] Lord Vishnu’s devotees (vaishnavas) are conside red pious because of their
[GITA:6108] higher levels of sattvic attributes, and not due to their brahminical
[GITA:6109] profession. Sri Madhwacharya in GTN  clarifies that the categorization
[GITA:6110] based on one ’s innate nature ( swabhava) manifests in one ’s natural
[GITA:6111] aptitudes such as  steadfast devotion to the Lord,  self-control, valor,
[GITA:6112] bravery, farming, commerce, service mindedness  etc. This categorization
[GITA:6113] should not be equated to the societal classification based on one’s family of
[GITA:6114] birth (oupadika).
[GITA:6126] Chapter 4                                                                                                                                           123
[GITA:6128] While the deities have predominant sattv qualities, Sri Rayaru in his
[GITA:6129] Prameya Sangraha  [PS] provides more details on the categorization of
[GITA:6130] deities. During the process of subtle creation, all individual souls obtain a
[GITA:6131] subtle body called Aniruddha deha. During this time, the various deities get
[GITA:6132] categorized - the four faced deity Brahma as brahmin, deities Vayudeva,
[GITA:6133] Sesha, Garuda, rudra etc., as kshatriyas, many Suryas, some children of
[GITA:6134] Aditi, many Maruts, Vasus etc., as vyshyas, and Ashwini twins, Prithvi,
[GITA:6135] Kala, Mrutyu etc., as shudras. This clear ly proves that there is nothing
[GITA:6136] intrinsically superior or inferior about the categories. They are simply
[GITA:6137] different from each other.
[GITA:6139] In the second half of this verse, the Lord clarifies that while He is the
[GITA:6140] creator of these categories, He i s not created by  anyone. He also has no
[GITA:6141] obligation to act.
[GITA:6143] Notes: Material nature comprises of three qualities, and these are
[GITA:6144] present in all living beings in varying degrees. The three qualities are sattv,
[GITA:6145] rajas and tamas. Sattv is generally translated as pure, virtuous,  pious etc.,
[GITA:6146] rajas as passion and tamas as ignorance.  Those identified with the quality
[GITA:6147] of sattv are generally known to have purity in thought, words, and actions .
[GITA:6148] Sri Madhwacharya identifies an additional attribute as part of sattv. This
[GITA:6149] attribute is devotion to the Lord as stated by Sri Madhwacharya i n his GTN
[GITA:6150] based on Naradeeya Purana . Hence the translation of sattv as pious is
[GITA:6151] more appropriate as piety also implies devotion.  The quality of rajas leads
[GITA:6152] one to be passionate about material possessions and  sense pleasures. For
[GITA:6153] brevity, from now on rajas will be translated as passion. The quality of
[GITA:6154] tamas results in ignorance and delusion and is characterized by excessive
[GITA:6155] lethargy, sleepiness, and indulgence in sense pleasures. Again, for brevity
[GITA:6156] tamas will be translated as ignorance.

[GITA:6173] 124                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:6174] Actions do not bind Me. I have no interest in any fruits from My
[GITA:6175] actions. One who truly knows Me thus wil l not get entangled by actions.
[GITA:6176] (4.14)
[GITA:6178] Comments: In the previous verse the Lord stated that He has no
[GITA:6179] obligation to perform any activities. In the next few verses, He provides the
[GITA:6180] nature of His activities and contrasts  them with those of individual souls.
[GITA:6181] Actions do not bind the Lord. The Lord has no interest in any outcome of
[GITA:6182] His actions and acts on His own free will. The reason for individual souls
[GITA:6183] getting entangled in actions is their expectations. The one who understands
[GITA:6184] the nature of the Lord’s actions will not be bound by actions. Sri Rayaru in
[GITA:6185] GV provides a convincing explanation for the inherent difference between
[GITA:6186] the Supreme Soul and the individual soul based on the choice of words in
[GITA:6187] this verse. The Lord says ‘ yo maam iti abhijanati ’, meaning the ones who
[GITA:6188] know Me (maam, meaning Krishna) thus will not get entangled by actions .
[GITA:6189] Here, the Lord’s attributes are the subject matter which must be properly
[GITA:6190] understood by others (yo = individual souls) to get released from bondage.

[GITA:6199] Comments: Why do learned ones who are aware of the Lord’s

[GITA:6202] that emperors such as Janaka  achieved liber ation by performing their

[GITA:6226] What is right action? What is inaction? Even learned ones get
[GITA:6227] confused by these questions. I will explain this matter to you by knowing
[GITA:6228] which, you will be rid of bondage. (4.16)
[GITA:6230] Comments: The previous verse taught that a seeker should perform
[GITA:6231] prescribed duties. This verse provides details on the types of actions – right
[GITA:6232] actions and inaction. Sri Rayaru in GV  provides an interesting explanation
[GITA:6233] for the use of the Sanskr it word ‘tat’ in this verse. tat is an interesting word
[GITA:6234] in Sanskrit and its meaning depends on the context. At least 3 meanings of
[GITA:6235] tat are – therefore, that, and from. The interpretations are –
[GITA:6237]  Even learned ones get confused about the concept of karma.
[GITA:6238] Therefore, you must understand it properly
[GITA:6239]  In the previous verse 4.15 , it was indicated that one must perform
[GITA:6240] prescribed duties (karma). It is that karma which is discussed in this
[GITA:6241] verse
[GITA:6242]  One will be rid of bondage by acquiring this knowledge
[GITA:6244] H$_©Umo ø{n ~moÕì`§ ~moÕì`§ M {dH$_©U… Ÿ&
[GITA:6245] AH$_©Uü ~moÕì`§ JhZm H$_©Umo J{V… Ÿ&& 17 &&
[GITA:6247] One should learn what constitutes right action, prohibited action  and
[GITA:6248] inaction, and learn about the distinction between them. All these actions are
[GITA:6249] under My control. The subject of act ion (karma) is extremely complex by
[GITA:6250] nature. (4.17)
[GITA:6252] Comments: In the previous verse, the words karma (action) and
[GITA:6253] akarma (inaction) were used where akarma was also interpreted to include
[GITA:6254] vikarma (prohibited action). In this verse, all three types of action s are
[GITA:6266] 126                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:6267] explicitly stated. S ri Rayaru in GV  stresses that one must strive hard to
[GITA:6268] understand the nature of action, especially since it is an extremely complex
[GITA:6269] topic.
[GITA:6271] Sri Rayaru also provides an interesting, second interpretation of this
[GITA:6272] verse following Sri Madhwacharya’s GTN . The words karmanaha,
[GITA:6273] vikarmanaha, and akarmanaha can be derived as – karma + naha,
[GITA:6274] vikarma + naha, and akarma + naha. The word naha means ‘from the
[GITA:6275] Lord’ (plural). With this de rivation, this verse can also be interpreted as
[GITA:6276] follows – all the three types of action (right action, prohibited action , and
[GITA:6277] inaction) are implemented by the different forms of  the Lord under His
[GITA:6278] control. ‘Different Forms’ is implied by the plural (naha) indicated above.
[GITA:6280] H$_©Ê`H$_© `… ní`oXH$_©{U M H$_© `… Ÿ&
[GITA:6281] g ~w{Õ_mZ² _Zwî`ofw g `wº$… H¥$ËñZH$_©H¥$V² Ÿ&& 18&&
[GITA:6283] The wise realize that they do not perform activities independently
[GITA:6284] and even when they are not active (during sleeping, dreaming), there is
[GITA:6285] activity being performed (such as breathing) by the Lord Almighty. Such a
[GITA:6286] person is performing duties fully  and will derive full benefits thereon.
[GITA:6287] (4.18)
[GITA:6289] Comments: Having introduced the types of action in previous
[GITA:6290] verses, the Lord now describes these actions in the next few verses.
[GITA:6291] Prescribed duties performed by one wi th the knowledge that the actual
[GITA:6292] work is enabled by the Lord is doing the right action ( karma). The one who
[GITA:6293] performs duties without knowing that the Lord is enabling one to work
[GITA:6294] engages in incorrect/futile action ( akarma). Actions not approved by the
[GITA:6295] scriptures constitute prohibited action (vikarma).
[GITA:6297] Sri Rayaru in GV  provides another interesting, second interpretation
[GITA:6298] of this verse based on Sri Madhwacharya’s GTN. The word karma can also
[GITA:6299] mean the individual soul based on the obligation to perform duties. The
[GITA:6300] Lord is also termed akarma as He has no obligation to perform anything.
[GITA:6312] Chapter 4                                                                                                                                           127
[GITA:6314] With this, the verse can be interpreted to mean as follows – the one who
[GITA:6315] knows that the dependent individual soul has obligation  to perform duties,
[GITA:6316] and that the independent Lord Al mighty has no obligation for duties , is
[GITA:6317] indeed knowledgeable.  Such a person is performing right actions fully.
[GITA:6319] This verse is identified by  Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha in BGS  as
[GITA:6320] being the summary of this chapter. As this chapter is predominantly about
[GITA:6321] the concept of action (karma yoga), this verse provides a succinct summary
[GITA:6322] of the concepts presented.

[GITA:6341] One who performs prescribed duties and sacrifices without expecting
[GITA:6342] any rewards would have incinerated all activities in the fire of spiritual
[GITA:6343] knowledge. Learned people consider such a pers on as truly knowledgeable.
[GITA:6344] (4.19)
[GITA:6357] 128                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:6358] One with spiritual knowledge, who is detached from the outcomes of
[GITA:6359] activities, who is ever contented, and who is focused on the Lord, even
[GITA:6360] when involved in normal activities will be considered as not performing
[GITA:6361] any activities. (4.20)
[GITA:6363] One who performs duties without any expectations, who has control
[GITA:6364] over mind and intellect, and who has no attachment to the physical body
[GITA:6365] will not be tainted by sin for actions performed solely for physical
[GITA:6366] sustenance. (4.21)
[GITA:6368] One who is con tent with whatever is given by the Lord, who is
[GITA:6369] beyond dualities (such as pain or pleasure ), who harbors no jealousy and
[GITA:6370] who treats success or failure with equanimity will not be entangled by
[GITA:6371] actions. (4.22)
[GITA:6373] Actions will not taint one who acts without exp ectations, who is
[GITA:6374] unattached to the physical body, who has  the mind focused on the Lord and
[GITA:6375] who performs duties as an offering (yagna) to the Lord. (4.23)
[GITA:6377] Comments: Verse 4.18  identified a wise person as one who performs
[GITA:6378] prescribed duties fully and perfec tly. These five verses describe the major
[GITA:6379] characteristics of such a person.
[GITA:6381] 1. Pandita: Verse 4.19  describes one who has conclusive knowledge as
[GITA:6382] Pandita, as recognized by learned ones. Such a person would have
[GITA:6383] incinerated all activities in the fire of spiritual knowledge.
[GITA:6385] 2. Ever Contented: Verse 4.20  describes a wise person as being ever
[GITA:6386] contented and not having any needs. Such a person has no
[GITA:6387] attachment to either activities or any outcomes from activities and
[GITA:6388] considers the self as a reflection of the indepen dent Lord. Even when
[GITA:6389] performing actions, such a person is considered as  not performing
[GITA:6390] any action at all, meaning such actions will not be binding.
[GITA:6402] Chapter 4                                                                                                                                           129
[GITA:6404] 3. Detached: Verse 4.21  describes a wise person as one who performs
[GITA:6405] prescribed duties with no bodily attachment s. Such a person when
[GITA:6406] performing day to day activities for physical sustenance will not be
[GITA:6407] tainted by any sins arising from such actions.
[GITA:6409] 4. Equanimous: Verse 4.22  describes a wise person as one who is not
[GITA:6410] perturbed by happiness or sadness, gain, or loss etc . Such a person
[GITA:6411] will not harbor jealousy over someone’s success and will be content
[GITA:6412] with whatever is granted by the Lord.
[GITA:6414] 5. Conviction in Divine Knowledge: Verse 4.23  summarizes the
[GITA:6415] characteristics of the wise person described in the previous 4 verses
[GITA:6416] and states that such a person is able to achieve these characteristics
[GITA:6417] due to single minded focus on the Lord. Such a person will indeed
[GITA:6418] perform all prescribed activities without expectations , without bodily
[GITA:6419] attachment, with knowledge about the independent Lor d, and as an
[GITA:6420] offering (yagna) to please the Lord. Such activities will not entangle
[GITA:6421] a wise person and will pave the way for liberation by the grace of the
[GITA:6422] Lord.
[GITA:6424] Verse 4.22 seems to identify two characteristics of a wise person – one
[GITA:6425] who is beyond dualities and one who is equipoised in success or failure. Do
[GITA:6426] these both mean the same and hence there is a repetition here? No. Sri Jaya
[GITA:6427] Teertha in [PD] clarifies that these two characteristics have a causal
[GITA:6428] relationship. One who is tolerant of dualities is equip oised in success or
[GITA:6429] failure.

[GITA:6436] All articles and substances used in performing Vedic rituals ( yagna)
[GITA:6437] belong to the Lord. Various sacrifices, ghee and indeed fire itself and the
[GITA:6449] 130                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:6452] ritual activities are all under the control of the Lord as He pervades and

[GITA:6455] Comments: In the previous verse, a wise person is described as
[GITA:6456] someone who has conviction in divine knowledge. This verse explains  and
[GITA:6457] describes such conviction. All aspects involved in the performance of
[GITA:6458] yagna (sacrifice) are under the control of the Lord. This  is also consistent
[GITA:6459] with verse 4.21, where a wise person was described as one who is detached.
[GITA:6460] Sri Rayaru in GV  explains the proper way of interpreting compound words
[GITA:6461] such as brahma havi  following the interp retation in Sri Madhwacharya’s
[GITA:6462] GTN. There are multiple ways of de riving such compound words in
[GITA:6463] Sanskrit. There is a danger that one can interpret brahma havi to mean that
[GITA:6464] the sacrifices offered in a sacrifice is identical with the Lord. Sri
[GITA:6465] Madhwacharya [GTN] interprets brahma havi as brahmani + havi ,
[GITA:6466] meaning the sacrifices offered in a sacrifice belongs to the Lord. This
[GITA:6467] applies to other aspects appearing  in this verse. This interpretation is also
[GITA:6468] consistent with the characteristics of a w ise person described in verses
[GITA:6469] 4.19 – 4.23.
[GITA:6470] Notes: The Sanskrit word yagna does not have a direct equivalent in
[GITA:6471] English. In general, yagna means an intense act or endeavor that is
[GITA:6472] performed for a specific purpose such as propitiating the Lord Almighty or
[GITA:6473] some other deities. Many scholars loosely translate yagna as sacrifice,
[GITA:6474] perhaps referring to offerings that are sacrifice d during fire rituals. In
[GITA:6475] keeping with the traditional translation, yagna will be translated as sacrifice
[GITA:6476] in this book with the knowledge that yagna actually stands for an intense
[GITA:6477] endeavor performed for a specific purpose.

[GITA:6795] Comments: These three verses describe three major benefits from
[GITA:6796] ‘sacrifice of knowledge ’ - acquiring and acting on divine, spiritual
[GITA:6797] knowledge (jnana yagna). In verse 4.36, knowledge is compared to a boat.
[GITA:6798] Just as one needs a boat to cross a river, similarly one needs proper
[GITA:6799] knowledge to traverse the river of worldly afflictions. A boat does not row
[GITA:6800] itself. It needs a sailor. Similarly, mere knowledge is not goo d enough. One
[GITA:6801] needs a proper teacher, and one must practice and act  upon such
[GITA:6802] knowledge. In verse 4.37 , it is stated that the fire of knowledge burns off
[GITA:6803] ill-effects of action just as a blazing fire turns wood into ashes. This implies
[GITA:6804] that knowledge should be sharp, strong, and powerful, just like a blazing

[GITA:6880] Therefore, O Bharata! Using the sword of knowledge, cut asunder
[GITA:6881] the layer of doubts  caused due to ignorance  enveloping your mind . Lift
[GITA:6882] yourself up and get going on performing your yoga, i.e., the duty of
[GITA:6883] fighting this just war. (4.42)
[GITA:6885] Comments: Arjuna had developed deep doubts about the need to
[GITA:6886] fight the war based on his fears of losing near and dear ones. Lord Krishna
[GITA:6887] concludes the discussion in this chapter by encouraging Arjuna to get rid of

[GITA:6889] prescribed duty of waging the rightful war with proper conviction.
[GITA:6891] Summary of Chapter 4
[GITA:6893] In chapter 3, the Lord taught that one must perform one ’s prescribed
[GITA:6894] duties without expectations. In this chapter, the Lord teaches more about
[GITA:6895] the nature of activities ( karma) of both the Lord and individual beings. In
[GITA:6896] verses 4.1-3, the Lord says that He had taught th is spiritual knowledge
[GITA:6897] previously to deities such as Surya etc. In response to Arjuna’s question in
[GITA:6909] 140                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:6910] 4.4 about the chronology of the Lord’s current manifestation and those of
[GITA:6911] other deities, the Lord provides details of His incarnations in 4.5-9 stating
[GITA:6912] that He manifests at  His own free will from time to time to protect
[GITA:6913] righteousness and virtu e in society and to destroy evil. In verse 4.13 , the
[GITA:6914] Lord discusses the creatio n of living beings based on one ’s innate nature,
[GITA:6915] aptitude, and activities. In ver se 4.14 , the Lord states that He h as no
[GITA:6916] obligations and activities do not bind Him. He states that one who clearly
[GITA:6917] understands the distinction between the supreme soul and individual souls
[GITA:6918] will not be entangled by actions. Categories and nature of activ ities are
[GITA:6919] described in verses 4.16-33 which provide comparison of nishkama karma
[GITA:6920] to other types of activities ( karma), and details of the types of nishkama
[GITA:6921] karma. Verses 4.16 to 4.18 , compare the different types of activities –
[GITA:6922] karma (right action), vikarma (prohibited action), and akarma (inaction).
[GITA:6923] Verse 4.18 describes the two attributes of one who is performing one’s duty
[GITA:6924] perfectly– (i) such a person realizes that even when performing prescribed
[GITA:6925] duties, the actual work is being enabled by the Lord  himself  and (ii)  when
[GITA:6926] not actively performing duties , (ex: during  sleep, dream)  activity such as
[GITA:6927] breathing is enabled by the Lord. Such a wise person will derive full
[GITA:6928] benefits from duties performed. In that sense verse 4.18  is a summary of
[GITA:6929] this entire chapter. Five verses (4.1 9- 23) describe the  characteristics of
[GITA:6930] such a wise person, which briefly are – pandit (highly knowledgeable), ever
[GITA:6931] contented, detached, equanimous. That person would also have deep
[GITA:6932] conviction in divine, spiritual knowledg e. Verses 4.24-30 contain a
[GITA:6933] discussion on different ty pes of sacrifices performed by seekers in their
[GITA:6934] quest for self -realization and liberation. These verses emphatically state
[GITA:6935] that Vedic sacrifice (yagna) not only refer s to the symbolic act s of
[GITA:6936] propitiating deities with fire rituals etc., but also refer s to other selfless acts
[GITA:6937] such as donating to charity, devotional worship to  the Lord Almighty,
[GITA:6938] spiritual education, self -control, self -discipline etc. The discussion on
[GITA:6939] sacrifices is concluded in verse 4.32 where the Lord exhorts Arjuna to fight
[GITA:6940] the just war to protect his citizens as that is his prescribed duty. Performing
[GITA:6952] Chapter 4                                                                                                                                           141
[GITA:6954] one’s prescribed duty as an offering to the Lord is indeed a superior form of
[GITA:6955] worshipping the Lord. In verse 4.33 , the Lord teaches that action is
[GITA:6956] complete only when it is accompanied by knowledge. In verses 4.36-38, the
[GITA:6957] Lord describes the great ness of knowledge and in verse 4.39  outlines the
[GITA:6958] attributes of a seeker searching for right knowledge. This chapter is
[GITA:6959] concluded in verse  4.42, where Lord Krishna exhorts Arjuna to use
[GITA:6960] knowledge (jnana) to get over any doubts he had about waging the war and
[GITA:6961] to focus on fighting the just war with conviction.

[GITA:6978] Chapter 5 - The Path of Renunciation
[GITA:6980] Chapter Introduction:  This chapter of 29 ver ses is known as
[GITA:6981] Sanyasa Yoga  (The Path of Renunciation). Renunciation of worldly
[GITA:6982] pleasures is termed sanyasa and performing prescribed duties as an offering
[GITA:6983] to the Lord is termed yoga (action). In this chapter, the Lord answers
[GITA:6984] Arjuna’s questions on fundamental aspects of these two concepts – sanyasa
[GITA:6985] and yoga. Arjuna’s argument is  that if renunciation were a better option
[GITA:6986] than action, he c ould perhaps adopt the life of an ascetic and avoid waging
[GITA:6987] the war. The Lord goes on to describe the characteristics of a renunciant
[GITA:6988] and clarifies that one must incorporate both these paths to achieve self -
[GITA:6989] realization. The Lord reiterates that Arjuna must focus on performing his
[GITA:6990] prescribed duty of waging the war to protect his citizens from the evil
[GITA:6991] Kauravas. This chapter a lso delves into the importance of detachment and
[GITA:6992] the characteristics of seekers who have developed detachment from
[GITA:6993] rewards through self-control.
[GITA:6995] Action or Renunciation? Which is Better?
[GITA:6997] AOw©Z CdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:6998] gÝÝ¶mg§ H$_©Um§ H¥$îU nwZ`m}J§ M e§g{g Ÿ&
[GITA:6999] ¶ÀN´>o` EV`moaoH§$ VÝ_o ~«y{h gw{Z[üV_² Ÿ&& 1 &&
[GITA:7001] Arjuna said: O Krishna! Sometimes you seem to praise the path of
[GITA:7002] renunciation and other times you seem to praise the path of action. Please
[GITA:7003] tell me clearly, which of the two is beneficial. (5.1)
[GITA:7005] Comments: In verse 2.4 8, the Lord clearly directs Arjuna to focus
[GITA:7006] on his prescribed duties without expectations. This concept was expanded
[GITA:7007] in Chapter 3 (karma yoga). In verse 4.22, from Chapter 4 ( jnana yoga), the
[GITA:7008] Lord stated that one must be equanimous in the face of happiness /sadness
[GITA:7009] and be content with whatever is granted by Him. These two characteristics
[GITA:7021] Chapter 5                                                                                                                                                143
[GITA:7023] are described by ‘yoga’ and ‘sanyasa’. If the latter is the better path, then
[GITA:7024] Arjuna could conclude that he would be better off focusing on
[GITA:7025] relinquishing all activities  and developing equanimity and devotion to the
[GITA:7026] Lord. He could then perhaps avoid participating in the destructive war.
[GITA:7028] Sri Rayaru in GV  gives us a second interpretation, where the
[GITA:7029] question is related to the comparison between ascetics and householders.
[GITA:7030] Verse 4.41 can be interpreted as describing the attribute of a  seeker who
[GITA:7031] has relinquished all outcomes from actions and has taken on  the role of an
[GITA:7032] ascetic. Verse 4.42  directs that one must perform one ’s prescribed duties
[GITA:7033] and hence can be interpreted as referring to a householder. So, Arjuna
[GITA:7034] could also be enquiring about the comparison between an ascetic and a
[GITA:7035] householder, and if the former were the better of the two, he c ould perhaps
[GITA:7036] embrace ascetism and avoid the battle.
[GITA:7038] Action and Renunciation - Both required for Liberation
[GITA:7040] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&

[GITA:7044] The Lord said:  Renunciation of worldly pleasures ( sanyasa) and
[GITA:7045] performing prescribed duties (yoga) are both necessary for one to ach ieve
[GITA:7046] liberation. Performing prescribed action is better than merely renouncing
[GITA:7047] worldly pleasures. (5.2)
[GITA:7049] Comments: The Lord categorically states that both –renunciation of
[GITA:7050] worldly pleasures  (sanyasa) and  performing prescribed duties as an
[GITA:7051] offering to  Him (karma yoga ) are necessary for one to achieve
[GITA:7052] self-realization and liberation. One cannot conclude that only ascetics
[GITA:7053] practice detachment and they do not have any obligations on action. Nor do
[GITA:7054] householders only practice prescribed activities without practicing
[GITA:7055] self-control. So, one cannot argue that  sanyasa and karma yoga  cannot
[GITA:7056] co-exist in the same person. Lord Krishna recognizes Arjuna’s motivation
[GITA:7068] 144                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:7069] in this question and states that performing prescribed duties as an offering
[GITA:7070] to the Lord ( karma yoga) is su perior to mere detachment, equanimity etc.
[GITA:7071] (sanyasa), but both are required for achieving self -realization and ultimate
[GITA:7072] liberation. Again, the Lord is impressing upon Arjuna that he must not
[GITA:7073] avoid participating in his prescribed duty of fighting the just war.

[GITA:7313] with temporary, worldly rewards and will never be able to escape from the
[GITA:7314] cycle of samsara.
[GITA:7316] gd©H$_m©{U _Zgm gÝÝ`ñ`m@ñVo gwI§ der Ÿ&

[GITA:7319] True happiness is experienced by those who completely surrender to

[GITA:7325] aware that none of the actions performed by that seeker are independently

[GITA:7353] Doership – Individual Souls and Lord Almighty
[GITA:7355] Z H$V¥©Ëd§ Z H$_m©{U bmoH$ñ` g¥O{V à^w… Ÿ&
[GITA:7356] Z H$_©\$bg§`moJ§ ñd^mdñVw àdV©Vo Ÿ&& 14 &&
[GITA:7358] ZmXÎmo H$ñ`{MV² nmn§ Z M¡d gwH¥$V§ {d^w… Ÿ&
[GITA:7359] AkmZoZm@d¥V§ kmZ§ VoZ _w÷pÝV OÝVd… Ÿ&& 15 &&
[GITA:7361] A living being cannot perform activities independently or get
[GITA:7362] activities performed by others nor achieve fruits from such actions nor get
[GITA:7363] fruits for others independently. The ever -independent Lord is responsible
[GITA:7364] for all these actions. (5.14)
[GITA:7366] Living beings cannot independently diminish sins nor claim credit
[GITA:7367] for good deeds. Their knowledge is veiled by ignorance, and hence they are
[GITA:7368] deluded. Being deluded, they cannot realize the Lord. (5.15)
[GITA:7370] Comments: Verses 5.8&5.9 state that living beings, wh en they interact
[GITA:7371] with the external world ( through actions such as seeing, talking) are not
[GITA:7372] actually doing so on their own. These two verses provide more insight into
[GITA:7373] the nature of action s as they relate t o living beings. Sri Rayaru in GV
[GITA:7374] provides two inter pretations for these verses depending on the attribution
[GITA:7375] for the words ‘prabhu’ in 5.14 and ‘vibhu’ in 5.15, both of which mean the
[GITA:7376] Lord. These two words can be either attributed to jiva, the individual soul
[GITA:7377] (as it is superior to inert objects) as also to the Lord Almighty (who is the
[GITA:7378] Lord of all).
[GITA:7390] Chapter 5                                                                                                                                                151
[GITA:7393]  Individual Souls: The first half of the verse 5.14 states that individual
[GITA:7394] souls cannot act on their own or can they cause action by someone
[GITA:7395] else. How about the reward for actions performed, regardless of how
[GITA:7396] they are performed? The second half of the verse (5.14) answers by
[GITA:7397] stating that individuals also do not have independence on the issue  of
[GITA:7398] rewards. The first half of 5.15  states that individual souls do not
[GITA:7399] accrue negative or positive effects of action on thei r own. If the Lord
[GITA:7400] is responsible for all actions, why is it that no one can physically see
[GITA:7401] the Lord? The second ha lf of 5.15  states that individuals cannot see
[GITA:7402] the Lord as they are covered by ignorance.
[GITA:7404]  Lord Almighty: The Lord has not granted individuals , ability to act
[GITA:7405] on their own. Likewise, the Lord has also not granted individuals, the
[GITA:7406] liberty to claim reward s for their actions on their own. If the Lord is
[GITA:7407] responsible for all actions of the individuals, will the Lord not be
[GITA:7408] tainted by such actions? The first half of 5.15  states that the Lord is
[GITA:7409] not tainted by actions of the individuals. The Lord provides
[GITA:7410] individuals apparatus and facilities to act based on the individuals’
[GITA:7411] innate nature to help them in their spiritual journey.
[GITA:7412] There are several questio ns that arise at this stage regarding the nature
[GITA:7413] of actions related to an individual soul, inert objects, and the Lord. These
[GITA:7414] questions are summarized as follows:
[GITA:7415]  If an individual soul does not have independence in performing
[GITA:7416] actions, how can that soul be held responsible for the consequences
[GITA:7417] of such actions?
[GITA:7419]  If the Lord Almighty is the one who is independent and is
[GITA:7420] responsible for all actions performed by individual souls, how can
[GITA:7421] the Lord be immune from the effects of such actions?
[GITA:7422] Sri Madhwacharya in hi s commentary on the Brahma Sutras  [BSB]
[GITA:7423] and in other works such as GTN , adequately answers these questions.
[GITA:7435] 152                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:7436] Firstly, one must understand the nature of attributes, doership (doer is an
[GITA:7437] entity that performs some action) and independence as they relate to the
[GITA:7438] three entities in the universe namely, individual souls, inert objects, and the
[GITA:7439] Lord Almighty.
[GITA:7441] Attribute\Entity Inert Objects Individual Souls Lord Almighty
[GITA:7442] Doership No Yes Yes
[GITA:7443] Independence No No Yes
[GITA:7445] The Lord  is independent in all aspects and has un limited ability to
[GITA:7446] perform activities independently. Hence, He has both doership and
[GITA:7447] independence. Inert objects neither have ability to perform anything nor do
[GITA:7448] they have independence. Individual souls do have doership but not
[GITA:7449] independence, hence they have  dependent doership. The relationship
[GITA:7450] between the Lord, inert objects and living beings is illustrated with the
[GITA:7451] example of a dairy farmer milking a cow through it s udders in Sri
[GITA:7452] Madhwacharya’s GTN 3-33. All three entities are required in the task of
[GITA:7453] extracting milk from a cow. The udder is akin to an inert object. It cannot
[GITA:7454] act, nor does it have any awareness or intent. The cow is  a living being. It
[GITA:7455] has awareness, it produces milk, it has an intention to give milk, but it
[GITA:7456] cannot independently extract milk f rom itself. The dairy farmer is like the
[GITA:7457] Lord who uses the udder and extracts milk from the cow.
[GITA:7458] Armed with the above information, the two questions raised can be
[GITA:7459] answered as follows:
[GITA:7461]  Individual souls also have the quality of doership, but they are  not
[GITA:7462] independent. The Lord grants individuals the ability to perform
[GITA:7463] activities based on their innate intent ( iccha), attempt (prayatna) and
[GITA:7464] knowledge ( jnana). After all everyone has an intent to achieve
[GITA:7465] liberation. The Lord recognizes this intent and grants the souls
[GITA:7466] facilities such as a physical body, mind, intellect and sense organs to
[GITA:7467] attain knowledge and perform prescribed duties. Even though
[GITA:7468] individual souls do not have independence in action, they do have
[GITA:7469] responsibility for their actions and hence are subje ct to dos and
[GITA:7481] Chapter 5                                                                                                                                                153
[GITA:7483] don’ts (vidhi, nishedha). The key here is the intent that is present in
[GITA:7484] individual souls. This concept is clarified in Brahma Sutra (2.3.47).
[GITA:7486]  The Lord is not tainted by actions performed by individual souls as
[GITA:7487] the Lord merely grants them the  ability to perform such actions. The
[GITA:7488] Lord has nothing to gain by providing  individual souls with the
[GITA:7489] facilities they need. He does so out of pure compassion.
[GITA:7491] With the above information one can also resolve apparent conflicts in
[GITA:7492] spiritual texts where in s ome texts individual souls are described as not
[GITA:7493] having the attribute of doership, while in other texts the individual souls are
[GITA:7494] described as having the attribute of doership. The former is indicating that
[GITA:7495] the doership is not independent and the latter is i ndicating that the doership
[GITA:7496] is dependent.
[GITA:7498] kmZoZ Vw VXkmZ§ `ofm§ Zm{eV_mË_Z… Ÿ&
[GITA:7499] Vofm_m{XË`dÁkmZ§ àH$me`{V VËna_² Ÿ&& 16 &&
[GITA:7501] For those whose ignorance is destroyed by proper knowledge about
[GITA:7502] the Lord, that very knowledge will reveal  the Supreme Lord to them like a
[GITA:7503] brilliant sun. (5.16)
[GITA:7505] Comments: The previous verse 5.15  indicated that the limitations of
[GITA:7506] individual beings are due to their knowledge enveloped by ignorance. This
[GITA:7507] verse clarifies how such ig norance can be overcome. If one ’s innate
[GITA:7508] knowledge is cov ered by ignorance , how can that person be convinced to
[GITA:7509] perform prescribed duties (yoga) with detachment (sanyasa)? Sri Rayaru in
[GITA:7510] GV explains that knowledge that is enveloped by ignorance is the innate
[GITA:7511] knowledge (swaroopa jnana ) that is specific to a soul. The ignorance can
[GITA:7512] be removed by the seeker obtaining proper knowledge through scriptural
[GITA:7513] studies and teachings from a Guru. This knowledge is termed ‘ paroksha’
[GITA:7514] (indirect). Thus, a seeker by obtaining paroksha knowledge can get rid of
[GITA:7515] ignorance, perform pre scribed duties with detachment and attain divine,
[GITA:7516] spiritual (aparoksha or direct) knowledge and reach the Lord.

[GITA:7809] Summary of Chapter 5
[GITA:7811] In chapter 3, the Lord t aught that one must perform one s prescribed
[GITA:7812] duties without expectations . (nishkama karma ). In chapter 4, the Lord
[GITA:7813] imparts knowledge ( jnana) about the nature of activities ( karma) of both
[GITA:7814] the Lord and ind ividual beings. In chapter 5, the Lord answers some
[GITA:7815] fundamental questions from Arjuna (5.1) regarding the concepts of
[GITA:7816] renunciation ( sanyasa) and action ( karma). It is apparent from Arjuna’s
[GITA:7817] question that if renunciation were a better option than action, he  could
[GITA:7818] perhaps adopt the life of an ascetic and avoid waging the war. The Lord
[GITA:7819] answers (5.2) by stating that while both the paths of renunciation and action
[GITA:7820] lead one to liberation, the path of action is superior. The Lord goes on to
[GITA:7821] describe the character istics of a renunciant (5.2) and clarifies that one must
[GITA:7822] incorporate both these paths to achieve self -realization (5.6). An of t quoted
[GITA:7823] example is that of a person who is sick in the stomach due to an unhealthy
[GITA:7824] diet. For such a person to heal , it is importa nt to both consume the
[GITA:7825] medication prescribed by the doctor and at the same time avoid indulging
[GITA:7826] in an unhealthy diet. By stating that the path of action is superior, the Lord
[GITA:7827] is clarifying to Arjuna that he must participate in his prescribed duty of
[GITA:7828] waging this war to protect his citizens , while detaching himself from any
[GITA:7829] outcomes of his actions. The Lord also clarifies that both ascetics and
[GITA:7830] householders are equally eligible to attain salvation , based on their efforts.
[GITA:7831] An ascetic who may have acquired divi ne, spiritual knowledge will still be
[GITA:7832] involved in performing activities and likewise a householder who is
[GITA:7833] preoccupied with performing prescribed activities will also be involved in
[GITA:7834] acquiring spiritual knowledge. Some scriptures downplay the role of
[GITA:7846] Chapter 5                                                                                                                                                161
[GITA:7848] actions such as ritual fire sacrifices which may only result in eye irritation ,
[GITA:7849] due to smoke. It is clarified that any such description of action is related to
[GITA:7850] actions that are performed with specific expectations. They do not apply to
[GITA:7851] actions performed as an off ering to the Lord without expectations (5.4). It
[GITA:7852] is also clarified that one cannot achieve much by merely relinquishing the
[GITA:7853] outcomes of actions, without offering them to the Lord. Any activity can be
[GITA:7854] deemed as complete and useful only when such activities are performed
[GITA:7855] with a pure mind and as an offering to the Lord with no material
[GITA:7856] expectations (5.6). An ideal seeker is one who performs prescribed duties
[GITA:7857] with detachment towards the rewards, performs activities while exercising
[GITA:7858] control over sense organs and the mind, knows that the Lord is the one who
[GITA:7859] is causing the action, and is aware that the Lord Almighty is the L ord of
[GITA:7860] everyone in the universe. He  performs activities with devotion and as a
[GITA:7861] worship to the Lord. Such a seeker will not be tainted by any ef fects of
[GITA:7862] actions just as water does not stick to a lotus leaf (5.10). One should realize
[GITA:7863] that it is the Lord who makes it possible for one to perform any activity.
[GITA:7864] The Lord activates all activities in the universe. However, the individual
[GITA:7865] souls are responsible for the outcomes of their activities, even though they
[GITA:7866] are enabled to act by the Lord. The individual soul has dependent doership
[GITA:7867] and the Lord is the only independent doer. The Lord activates the intent and
[GITA:7868] attempt of the individual souls , hence the i ndividual souls are held
[GITA:7869] responsible for the actions. The Lord is never tainted by any such actions ,
[GITA:7870] as He has nothing to gain by any action and performs them out of pure
[GITA:7871] compassion for the individual souls (5 -14, 5-15). The nature of knowledge
[GITA:7872] in learned ones is described in verses 5.15 to 5.17 . Knowledge is of two
[GITA:7873] types, indirect and direct. The inherent knowledge in individual souls is
[GITA:7874] masked by ignorance, and seekers get rid of this ignorance through spiritual
[GITA:7875] studies, analysis, and listening to lecture s from teachers (indirect
[GITA:7876] knowledge) etc. This paves the way for seekers to achieve self -realization
[GITA:7877] (direct knowledge). Learned ones perceive the same blemishless Lord full
[GITA:7878] of infinite auspicious attributes present in all living beings (5.18). Learned
[GITA:7879] ones who have developed detachment from sense pleasure , experience
[GITA:7880] peace due to a sense of liberation, but everlasting bliss is only possible
[GITA:7881] through meditation with the mind focused exclusively on the Lord (5.12).
[GITA:7893] 162                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:7894] Learned ones avoid indulging in sense pleasures which are temporary and
[GITA:7895] lead only to misery  (5.22). The Lord exhorts one to develop control over
[GITA:7896] sense organs and emotions such as desire, anger in one ’s current lifetime
[GITA:7897] itself while one has a human form, as this will not be possible with other
[GITA:7898] life f orms (5.23). The procedure for performing concentrated meditation
[GITA:7899] which was stated as a necessity in verse 5.21 is described in verses 5.27 and
[GITA:7900] 5.28. The chapter is concluded in 5.29  which describes the characteristics
[GITA:7901] of the Lord who is the goal of such m editation. A seeker who meditates on
[GITA:7902] the Lord, knowing the Lord as the consumer of all sacrifices and rituals, as
[GITA:7903] the Lord of all, and as one who is the well-wisher for everyone, will indeed
[GITA:7904] achieve liberation.

[GITA:7923] Chapter 6 - The Path of Self Restraint
[GITA:7925] Chapter Introduction: This chapter of 47 verses is termed Atma
[GITA:7926] Samyama Yoga (The Path of Self Restraint) or Dhyana Yoga (The Path of
[GITA:7927] Meditation). The previous chapters described the broad contours of the path
[GITA:7928] of action ( karma yoga ) and the path of knowledge ( jnana yoga ). Further,
[GITA:7929] the characteristics of a seeker who is on a  journey to self -realization were
[GITA:7930] broadly identified as one having detachment from outcomes of action
[GITA:7931] (sanyasa) and perform ing prescribed duties ( yoga) as an offering to the
[GITA:7932] Lord. This was briefly described in verse 2.39 . Yoga as described here
[GITA:7933] prepares a seeker to learn more about the greatness of the Lord which is
[GITA:7934] covered in detail in chapters 7 to 12. This chapter delves m ore into the
[GITA:7935] details of yoga (action) and its components. Yoga has two components –
[GITA:7936] external and internal. The external component of yoga refers to the
[GITA:7937] prescribed activities that one must perform that are visible to others. For
[GITA:7938] example, Arjuna waging the w ar to protect his citizens from the Kauravas’
[GITA:7939] misrule. This aspect of yoga was briefly described in verse 2.45  and was
[GITA:7940] expanded in chapters 3 to 5. The internal component of yoga is termed
[GITA:7941] dhyana yoga (path of meditation), This is also an essential aspect of yoga
[GITA:7942] and was briefly described in verse 5.27 . This chapter delves into details of
[GITA:7943] dhyana yoga . Characteristics of a true yogi are described. The physical
[GITA:7944] aspects of meditation such as place, physical pose, breath control etc., are
[GITA:7945] also described. Requir ements for moderation in consumption are also
[GITA:7946] discussed. To a question from Arjuna regarding the condition of those who
[GITA:7947] make a sincere attempt but are not able to successfully implement karma
[GITA:7948] and dhyana, the Lord teaches that no  sincere effort is a waste, and such
[GITA:7949] seekers will get additional opportunities to complete their spiritual journey.
[GITA:7966] 164                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:7967] The Ascetic and the Yogi
[GITA:7969] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&

[GITA:7972] The Lord said:  One who performs prescribed duties without
[GITA:7973] expectations is both a real ascetic and a real yogi; not the one who has
[GITA:7974] simply relinquished performing ritual fire sacrifices. (6.1).
[GITA:7976] Comments: As indicated before, this chapter delves into details of
[GITA:7977] dhyana yoga, or the internal component of yoga (path of action). When is a
[GITA:7978] seeker eligible to follow the path of dhyana (meditation) which prepares
[GITA:7979] one to learn about the qualities of  the Lord? This verse states that a true
[GITA:7980] seeker who has both detachment towards outcomes of actions  and
[GITA:7981] commitment to performing prescribed duties is ready and eligible for
[GITA:7982] dhyana yoga.
[GITA:7984] Some schools such as sankhya, hold the view that ascetics who have
[GITA:7985] relinquished ritual fire sacrifices are the only ones eligible for dhyana yoga.
[GITA:7986] This verse clarifies  that even ascetics have obligations to perform
[GITA:7987] sacrifices such as worship of the  Lord, learning and preaching scripture s
[GITA:7988] etc., as was stated in verse 4.25 . Hence all seekers (including ascetics,  and
[GITA:7989] householders) are eligible for dhyana yoga if they perform their prescribed
[GITA:7990] duties without expectations.

[GITA:7995] O Pandava (Arjuna)! Understand that relinquishing passions such as
[GITA:7996] desire and anger (detachment) is an integral part of karma yoga. One who
[GITA:7997] is performing activities without getting rid of desire is not a real yogi. (6.2)
[GITA:8010] Chapter 6                                                                                                                                             165
[GITA:8012] Comments: Previous verses stated that a real seeker has both the
[GITA:8013] characteristics of detachment from outcomes and commitment to
[GITA:8014] performing prescribed activities, which are broadly termed sanyasa and
[GITA:8015] yoga. To emphasize the fact that these are not separate paths, this verse
[GITA:8016] explicitly states that sanyasa as described here is an essential component of
[GITA:8017] yoga.
[GITA:8019] Amééjmo_w©Zo`m}J§ H$_© H$maU_wÀ`Vo Ÿ&

[GITA:8022] For the one who has indirect knowledge (through scriptures) of the
[GITA:8023] Lord, the path of achieving direct, divine knowledge is through the path of
[GITA:8024] action. One who has achieved direct knowledge of the Lord, through
[GITA:8025] steadfast pr ayer and meditation, will experience exuberance in bliss upon
[GITA:8026] liberation. (6.3)
[GITA:8028] Comments: Knowledge is of two types. Indirect knowledge
[GITA:8029] (paroksha jnana) is the knowledge that a seeker acquires through study of
[GITA:8030] scriptures, from listening to teachers etc. T his knowledge helps t he seeker
[GITA:8031] to get rid of ignorance that cover s innate knowledge (verse 5.16). A seeker
[GITA:8032] armed with such indirect knowledge, by practicing sanyasa and yoga, will
[GITA:8033] be eligible for self-realization through direct, divine knowledge ( aparoksha
[GITA:8034] jnana). Will an aparoksha jnani indulge in activities and if so, what is to be
[GITA:8035] gained? This verse builds  upon the description in verse 3.20  and clarifies
[GITA:8036] that an aparoksha jnani continues to perform activities to set an example to
[GITA:8037] the society. Such action s are not wasted efforts but will result in increased
[GITA:8038] exuberance in bliss upon liberation. There is another difference in duties
[GITA:8039] performed by paroksha and aparoksha jnanis . The former needs to also
[GITA:8040] engage in service to society to help those in need (just a s one needs to pay
[GITA:8041] taxes). The latter does not have such  a broad mandate but needs to serve
[GITA:8042] superior souls.

[GITA:8060] One who is naturally disinterested in sense pleasures, has no
[GITA:8061] attachment to actions, and performs actions only as an offering to the Lord
[GITA:8062] is said to have achieved direct knowledge of the Lord. (6.4)
[GITA:8064] Comments: This verse describes the characteristics of a realized
[GITA:8065] soul (aparoksha jnani ) who has attained direct, divi ne knowledge. Such a
[GITA:8066] person is said to be naturally disinterested in sense pleasures and in rewards
[GITA:8067] from actions. This is different from other seekers who are yet to reach this
[GITA:8068] stage. These other seekers may also have developed aversion to sense
[GITA:8069] pleasures, but such aversion does not come to them naturally. They must
[GITA:8070] actively practice control of sense organs.
[GITA:8072] The Mind is a Friend and an Enemy
[GITA:8074] CÕaoXmË_Zm@@Ë_mZ§ Zm@Ë_mZ_dgmX`oV² Ÿ&

[GITA:8077] One should elevate oneself th rough the mind and should never fall
[GITA:8078] into misery because of a weak mind. The mind is one’s friend and is also
[GITA:8079] one’s enemy. (6.5)
[GITA:8081] Comments: The next few verses describe the role of the mind in a
[GITA:8082] seeker’s evolution. The specialty of this verse is that it ha s 7 repetitions of
[GITA:8083] the word ‘atma’. This is a remarkably interesting word i n Sanskrit that has
[GITA:8084] different meanings such as – self, Lord Almighty, mind, intellect, devotion
[GITA:8085] etc. One can decipher the actual meaning only by looking at the context in
[GITA:8086] which this word is used. The above translation interprets the 7 occurrences
[GITA:8087] of atma as one, oneself, mind, mind, mind, one and mind.
[GITA:8089] Sri Rayaru [GV] provides an alternate meaning of this verse by
[GITA:8090] interpreting atma as the Lord Almighty in some places. T he Lord is o nes
[GITA:8102] Chapter 6                                                                                                                                             167
[GITA:8104] friend and the Lord is also one ’s enemy. Hence, one must strive to earn  the
[GITA:8105] Lord’s grace and one must avoid earning His wrath.
[GITA:8107] ~ÝYwamË_m@@Ë_ZñVñ` `oZmË_¡dmË_Zm {OV… Ÿ&

[GITA:8110] For one who wins over the mind with the intellect, the mind is
[GITA:8111] indeed a friend. For one who cannot win over  the mind, it becomes an
[GITA:8112] enemy (the Lord becomes a friend to the devoted, and an enemy to those
[GITA:8113] not devoted). (6.6)
[GITA:8115] Comments: This verse provides the reason for the mind to be
[GITA:8116] someone’s friend or enemy. For one who has developed control over  the
[GITA:8117] mind using the intellect, the mind is a friend. For such a seeker, the mind is
[GITA:8118] a fertile ground for performing concentrated meditation on the Lord. For
[GITA:8119] one who has no control over the mind, the m ind itself becomes an enemy.
[GITA:8120] So, the mind is like a key, which can be used to both lock and open a door.
[GITA:8122] A second interpretation as per Sri Rayaru in GV is as follows: For a
[GITA:8123] seeker who has won over the Lord through devotion, the Lord becomes a
[GITA:8124] friend. Those who are not devoted to the Lord will have the Lord as their
[GITA:8125] enemy. In the above two interpretations the word ‘ atma’ has been
[GITA:8126] translated as intellect and devotion, respectively.

[GITA:8173] Such a person treats everyone – well-wishers, friends, enemies,

[GITA:8197]  Friends: Those who go out of their way to save others from danger

[GITA:8331] O Arjuna! One cannot achieve benefits of such meditation if one
[GITA:8332] over eats or does not eat at all. Similarly, one who oversleeps or does not
[GITA:8333] sleep at all, will also lose all benefits from meditation. (6.16)

[GITA:8336] moderation in eating, relaxing, sleeping, and other daily activities. (6.17)
[GITA:8338] Comments: These two verses describe the requirements for physical
[GITA:8339] wellbeing for a seeker to successfully perform concentrated meditation . It
[GITA:8340] is important for a seeker to ensure physical wellbeing by observing
[GITA:8341] moderation in habits such as eating, sleeping etc. It is evident from practice
[GITA:8342] that overeating leads to bodily discomfort. Similarly, oversleeping leads to
[GITA:8343] laziness and lethargy. Neit her of these conditions are conducive for
[GITA:8344] meditation. Likewise, one should not unnecessarily indulge in difficult,
[GITA:8345] strict fasting (as some do to reduce weight) as this can also have health
[GITA:8346] consequences. Basically, one needs to observe moderation in eating and
[GITA:8347] sleeping. However, those who are in good physical condition, should not
[GITA:8348] avoid fasting on special days such as Ekadashi.

[GITA:8631] Arjuna said: O Madhusoodana! I cannot see how the mind, which by

[GITA:8634] O Krishna! The mind is always w avering, it is turbulent, it is strong
[GITA:8635] and obstinate. It can corrupt one’s body and sense organs. It is my view that
[GITA:8636] trying to control the mind is extremely difficult, just like catching  the wind.
[GITA:8637] (6.34)
[GITA:8649] Chapter 6                                                                                                                                             179

[GITA:8655] organs astray. How ca n one control such a mind ? It would be like trying to
[GITA:8656] capture the wind. These are natural questions that would arise in a seeker.

[GITA:8665] The Lord said:  O Arjuna, One with Strong Arms! No doubt it is
[GITA:8666] exceedingly difficult to control the wavering mind. O Son of Kunti! It can
[GITA:8667] be controlled b y practice (of dhyana meditation) and de tachment (from

[GITA:8670] One who cannot achieve control over the mind can never benefit
[GITA:8671] from meditation. One should strive to achieve mind -control through

[GITA:8674] Comments: In these tw o verses, the Lord prescribes two ways for
[GITA:8675] one to achieve control over the mind. One would be to keep practicing
[GITA:8676] dhyana meditation and the other would be to develop detachment from
[GITA:8677] sense pleasures. Both these are not easy to achieve but one must strive to
[GITA:8678] continuously practice and over time one will be able to control one ’s mind.
[GITA:8679] It is evident from one ’s experience that one interested in learning any skill
[GITA:8680] in life such as sports or music, must continuously practice and never give
[GITA:8681] up. We see many examples of  high achievers who have excelled in their
[GITA:8682] chosen profession by sheer grit, determination, and constant practice. The
[GITA:8694] 180                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:8695] same qualities when applied to meditation and detachment will he lp one
[GITA:8696] develop control over one’s mind.
[GITA:8698] One can question as to why one wo uld need to develop detachment
[GITA:8699] by avoiding indulgence in sensual pleasures as one can wait for such time
[GITA:8700] till all desires are exhausted. Sri Jaya  Teertha in PD  uses the example of a
[GITA:8701] wayward, drunk elephant which naturally becomes tame with exhaustion.
[GITA:8702] But this is not true of sense organs. I t is impossible to satiate sense organs
[GITA:8703] by mere consumption. For example, one who craves good food and
[GITA:8704] consumes it in excess may temporarily feel satisfied and in fact may refuse
[GITA:8705] more food due to exhaustion. However, this  feeling does not last, and the
[GITA:8706] craving comes back the next day. So, one must continuously practice
[GITA:8707] detachment to achieve control over one’s mind.
