[GITA:8852] spiritual path  and will eventually be rid of sins and reach His abode. It
[GITA:8853] must be noted that mere intention to perform prescribed activities and
[GITA:8854] dhyana meditation are not enough. That intention must be followed by
[GITA:8855] sincere attempts at execution.
[GITA:8857] Vnpñdä`mo@{YH$mo `moJr km{Zä`mo@{n _Vmo@{YH$…Ÿ&
[GITA:8858] H${_©ä`üm{YH$mo `moJr Vñ_mX² ¶moJr ^dmOw©Z Ÿ&& 46&&
[GITA:8860] One who is on the path of intense meditation on the Lord is superior
[GITA:8861] to the one who practices strict penance. Such a seeker is also superior to
[GITA:8862] one who has attained (indirect) spiritual knowledge and superior also to one
[GITA:8863] focused on performing only ritualistic activities. O Arjuna! Immerse
[GITA:8864] yourself in such intense meditation on the Lord. (6.46)
[GITA:8877] 184                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:8878] Comments: In this verse, the Lord extols the virtues of dhyana yoga.
[GITA:8879] Performing concentrated medi tation on the Lord, being fully aware of the
[GITA:8880] Lord’s infinite auspicious attributes devoid of blemishes and  performing
[GITA:8881] prescribed activities only as an offering the Lord without expectations is
[GITA:8882] the most superior path for a seeker to attain the Lord.
[GITA:8884] The Superior Yogi
[GITA:8886] `mo{JZm_{n gd}fm§ _ÒVoZmÝVamË_Zm Ÿ&
[GITA:8887] lÕmdmZ² ^OVo `mo _m§ g _o `wº$V_mo _V… Ÿ&& 47 &&
[GITA:8889] A seeker who performs such dhyana yoga with devotion to the Lord
[GITA:8890] is superior. The one who performs such yoga by serving the  Lord is more
[GITA:8891] superior and the one who performs such yoga with devotion, service and
[GITA:8892] without any expectations is the most superior among all such seekers.
[GITA:8893] (6.47)
[GITA:8895] Comments: The Lord concludes the teaching on dhyana yoga
[GITA:8896] meditation by describing the relativ e gradations among seekers who
[GITA:8897] perform such yoga. Some perform their prescribed activities and exercise
[GITA:8898] concentrated meditation on the Lord. When such meditation is combined
[GITA:8899] with devotion to the Lord (and is not done just mechanically ), such efforts
[GITA:8900] are co nsidered superior by the Lord. Seekers who go a step further and
[GITA:8901] offer their service to the Lord are even more superior. Finally, seekers who
[GITA:8902] perform prescribed duties with devotion, with their minds fully immersed
[GITA:8903] in the Lord and serve the Lord without an y expectation are considered by
[GITA:8904] Lord Krishna to be the most superior among all seekers.
[GITA:8906] Given that the purpose of this chapter is to teach path of dhyana
[GITA:8907] (meditation), this last verse fully summarizes the core concepts in this
[GITA:8908] chapter. Hence, it is consid ered the summary verse by Sri  Madinur Vishnu
[GITA:8909] Teertha in his BGS.
[GITA:8923] Chapter 6                                                                                                                                             185
[GITA:8925] Summary of Chapter 6
[GITA:8927] The previous chapters described the paths of action and knowledge
[GITA:8928] (karma yoga, jnana yoga). Yoga has two components – external (prescribed
[GITA:8929] activities that one performs  which are visible to others ) and internal . The
[GITA:8930] internal component of yoga is termed dhyana yoga  (path of meditation),
[GITA:8931] This chapter delves into details of dhyana yoga or atma samyama yoga (the
[GITA:8932] Path of Self -Restraint). The Lord starts by stating that a real  yogi is one
[GITA:8933] who relinquishes expectations from actions and not one who merely gives
[GITA:8934] up ritual fire sacrifices (6.1). Such a seeker also has societal obligations to
[GITA:8935] help the underprivileged (6.3). A seeker must exercise control over the
[GITA:8936] sense organs and the mind. The importance of  the mind which can be both
[GITA:8937] a friend and a foe to a seeker is explained in verses 6.5–6.8. A yogi sees the
[GITA:8938] Lord equally in everyone. The process of meditation in terms of location,
[GITA:8939] physical pose etc., are described in verses 6.10 –6.14. Successful meditation
[GITA:8940] also requires moderation in activities such a s eating, sleeping etc. Verses
[GITA:8941] 6.20-6.23 describe the nature of inner bliss experienced by a yogi during
[GITA:8942] dhyana meditation. The requirement for controlling  the sense organs and
[GITA:8943] the mind for successful medi tation are described in verses 6.24 -6.32.
[GITA:8944] Arjuna expresses the difficulty one would face in controlling the mind in
[GITA:8945] verses 6.33 -6.34, and Lord Krishna describes  the solution for the fate of
[GITA:8946] those seekers who may sincerely approach  the spiritual path but are not
[GITA:8947] able to execute it for various reasons. In verses 6.40 -6.45, the Lord assures
[GITA:8948] that no sincere efforts are wasted, and the seeker will get additional
[GITA:8949] opportunities for self -realization in future births. In verse 6.47 , the Lord
[GITA:8950] concludes the teachings in this chapter by stating th at among all seekers
[GITA:8951] who practis e dhyana meditation, superior are those who perform their
[GITA:8952] prescribed activities with devotion to the Lord, without expectations .
[GITA:8954] && h{V fð>mo@Ü¶m`… &&
[GITA:8955] End of Chapter 6
[GITA:8967] 186                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:8969] gá_mo@Ü`m`… - kmZ{dkmZ`moJ…
[GITA:8970] Chapter 7 - The Path of Knowledge and Wisdom
[GITA:8972] Chapter Introduction: In this chapter of 30 verses, the Lord teaches
[GITA:8973] the concepts of jnana (knowledge) and vijnana (special knowledge or
[GITA:8974] wisdom). In verse 2.39, the Lord stated that He w ould teach about the yoga
[GITA:8975] (way or path) to achieve divine, spiritual knowledge, knowing which one
[GITA:8976] would be able to properly perform prescribed duties, get rid of accrued sins ,
[GITA:8977] and achieve liberation. Such procedures were described from chapters 2 to
[GITA:8978] 6. The  path described had two components, external and internal. The
[GITA:8979] external component dealt with the procedures to be performed, and this was
[GITA:8980] covered till chapter 5. Chapter 6 dealt with the internal procedure of
[GITA:8981] dhyana meditation that a seeker needs to perfor m. Thus, the first 6 chapters
[GITA:8982] were broadly concerned with descriptions of the  methods and procedures
[GITA:8983] (both external and internal) a seeker would need to perform to be able to
[GITA:8984] acquire divine, spiritual knowledge. The next 6 chapters describe in more
[GITA:8985] detail such divine, spiritual knowledge about the Lord Almighty , which
[GITA:8986] forms the principal message of the Gita. In the earlier chapters 2 – 6, there
[GITA:8987] were some discussions on the Lord’s attributes which were included
[GITA:8988] contextually, but the next 6 chapters provide m ore, exclusive details about
[GITA:8989] the Lord’s attributes. The term jnana in general means ordinary knowledge,
[GITA:8990] which is acquired through the study of scriptures, learning from teachers
[GITA:8991] etc. This is also known as paroksha jnana  (indirect knowledge) , as one
[GITA:8992] acquires this before attaining self -realization. Vijnana is specialis ed
[GITA:8993] knowledge or wisdom acquired after self -realization. This is also known as
[GITA:8994] aparoksha jnana  (direct knowledge). This chapter provides a detailed
[GITA:8995] discussion of the se two types of knowledge .  The two types of knowledge
[GITA:8996] are specifically about the Lord Almighty.
[GITA:9012] Chapter 7                                                                                                                                             187
[GITA:9014] Discourse on Divinity
[GITA:9016] lr^JdmZwdmM &

[GITA:9018] Ag§e`§ g_J«§ _m§ `Wm kmñ`{g VÀN>¥Uw Ÿ&& 1 Ÿ&&
[GITA:9019] The Lord said:  O Partha! With your mind fully absorbed in  Me,
[GITA:9020] seeking refuge in Me, meditate on Me.  Listen to Me to understand the way
[GITA:9021] (yoga) you can extensively know Me, dispelling all the doubts. (7.1)
[GITA:9022] Comments: The Lord starts His sermon to Arjuna about His
[GITA:9023] attributes. To understand these, seekers would require th eir mind s to be
[GITA:9024] completely focused on the Lord with firm conviction that the Lord is the
[GITA:9025] protector and shelter for all. The Lord uses the adjectives asamshayam
[GITA:9026] (without doubt) and samagram (complete) in this verse. Sri Madhwacharya
[GITA:9027] in his GB  clarifies that these words cannot be interpreted to conclude that
[GITA:9028] one can completely understand the Lord. Rather they refer to the
[GITA:9029] knowledge that a seeker can acquire, meaning that by listening to the
[GITA:9030] Lord’s teachings attentively, a seeker can understand the Lord’s attr ibutes
[GITA:9031] to the maximum extent (based on the seeker’s abilities). Even deities such
[GITA:9032] as Rudra, Brahma etc., cannot completely comprehend the Lord’s attributes
[GITA:9033] which are infinite.

[GITA:9037] I will impart  to you in full  the spiritual knowledge  (indirect
[GITA:9038] knowledge – paroksha jnana) and wisdom (direct knowledge  – aparoksha
[GITA:9039] jnana) about Me knowing which there will be nothing else to know. (7.2)
[GITA:9040] Comments: The Lord states the two types of knowle dge that He
[GITA:9041] would be imparting. Jnana refers to ordinary or indirect knowledge
[GITA:9042] (paroksha jnana ) which one normally acquires through studies of
[GITA:9043] scriptures, learning from teachers etc. Vijnana = vishesha jnana  refers to
[GITA:9055] 188                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:9056] specialized knowledge which refers to the direct knowledge ( aparoksha
[GITA:9057] jnana) that one would acquire after having been blessed with a vision of the
[GITA:9058] Lord.

[GITA:9115] inert nature and all living beings is Mother  Nature (Goddess Mahalakshmi)

[GITA:9148] 190                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita

[GITA:9153] common for many to refer to a kingdom by the name of its king. This is
[GITA:9154] done in the context of a king who has full control over his kingdom.
[GITA:9156] The Lord is Supreme
[GITA:9158] _Îm… naVa§ ZmÝ`V² {H${#mXpñV YZ§O` Ÿ&
[GITA:9159] _{` gd©{_X§ àmoV§ gyÌo _{UJUm Bd Ÿ&& 7 &&
[GITA:9161] O Dhananjaya! There is no entity in this universe that is superior to
[GITA:9162] Me (Lord Krishna). Everything in the universe is supported by Me, just like
[GITA:9163] a garland of pearls is supported by a string. (7.7)
[GITA:9165] Comments: This verse is one of the most quoted verses in the Gita
[GITA:9166] as it emphatically captures the Lord’s declaration that He is the Supreme
[GITA:9167] One, and everything and everyone in the universe are under His control – in
[GITA:9168] other words, the principle of Vishnu’s Supremacy ( Vishnu Sarvottamatva).
[GITA:9169] When the Lord indicates  that everythin g in the universe act s under His
[GITA:9170] control and He is responsible for the universe’s creation and dissolution, He
[GITA:9171] clarifies that there is no one superior to Him and He is also responsible for
[GITA:9172] the sustenance of the universe. Any confusion that some may have th at
[GITA:9173] perhaps Maya (or illusion) covers even the Lord, is categorically dispelled
[GITA:9174] here.
[GITA:9176] It is interesting to note the simile of a bunch of pearls supported by a
[GITA:9177] string is used here to describe the Lord supporting the universe. While one
[GITA:9178] can see pearls worn by someone, the string is not visible. But if the string
[GITA:9179] were to snap, the pearls will not hold together. Similarly, while the Lord
[GITA:9180] supports the universe, one cannot see Him. He indeed works in mysterious
[GITA:9181] ways.
[GITA:9193] Chapter 7                                                                                                                                             191
[GITA:9195] Author’s Note: This is also an interesting v erse from the perspective
[GITA:9196] of numerology. Number 7 is considered very auspicious, and Gita has 700
[GITA:9197] verses. The fact that the Lord’s supremacy is demonstrated in the 7 th verse
[GITA:9198] of the 7th chapter is worth noting.

[GITA:9203] O Son of Kunti! I am the sweetness in water. I am the radiance in the
[GITA:9204] Sun and the Moon. I am the primordial syllable Om in the Vedas. I am the
[GITA:9205] sound in space. I am virility in humans. (7.8)
[GITA:9207] Comments: In verse 7.2 , the Lord resolved to teach Arjuna both
[GITA:9208] indirect (ordinary) knowledge ( jnana) and direct (special, divine)
[GITA:9209] knowledge (vijnana). Some aspects of indirect knowledge were covered in
[GITA:9210] verses 7.4 – 7.7. In the next few verses, the Lord provides more specialized
[GITA:9211] details about His attributes and glories which form specialized knowledge
[GITA:9212] (vijnana). In verses 7.4 – 7.7, the Lord states that everything and everyone
[GITA:9213] in the universe act under His ownership and control. In the next few verses,
[GITA:9214] He provides more details ab out the meaning of ownership. The basic
[GITA:9215] elements of nature such as water, fire etc., are under His control , and in
[GITA:9216] addition, the Lord owns and powers the essence in these elements. The
[GITA:9217] Lord provides the character of sweetness to water; hence He is known as
[GITA:9218] sweetness. Likewise, He powers the radiance in the Sun and the Moon. He
[GITA:9219] is also known as Om, the primordial syllable which is the root for all Vedic
[GITA:9220] literature. The syllable Om is made up of 3 letters; a, u, and ma, and these
[GITA:9221] gave rise to the triumvirate in the holy hymn, Gayatri which in turn gave
[GITA:9222] rise to the 3 parts of the Purusha Sookta hymns from the Vedas, from
[GITA:9223] which arose  Vedic literature. The Lord also empowers virility in humans.

[GITA:9240] I am the fragrance on earth. I am the brilliance in fire. I am the life in

[GITA:9256] Know that I am the  eternal seed and the root cause for the existence
[GITA:9257] of all beings. Intelligence in the intelligent is due to Me. Strength in the
[GITA:9258] powerful is due to Me (The Lord is the root cause not only of  all beings but
[GITA:9259] also of their strength and qualities). (7.10)
[GITA:9261] Comments: The Lord has stated previously that all objects in the
[GITA:9262] universe such as the five basic elements of nature, the Sun, the Moon etc.,
[GITA:9263] are all under His control. In addition, He has separately clarified in verses
[GITA:9264] 7.8 onwards, that not only are all objects under His control, their innate
[GITA:9265] attributes (such as sweetness in water, radiance/energy in fire) are also due
[GITA:9266] to Him alone. A tailor de signs a dress using basic materials such as cloth,
[GITA:9267] thread etc., and the finished dress has all characteristics of its ingredients
[GITA:9268] such as softness, strength etc. The tailor gets the credit for creating the
[GITA:9269] dress, but he ha s no role in the presence of the i nnate qualities of the
[GITA:9270] ingredients. The Lord is not like the tailor in this example. He not only is
[GITA:9271] responsible for the creation of   objects but is also responsible for the innate
[GITA:9272] qualities in those objects. These aspects form part of vijnana, which is
[GITA:9273] specialized knowledge about the Lord’s greatness. A seeker needs to
[GITA:9285] Chapter 7                                                                                                                                             193
[GITA:9287] understand this, and only then will he be able to develop trust and faith in
[GITA:9288] worshipping the Lord. Sri Rayaru in GV  also interprets this verse to
[GITA:9289] indicate that even deities who govern the in trinsic attributes of objects are
[GITA:9290] under the Lord’s control.

[GITA:9337] Ignorance – Causes, Effect, and Solution
[GITA:9339] {Ì{^Jw©U_`¡^m©d¡ao{^… gd©{_X§ OJV² Ÿ&
[GITA:9340] _mo{hV§ Zm{^OmZm{V _m_oä`… na_ì``_² Ÿ&& 13Ÿ&&
[GITA:9342] Deluded by the influence of the three qualities of nature, the world
[GITA:9343] fails to recognize Me as the supreme ( param) and immutable ( avyayam)
[GITA:9344] being. (7.13)
[GITA:9346] Comments:  How can the world made up of the three qualities come
[GITA:9347] under delusion and not realize the Lord as being beyond the three qualities?
[GITA:9348] Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that people look at other people in the world
[GITA:9349] whose physical bodies are made up of the three qualities. They conclude
[GITA:9350] that similarly, the Lord’s body could also be made up of these three
[GITA:9351] qualities. However, learned ones understand that the Lord’s body i s
[GITA:9352] transcendental in nature and is not subject to birth or decay or destruct ion.
[GITA:9353] The Lord who has limitless auspicious attributes is beyond the three
[GITA:9354] qualities of nature. This concept is also part of vijnana (specialized
[GITA:9355] knowledge about the Lord).
[GITA:9357] While the Lord, during His incarnation in this world as Rama or
[GITA:9358] Krishna, looks and acts like any other human being, from time to time He
[GITA:9359] also demonstrates extraordinary powers (far and beyond any human’s
[GITA:9360] capacity) which are described in epics such as the Mahabharata. Hence, a
[GITA:9361] seeker will be able to understand the Lord’s superiority by hearing about
[GITA:9362] His glories.

[GITA:9479] This verse uses the phrase ‘atma eva’ when describing learned ones.
[GITA:9480] Some philosophers interpret ‘ atma eva ’ to mean ‘My own form’ quoting
[GITA:9481] the text ‘ nama roopevihaya ’ from the Atharva Upanishat  (6.8) in
[GITA:9482] reference to rivers merging in an ocean and apparently losing their identity.
[GITA:9483] Sri Vidyasagara Madhava Te ertha quotes Sri Madhwacharya’s
[GITA:9484] interpretation of  this Upanishat and points out that the proper word
[GITA:9485] derivation of the above text is ‘ nama roope Savihaya’ = nama roope
[GITA:9486] avihaya, which indicates that rivers maintain their identity even when they
[GITA:9487] merge with the ocean. The proper interpretation of the phrase ‘atma eva’ is
[GITA:9488] that learned ones are extremely dear to the Lord.

[GITA:9664] The word yogamaya is interpreted as ‘ yoga sahita maya’ , where

[GITA:9666] Durga. As per Sri Madhwacharya [GB] , Sri Jaya  Teertha [PD], and Sri
[GITA:9667] Rayaru [GV], yoga can be interpreted to mean either upaya (means or
[GITA:9668] instrument) or strength ( shakti). However, in this verse, the interpretation
[GITA:9669] of yoga as strength is correct as maya already represents the instrument
[GITA:9670] (upaya) of strength. This interpretation is also supported by Padma
[GITA:9671] Purana.

[GITA:9797] Summary of Chapter 7
[GITA:9799] The first 6 chapters were broadly concerned with descriptions o f the
[GITA:9800] methods and procedures ( both external and internal) that a seeker would
[GITA:9801] need to perform to be able to acquire divine, spiritual knowledge. The next
[GITA:9802] 6 chapters describe in more detail such divine, spiritual knowledge about
[GITA:9803] the Lord, which forms the principal message of the Gita. In earlier chapters
[GITA:9804] 2 – 6, there were some discussions on the Lord’s attributes which were
[GITA:9805] included contextually, and the next 6 chapters provide more  exclusive
[GITA:9806] details about the Lord’ attributes. Chapter 7 provides a detailed discussion
[GITA:9807] of the two types of learning – knowledge and wisdom. Ordinary knowledge
[GITA:9808] (jnana) is that knowledge that is gained from scriptural studies and through
[GITA:9809] teachers. Wisdom or d irect knowledge ( vijnana) is specialized knowledge
[GITA:9810] about the Lord Almighty that one can attain aft er self-realization. In verses
[GITA:9811] 7.4 - 7.6, the components of the eight -fold nature in the univ erse are
[GITA:9812] identified. In verses 7.7  - 7.11, the Lord describes His ownership of
[GITA:9813] everything in the universe and stresses that He is responsible for even the
[GITA:9814] intrinsic attri butes of objects. The cause of ignorance, the influence of
[GITA:9815] delusion on living beings , and procedure to overcome delusio n are also
[GITA:9816] discussed in verses 7.13 – 7.14. The various types of seekers who are
[GITA:9817] devoted to the Lord are identified in verses 7.16 – 7.19 as those in sickness,
[GITA:9818] those seeking spiritual knowledge, those seeking riches, and those who
[GITA:9819] have already acquired divine, spiritual knowledge . Among these four types
[GITA:9820] of devotees, the Lord is fond of the last type who worship Him without any
[GITA:9821] expectations. Verses 7.20 – 7.23 deal with worshippers of other deities in
[GITA:9822] comparison with those who are exclusively devoted to the Lord Almighty.
[GITA:9823] Those who only worship other deities may receive temporary fruits and
[GITA:9835] Chapter 7                                                                                                                                             205
[GITA:9837] those who exclusively worship the Lord Almighty ultimately attain
[GITA:9838] everlasting bliss. In verses 7.24 - 7.26, the issue of false knowledge is
[GITA:9839] described. In verse 7.28 , the Lord exhorts the virtuous to overcome false
[GITA:9840] knowledge and worship Him with conviction. The chapter ends with a
[GITA:9841] message from the Lord in ve rses 7.29 – 7.30 about the thoughts that a
[GITA:9842] seeker should focus on at the time of leaving this world. These last two
[GITA:9843] verses act as a bridge to the next chapter where the concepts introduced
[GITA:9844] here are dealt with in detail.

[GITA:9859] 206                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:9860] Aï>_mo@Úm`… - Aja~«÷`moJ…
[GITA:9861] Chapter 8 - The Imperishable Lord
[GITA:9863] Chapter Introduction: This chapter, titled Akshara Brahma Yoga ,
[GITA:9864] the path of  the imperishable Lord , comprising 28 verses , shows the sure
[GITA:9865] path to reach the Lord through concentrated meditatio n and single pointed
[GITA:9866] devotion. The previous chapter covered the issues of  indirect knowledge
[GITA:9867] and direct knowledge as they relate to  the Lord. Towards the  end of the
[GITA:9868] chapter, in verses 7.29 and 7.30 , the Lord introduced some special topics
[GITA:9869] such as Adhibhoota, Adhidaiva, Adhiyajna, etc. This terminology was used
[GITA:9870] for the first time , and Arjuna naturally has questions about its  context and
[GITA:9871] meaning. The Lord answers Arjuna’s questions, and much of the chapter is
[GITA:9872] devoted to the act of remembering the Lord during one’s final moments and
[GITA:9873] one’s journey hereafter.

[GITA:9884] Arjuna said, “O Purushottama (The Supreme One)! ” Who is Brahma

[GITA:9911] Brahma, Karma, Adhibhoota, Adhidaiva, Adhyatma, Adhiyajna
[GITA:9913] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&

[GITA:9917] The Lord said: Brahma refers to the imperishable Lord who pervades
[GITA:9918] everything and everyone. Adhyatma refers to the material equipment  that
[GITA:9919] allows a soul to act (body, sens e organs, conscience). Karma refers to the
[GITA:9920] Lord’s act of creation, which is responsible for the birth and e xistence of all
[GITA:9921] living beings. 8.3
[GITA:9923] Comments: The Lord responds to each of Arjuna’s eight questions.
[GITA:9925]  Brahma refers to the imperishable Lord Almighty . The adjective
[GITA:9926] param (meaning supreme) is used here to denote the Lord Almighty ,
[GITA:9927] as there are other imperishable (akshara) entities also in the universe
[GITA:9928] such as inert nature, the letters, the Vedas, etc. (verse 2.17)  which
[GITA:9929] are dependent on the Lord
[GITA:9930]  Adhyatma (prime self) refers to material equipment that helps a soul
[GITA:9931] function in this world: the physical body, sense organs, and
[GITA:9932] conscience (which the Lord grants according to a soul’s svabhāva or
[GITA:9933] innate nature).
[GITA:9934]  Karma (Fruitive Action) refers to visarga, the special activity of
[GITA:9935] creating the universe performed by the Lord Almighty.
[GITA:9937] A{Y^yV§ jamo ^md… nwéfüm{YX¡dV_² Ÿ&

[GITA:9951] O Arjuna! The five b asic elements of material nature (earth, fire,
[GITA:9952] water, space, and wind) form Adhibhoota. Superior deities who reside
[GITA:9953] inside and govern the physical bodies of living beings (namely Sesha, the
[GITA:9954] serpent deity, and the four faced deity Brahma) form Adhidaiva. Powering
[GITA:9955] all living bein gs and the consumer of offerings in all sacrifices is I, going
[GITA:9956] by the name of Adhiyajna (Lord of Sacrifice). (8.4)
[GITA:9958] Comments: The Lord continues to answer Arjuna’s remaining questions:
[GITA:9960]  Adhibhoota (Prime Nature) refers to the five basic elements of
[GITA:9961] nature, (fire, water, earth, space, and wind) that comprise one ’s
[GITA:9962] physical body.
[GITA:9963]  Adhidaiva (prime deities) refers to superior deities such as Sesha and
[GITA:9964] four-faced Brahma that reside in the bodies of living beings.
[GITA:9965]  Adhiyajna (Lord of Sacrifice) refers to Me (Lord Krishna).
[GITA:9966]  The Lord is termed Adhiyajna as He activates and po wers one to
[GITA:9967] perform sacrifices , and He is also the consumer of the essence of
[GITA:9968] such sacrifices, as was stated previously (verse 5.29).
[GITA:9970] Sri Rayaru in GV  provides additional interpretations for some of these
[GITA:9971] entities based on Sri Madhwacharya’s GB as follows: Adhyatma also refers
[GITA:9972] to the Lord’s form (as He has the prime or supreme form), Adhidaiva also
[GITA:9973] refers to Goddess Mahalakshmi (as she is the foremost among all deities),
[GITA:9974] and Adhibhoota refers to all living beings (as living beings are superior to
[GITA:9975] inert objects).

[GITA:9998] One who thinks of Me (Kris hna) at the time of leavin g one’s body

[GITA:10001] O son of Kunti! Whatever entity one think s of at the time of leaving
[GITA:10002] one’s body, one will attain the same entity (due to the force of habit). (8.6)
[GITA:10004] Comments: The Lord answers Arjuna’s eight h question by stating
[GITA:10005] that learned seekers remember the Lord at the time of leaving  the body
[GITA:10006] which results in their  attaining the Lord, which is a state of permanent,
[GITA:10007] exalted happiness dev oid of any misery. How does one  who is focused on
[GITA:10008] the Lord at t he ti me of departing this world  reach the Lord? Whatever
[GITA:10009] entity one is thinking of during the last moments, the person will attain that
[GITA:10010] entity in the succeeding births. The story of King Bharata in the Bhagavata
[GITA:10011] Purana illustrates this. Bharata once rescued a d eer strugg ling in flood
[GITA:10012] waters and nursed it back to health. He developed a strong attachment to it
[GITA:10013] and was thinking of it even at the last moments of his life. This resulted in
[GITA:10014] him being born as a deer.
[GITA:10016] It should be noted that the verse says, anta kala , meaning the final
[GITA:10017] moments. It does not say the  final instant. This is because  everyone, at the
[GITA:10018] exact final instant of the soul leaving the body , feels relief. However, it is
[GITA:10019] only the learned  devotees of the Lord who  remember Him in the moments
[GITA:10020] leading up to death.
[GITA:10022] Sri Madhwacharya in his Bhagavata Tatparya Nirnaya  [BTN]
[GITA:10023] commentary on the epic Bhagavata Maha Purana  [BMP] (10.1.42)
[GITA:10024] quotes the Naradeeya Purana  and states that one ’s innate eligibility and
[GITA:10025] the Lord’s will are the deci ding factors in determinin g one’s next birth (in
[GITA:10026] addition to ones final thoughts). Thus, one who is thinking of angels during
[GITA:10027] the last moments may not be born as an angel but may be born in the
[GITA:10028] vicinity of angels.

[GITA:10197] hymn, the Purusha Sookta, from which all Vedic literature emerged. Later

[GITA:10279] Those who know that the Lord’s day spans over multitudes of yugas

[GITA:10283] Comments: In this verse, the Lord introduces the concept of day and
[GITA:10284] night in relation to His acts of creation and dissolution of the universe. Sri
[GITA:10285] Rayaru in GV states that the word sahasra used in this verse should not be
[GITA:10286] construed to literally mean thousands, but to uncountable multitudes (as no
[GITA:10287] one can count the Lord’s time). The duration of creation and dissolution of
[GITA:10288] the universe  are symbolically indicated as daytime and night-time for the
[GITA:10289] Lord Almighty, as His time cannot be measured.
[GITA:10291] Sri Satyadhyana Teertha in his GPC states that the yuga referred here
[GITA:10292] indicates one hundred years of deity Brahma, whose one year is made up of
[GITA:10293] 360 days, with each day equating to 864 crore (8.64 billion) human years.

[GITA:10342] The unmanifest entity, which is vastly different  and superior to the

[GITA:10351] Comments: Since the previous verses described the concepts of day
[GITA:10352] and night for the Lord to represent the times of creation and dissolution of
[GITA:10353] the universe, one may question if the Lord is also subject to birth and
[GITA:10365] Chapter 8                                                                                                                                          217
[GITA:10367] decay. Verse 8.20  clarifies that the Lord , who is responsible for creation
[GITA:10368] and dissolution , is eternal, has no beginning or end , and is imperishable.
[GITA:10369] Verse 8.21  clarifies that He goes by the name of Akshara (one without
[GITA:10370] decay), because of His imperishable nature . This verse also states that one
[GITA:10371] who reaches the Lord’s abode will never return to the earth.
[GITA:10373] Verse 8.20  uses the terms para and anya meaning supreme and
[GITA:10374] different, respectively, indicating that the Lord Almighty is superior to and
[GITA:10375] different from all other entities i n the universe, such as individual souls and
[GITA:10376] inert objects. This concept i s further emphasised later in C hapter 15 (verses
[GITA:10377] 16-20) and validates the  philosophy of dualism  propagated by Sri

[GITA:10380] Devotion is the Superior Path

[GITA:10385] O Partha! The Supreme One is reachable only through pure,
[GITA:10386] exclusive devotion. Such a Lord is resident in all beings and pervades the
[GITA:10387] entire universe. (8.22)
[GITA:10389] Comments: In verse 8.10, it i s stated that devotion, meditation, and
[GITA:10390] detachment are all required for one to reach the Lord. As per Sri Rayaru
[GITA:10391] [GV], this verse clarifies that devotion to the Lord is the preeminent path.
[GITA:10393] Returning and Non-returning Paths
[GITA:10395] `Ì H$mbo ËdZmd¥{Îm_² Amd¥qÎm M¡d `mo{JZ… Ÿ&

[GITA:10411] 218                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:10412] Yy_mo am{ÌñVWm H¥$îU… fÊ_mgm X{jUm`Z_² Ÿ&

[GITA:10418] O Arjuna, superior among the Bharatas! I will now teach you about
[GITA:10419] the paths taken by seekers , from which they will either return to this world
[GITA:10420] or not return to this world. The paths are identifie d by the ir respective
[GITA:10421] governing deities. (8.23)
[GITA:10423] Eligible seekers, leaving this world through the path s of deities
[GITA:10424] governing fire, light, daytime, the fortnight of  the waxing moon, and the
[GITA:10425] first half of a lunar year, will reach the abode of the Lord and not return to
[GITA:10426] this world. (8.24)
[GITA:10428] Other seekers leaving this world through the path of deities
[GITA:10429] governing smoke, nighttime, the fortnight of the waning moon, and  the
[GITA:10430] second half of a lunar year will reach the land of the Moon deity and will
[GITA:10431] return to this world again. (8.25)
[GITA:10433] These two paths are permanent and are termed the Shukla path and
[GITA:10434] the Krishna path. Those leaving through the first path will not return , and
[GITA:10435] those leaving through the second path will return to this world. (8.26)
[GITA:10437] Comments: These three v erses describe the paths taken by a soul
[GITA:10438] after leaving the physical body. The soul progressively traverse s the worlds
[GITA:10439] governed by various deities. Some seekers leave this world and traverse the
[GITA:10440] worlds governed by the following deities : Agni/Archi (fire), Aha (daytime),
[GITA:10441] Shukla Paksha (fortnight of waxing moon), and uttarayana (first half of a
[GITA:10442] lunar new year). These seekers , who predominantly take the path of
[GITA:10443] knowledge ( jnana yogis ), will ultimately reach the abode of the Lord
[GITA:10444] Almighty and never return to the  earth. Other seekers leave this world and
[GITA:10445] traverse the worlds gov erned by the following deities:  dhooma (smoke),
[GITA:10457] Chapter 8                                                                                                                                          219
[GITA:10459] ratri (nighttime), krishna paksha  (fortnight of the waning moon) and
[GITA:10460] dakshinayana (second half of a lunar new year). These seekers, who are
[GITA:10461] focused on the path of action (karma yogis) with the expectation of rewards
[GITA:10462] will return to this earth.
[GITA:10464] Some commentators adopt the literal translation of the times and
[GITA:10465] periods indicated in these verses and wrongly conclude that the destination
[GITA:10466] of a soul dep ends on the time, day, fortnight, and month of lea ving this
[GITA:10467] world. Sri Rayaru in GV, based on Sri Madhwacharya’s GB,  clarifies that
[GITA:10468] the reference to the time periods indicated in these verses should be
[GITA:10469] interpreted to mean the respective governing deities. After all, time is inert.
[GITA:10470] How can time determine the destination of a soul? Also, not all entities
[GITA:10471] identified in these verses are related to time ( kala). For example,
[GITA:10472] agni/archi, and dhooma are not related to time. Hence , the entities
[GITA:10473] described in these ve rses can only be interpreted to mean their respective
[GITA:10474] governing deities. Furt her, as per Sri Madhwacharya’s GB , in the Padma
[GITA:10475] Purana it is clarified that an aparoksha jnani (a seeker with direct, divine
[GITA:10476] knowledge of the Lord) will achieve li beration regardless of the time, day,
[GITA:10477] fortnight, month of leaving this world.
[GITA:10479] In the Mahabharata, it i s stated that Bheeshma waited  until the
[GITA:10480] onset of uttarayana (the first half of the lunar year) to leave this world.
[GITA:10481] Does this not imply the superiority of one period ove r the other? It is
[GITA:10482] clarified by Sri Jaya  Teertha in [ND] that among those who attain
[GITA:10483] liberation, the ones who leave their body during the period of uttarayana
[GITA:10484] experience higher bliss. One must remember that Bheeshma was an iccha
[GITA:10485] marani and had the power to decide the time of his exit from th e world. His
[GITA:10486] situation cannot be generalized.
[GITA:10488] In summary, a soul’s destination after leaving t he physical body is
[GITA:10489] based on its efforts and performance during its  soul’s lifetime in this world
[GITA:10490] and the acquisition of divi ne, spiritual knowledge , including knowledge
[GITA:10491] about the paths taken hereafter. The destination is not determined by the
[GITA:10503] 220                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:10504] time of the soul leaving the body. Sri  Rayaru also clarifies this in GV,
[GITA:10505] quoting the Brahma Sutra (4.2.22).

[GITA:10515] O Partha! A se eker who properly understands these two paths and
[GITA:10516] acts accordingly will never be deluded. O Arjuna, hence, always practis e
[GITA:10517] the prescribed activities to reach the Lord. (8.27)
[GITA:10519] One who understands these principles will accrue more benefits
[GITA:10520] compared to accru als from studying the Vedas, performing sacrifices, and
[GITA:10521] donating to others. Moreover, such a seeker will indeed reach the Lord’s

[GITA:10524] Comments: These two verses conclude the teachings in this chapter.
[GITA:10525] Lord Krishna instructs Arjuna to understand thoroughly the process of a

[GITA:10528] duty of waging the just war with proper conviction in the concepts
[GITA:10529] described in this chapter. Further, such knowledge about the paths taken by
[GITA:10530] a soul result s in one earn ing much more benefit than that  available from

[GITA:10534] Summary of Chapter 8
[GITA:10536] Chapter 7 covered the issues of knowledge and wisdom as they relate
[GITA:10537] to the Lord. Towards the end of that chapter, in verses 7.29 and 7.30 , the
[GITA:10549] Chapter 8                                                                                                                                          221
[GITA:10551] Lord introduced some special topics such as Adhibhoota, Adhid aiva,
[GITA:10552] Adhiyajna, etc. This terminology was used for the first time , and Arjuna
[GITA:10553] naturally had questions about their  context and meaning. The Lord answers
[GITA:10554] Arjuna’s questions, and much of the chapter is devoted to the act of
[GITA:10555] remembering the Lord dur ing one’s final moments and one ’s journey
[GITA:10556] hereafter. Arjuna asks eight questions in verses 8.1 and 8.2  and the Lord
[GITA:10557] answers them in verses 8.3 - 8.5. Brahma refers to the imperishable Lord.
[GITA:10558] Adhyatma refers to material equipment  that allow s a soul to act (body,
[GITA:10559] sense organs, conscience). Karma refers to the Lord’s act of creation ,
[GITA:10560] which is responsible for the birth and existence of all living beings. Basic
[GITA:10561] elements of material nature such as earth and fire form  ‘Adhibhoota’.
[GITA:10562] Superior deities who reside inside and gove rn the physical bodies of living
[GITA:10563] beings (namely Sesha, the serpent deity , and the four -faced deity Brahma)
[GITA:10564] form Adhidaiva. Powering all living beings and the consumer of offerings
[GITA:10565] in all sacrifices is the Lord, going by the name of  Adhiyajna (Lord of
[GITA:10566] Sacrifice). The Lord answers Arjuna’s eighth question by stating that
[GITA:10567] learned seekers remember the Lord at the time of leaving their bodies,
[GITA:10568] which results in their  attaining Him. In verses 8.6  - 8.14, the Lord teaches
[GITA:10569] the need for one to remember Him during the  final moments and the
[GITA:10570] procedure to do the same. Verses 8.15 - 8.16 state that those who remember
[GITA:10571] the Lord properly during their final moments will not return to earth. The
[GITA:10572] concept of the Lord Almighty’s day and night and their relationship to His
[GITA:10573] acts of creation and dissolution of the universe are addressed in verses
[GITA:10574] 8.17-8.20. The Lord declares in verse 8.22 that the path of devotion is
[GITA:10575] supreme among all paths available to reach the Lord. The paths taken by a
[GITA:10576] soul after leaving the physical body are described in verses 8.23 - 8.26. The
[GITA:10577] chapter is concluded in verses 8.27 and  8.28 with the Lord instructing
[GITA:10578] Arjuna to focus on his prescribed duty of waging the just war while being
[GITA:10579] fully aware of the key concepts covered in this chapter . These include the
[GITA:10580] knowledge of paths traversed by a soul after leaving the physical body ,
[GITA:10581] with the ultimate destination being the Lord’s abode.

[GITA:10599] Chapter 9 – Path of Supreme Knowledge and Secrets
[GITA:10601] Chapter Introduction: This chapter, titled the ‘Path of Supreme
[GITA:10602] Knowledge and Secrets’ comprises 34 verses. The central message here is
[GITA:10603] an assurance to all seekers that they will have their desires fulfilled through
[GITA:10604] devoted worship and meditation on the Lord. Th e wise seek the Lord
[GITA:10605] through such devotion and worship, while the ignorant seek limited
[GITA:10606] material and mundane gains , and never lead a fulfilled life. This chapter is
[GITA:10607] a continuation of the concepts in Chapter 7 where some important attributes
[GITA:10608] of the Lord wer e revealed. Towards the end of Chapter 7, the Lord
[GITA:10609] introduces some new concepts such as Adhyatma, Adhibhoota, Adhidaiva,
[GITA:10610] Adhiyajna etc. Arjuna’s questions about these concepts were answered in
[GITA:10611] Chapter 8. Now, the Lord continues the discussion from Chapter 7. In that
[GITA:10612] sense, Chapters 7, 8 and 9 are in proper sequence. While the Lord has
[GITA:10613] infinite auspicious forms, attributes, activities etc., there are eight activities
[GITA:10614] of the Lord Almighty that directly impact living beings. They are – creation
[GITA:10615] (Srishti), sust enance ( Stithi), dissolution ( laya), regulation ( niyamana),
[GITA:10616] knowledge ( jnana), ignorance ( ajnana), bondage ( bandha) and liberation
[GITA:10617] (moksha). Together they are called Janmadi ashtaka  and they are also
[GITA:10618] covered in this chapter. This chapter is called  the Path  of Supreme
[GITA:10619] Knowledge (‘Raja Vidya Yoga ’) as it teaches these particularly important
[GITA:10620] concepts about the Lord. It is also called  the Path of supreme secrets (‘Raja
[GITA:10621] Guhya Yoga’) meant only for the faithful.
[GITA:10623] The Lord’s Greatness

[GITA:10649] The Lord said: I will now impart most confidential principles to you,
[GITA:10650] as you are devoid of faults such as envy and are eligible to receive this
[GITA:10651] teaching. Gaining this sacred and special knowledge along with knowledge
[GITA:10652] from the scriptures will free you from evil. (9.1)
[GITA:10654] It is the cro wn of knowledge. It is the pinnacle of secrets. It is
[GITA:10655] purifying. It is superior. It is the means to learn about the Lord Almighty
[GITA:10656] who powers everyone’s sense organs. It is easy to follow, and it is the path
[GITA:10657] for eternal bliss. (9.2)
[GITA:10659] O Parantapa! Those who do not have faith in the knowledge that
[GITA:10660] teaches about the Lord Almighty will not reach the Lord and will keep
[GITA:10661] returning to this mortal worldly life. (9.3)
[GITA:10663] Comments: The Lord starts His sermon by stating that He will be
[GITA:10664] teaching particularly, important and very confidential concepts here. This is
[GITA:10665] to draw the attention of seekers and to generate curiosity in them. Only
[GITA:10666] those who are pure and are devoid of negative attributes such as envy are
[GITA:10667] eligible and able to understand these teachings. The Lord resolves to teach
[GITA:10668] Arjuna both general knowledge that would be available from scriptures
[GITA:10669] (jnana) and special, divine knowledge ( vijnana) which is not easily
[GITA:10670] available. Only those who are sincere in their devotion to the Lord can
[GITA:10671] imbibe such special knowledge, hence it is most secretive.
[GITA:10673] The Lord imparts this knowledge over the nex t 16 verses. In 12
[GITA:10674] verses from 9.4 – 9.15, general knowledge ( jnana) that would be available
[GITA:10675] from scriptures is taught. The next 4 verses 9.16 – 9.19, contain discussion
[GITA:10676] on special, divine knowledge (vijnana).

[GITA:10689] The Omnipresent, Indwelling Lord
[GITA:10691] _`m VV{_X§ gdª OJXì`º$_y{V©Zm Ÿ&
[GITA:10692] _ËñWm{Z gd©^yVm{Z Z Mmh§ VoîddpñWV… Ÿ&& 4 Ÿ&&
[GITA:10694] Z M _ËñWm{Z ^yVm{Z ní` _o `moJ_¡œa_² Ÿ&
[GITA:10695] ^yV^¥Þ M ^yVñWmo __mË_m ^yV^mdZ… Ÿ&& 5 Ÿ&&
[GITA:10697] `Wm@@H$mepñWVmo {ZË`§ dm`w… gd©ÌJmo _hmZ² Ÿ&
[GITA:10698] VWm gdm©{U ^yVm{Z _ËñWmZrË`wnYma` Ÿ&& 6 &&
[GITA:10700] Everything in this universe is pervaded by My unmanifest form
[GITA:10701] which cannot be seen. All inert objects and sentient beings are supported by
[GITA:10702] Me. But I am not dependent on anyone for support. (9.4)
[GITA:10704] Everything in the universe, including sentient beings and inert
[GITA:10705] objects, even though  anchored in Me (Krishna), cannot perceive Me
[GITA:10706] through sense organs . Look at My infinit e, divine powers . Even though
[GITA:10707] they are anchored in Me, I do not depend on them. (9.5)
[GITA:10709] The majestic wind blowing in space is not impacted by the attributes
[GITA:10710] of entities that it encounters. Similarly, even though every living being is
[GITA:10711] anchored in Me, there is no mutual superimposition of attributes. (9.6)
[GITA:10713] Comments: These three verses provide details  on the concept of the
[GITA:10714] Lord’s manifestation in every object in the universe; inert and sentient. The
[GITA:10715] Lord is omnipresent and is the supporter for everything in the universe but
[GITA:10716] Himself needs no support of anyone or anything. If the Lord is pervading
[GITA:10717] everywhere, why is He not seen? Verse 9.4  defines the Lord’s attribute of
[GITA:10718] avyakta (the unmanifest), because of which He is not seen.
[GITA:10720] Anyone standing on the ground experiences the condition of the
[GITA:10721] ground. For example, if the ground is cool or hot due to  the weather, one
[GITA:10733] Chapter 9                                                                                                                                        225
[GITA:10735] standing on it will feel the cold or the heat. This is due to the impact of
[GITA:10736] contact between the object that is supported and the object that is providing
[GITA:10737] the support. So, if the Lord is supporting everything in the universe, why is
[GITA:10738] that support not felt physically by the beings in the unive rse? This is
[GITA:10739] answered in verse 9.5, where it is stated that those who are supported by the
[GITA:10740] Lord cannot perceive Him through their sense organs. This is
[GITA:10741] fundamentally because (unlike the example of the ground ), t he Lord does
[GITA:10742] not have a physical form made up of material nature but has a
[GITA:10743] transcendental form.
[GITA:10745] It must be noted  in verse 9.5,  the Lord uses the term ‘ mama atma ’
[GITA:10746] (my soul) as the entity that pervades and supports everything in t he
[GITA:10747] universe. However, in v erse 9.4, the Lord uses the term ‘ avyakta moorthy’
[GITA:10748] (unmanifest form) as the entity that pervades and supports everything in the
[GITA:10749] universe. How can these be reconciled? Sri Jaya  Teertha in PD  explains
[GITA:10750] that the reason for using different terminology is to con firm that, in the case
[GITA:10751] of the Lord, His form and soul are the same. This is quite different from the
[GITA:10752] case of living beings where the physical form and the soul are different.
[GITA:10754] The concept in verse 9.5 is illustrated through the examp le of a
[GITA:10755] gentle breeze i n verse 9.6 . A gentle, majestic wind blowing in space
[GITA:10756] encounters many objects in its path but does not assume the attributes of
[GITA:10757] those objects. Likewise, even though the Lord pervades everything in the
[GITA:10758] universe and supports everyone in the universe, His att ributes do not get
[GITA:10759] contaminated by entities He encounters. They too  cannot imbibe His
[GITA:10760] attributes onto themselves. Some can question the appropriateness of using
[GITA:10761] the wind as an example. When a gently blowing wind is in the vicinity of a
[GITA:10762] fragrant object (say a flower), one who is nearby can smell the fragrance of
[GITA:10763] the flower carried by the wind. How can one say that the wind is not
[GITA:10764] contaminated b y the fragrance? Sri Rayaru in GV  answers by stating that
[GITA:10765] fragrance does not itself become a quality of the wind. The wind stays
[GITA:10766] independent of the fragrance. The particles that constitute fragrance are
[GITA:10767] carried by the wind but do not become an attribute of the wind. Once the
[GITA:10768] wind travels a sufficient distance, the fragrance is no longer present as
[GITA:10780] 226                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:10781] those particles are di ssipated. This proves that  the wind itself does not take
[GITA:10782] on the attribute of the fragrance. Hence, the example of the wind is
[GITA:10783] appropriate.
[GITA:10785] These verses describe the attribute of Stithi (sustenance) among the
[GITA:10786] eight major attributes of the Lord referred to in the introduction to this
[GITA:10787] chapter.
[GITA:10789] Role of the Lord Almighty During Creation and Dissolution

[GITA:10794] O Son of Kunti! During the grand dissolution of the universe, all
[GITA:10795] sentient and non -sentient entities will merge with the triumvirate of nature
[GITA:10796] (sattva, rajas and tamas attributes) which are under My control. At the start
[GITA:10797] of the next cycle, I will recreate the entities (give them physical forms).
[GITA:10798] (9.7)
[GITA:10799] Comments: After dis cussing His attributes of omnipresence and
[GITA:10800] pervasiveness in verses 9.4 – 9.6, the Lord describes His role in the process
[GITA:10801] of creation ( Srishti) and dissolution ( laya) of the universe  in the next few
[GITA:10802] verses .
[GITA:10804] The Lord uses the term ‘visrujami’ to describe His act of creation of
[GITA:10805] the universe, instead of the usual term ‘srujami’. Sri Rayaru clarifies in GV
[GITA:10806] that ‘visrujami’ refers to special creation while srujami refers to normal
[GITA:10807] creation. This is to indicate the fact that the souls of living beings are
[GITA:10808] eternal and are not subject to creation, and during the time of creation, the
[GITA:10809] Lord gives physical bodies to different souls in different species , based on
[GITA:10810] the nature of those souls.

[GITA:10825] Chapter 9                                                                                                                                        227
[GITA:10828] The triumvirate of nature is always under My control. Using them as
[GITA:10829] the material cause, I keep creating multitudes of entities (sentient and inert)
[GITA:10830] again and again. (9.8)
[GITA:10832] Comments: The previous verse stated the Lord’s activities of
[GITA:10833] creation and dissolution of the universe. In this verse, the Lord states the
[GITA:10834] procedure that He uses for creation. The Lord utilizes the inert nature
[GITA:10835] which is under His control as the material cau se for creation. Sri Rayaru in
[GITA:10836] GV clarifies that the Lord does not need an y entity or utility to perform
[GITA:10837] activities, but He uses inert nature for creation out of His free will.
[GITA:10839] Z M _m§ Vm{Z H$_m©{U {Z~ÜZpÝV YZ§O` Ÿ&

[GITA:10842] O Dhananjaya! These activities such as creation of the universe can
[GITA:10843] never bind Me. Even though I perform these activities, it is as if I never
[GITA:10844] performed them because of My detachment. (9.9)
[GITA:10846] Comments: Anyone performing any activity naturally must face
[GITA:10847] consequences for such activity. Is the Lord also bound by His activities
[GITA:10848] such as creation which results in multitudes of entities being born? This
[GITA:10849] verse answers by stating that the Lord is not bound by His actions. There
[GITA:10850] are two reasons for this . One, the Lord does not perform these actions for
[GITA:10851] any gain but rather to help the i ndividual souls on their spiritual journey .
[GITA:10852] Secondly, the Lord Himself controls all activities ( karma). Therefore,
[GITA:10853] karma can never bind the Lord.
[GITA:10855] Sri Madhwacharya in GB  explains the context for the use of the
[GITA:10856] word udaaseena (meaning indifference) when it  comes to the Lord’s
[GITA:10857] attitude in performing actions such as creation. It is known that one needs
[GITA:10858] the Lord’s grace to receive any benefits from Him . Given this, the Lord
[GITA:10859] must have some interest in such activities. How can He then be indifferent?
[GITA:10860] We can unde rstand this when we see that t he word ‘indifferent’ refers to
[GITA:10872] 228                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:10873] the Lord’s effortless, unattached approach to His activities as He has
[GITA:10874] nothing to gain from them.

[GITA:10879] O Son of Kunti ! Under My supervision, Mother Nature creates the
[GITA:10880] universe made up of sentient and inert objects. Through the mother nature,
[GITA:10881] the universe undergoes the cycle of repeated creation. (9.10)
[GITA:10883] Comments: If the Lord indeed shows indifference in the process of
[GITA:10884] creation of the Universe , as stated in the previous verse, does it mean that
[GITA:10885] the Lord has no interest in or oversight over this activity? This verse
[GITA:10886] counters this question by stating that the process of creation and indeed all
[GITA:10887] His activities occur under His supervision, which is implied by the use of
[GITA:10888] the word adhyaksha. Sri Rayaru explains in GV  that adhyaksha means one
[GITA:10889] who is overseeing or supervising the activity , as aksha means seeing. The
[GITA:10890] process of creation is performed by sentient Mother Nature (Sri Lak shmi)
[GITA:10891] using inert nature , under the supervision and control of the Lord. In
[GITA:10892] summary, while the Lord performs creation using  sentient and insentient
[GITA:10893] nature without effort or attachment, He supervis es and oversee s the
[GITA:10894] process. This verse describes the attrib ute of Niyamana (regulation) among
[GITA:10895] the eight major attributes of the Lord referred to in the introduction to this
[GITA:10896] chapter, as the Lord is seen to be supervising and overseeing the process of
[GITA:10897] creation.

[GITA:10917] Chapter 9                                                                                                                                        229
[GITA:10919] Ignorant fools are unaware that I (Krishna) am the Supreme being,
[GITA:10920] eternal and full of infinite, auspicious attributes. They insult Me by
[GITA:10921] considering Me as having a human like body (subject to decay and death).
[GITA:10922] (9.11)
[GITA:10924] Those with demoniac natures have their intellect clouded with
[GITA:10925] ignorance. Their desires  for heaven will not be realized. Thei r rituals and
[GITA:10926] sacrifices are a wasted effort. They will not attain true spiritual knowledge
[GITA:10927] and they are senseless. (9.12)
[GITA:10929] Comments: while the Lord, who has infinite powers is responsible
[GITA:10930] for the creation, sustenance, and dissolution of the universe and f or
[GITA:10931] granting physical bodies to all souls, why is it that some consider Him the
[GITA:10932] same as other human beings? And why are there no consequences for those
[GITA:10933] who are insulting the ever-compassionate Lord? These two verses provide
[GITA:10934] the answers. Ignorant ones look a t the Lord’s incarnations such as Rama,
[GITA:10935] Vamana, Krishna etc., and assume that the Lord too has a human like body.
[GITA:10936] They are not able to comprehend the Lord’s infinite attributes and strength.
[GITA:10937] The reason for their ignorance is their innate nature , which the Lord
[GITA:10938] describes using the word ‘ prakrutim’ (by nature). Some even have hatred
[GITA:10939] towards the Lord. Such demoniac people will not achieve any lasting
[GITA:10940] rewards or spiritual knowledge , and hence will not be able to perform any
[GITA:10941] activity that would lead to liberation.
[GITA:10943] In the epic [BMP] Bhagavata Maha Purana (7th canto, 7 -1-32),
[GITA:10944] there is a discussion on Shishupala  (the king of Chedi  and a known
[GITA:10945] adversary of Krishna ) who hurled many abuses at the Lord  and was killed
[GITA:10946] by Him. As per BMP, ultimately Shishupala achieves moksha. Some
[GITA:10947] interpret this to mean that even those who constantly hate the Lord are
[GITA:10948] thinking about Him incessantly and hence are eligible for moksha. It is
[GITA:10949] clarified in Sri Madhwacha rya’s [MBTN] verse 21 -259, and BTN  verse
[GITA:10950] 7-1-32, that Shishupala had two separate souls resident in his body. One
[GITA:10951] was the pious soul of Jaya (one of the doorkeepers of the Lord’s abode) and
[GITA:10952] the other was that of a demon. Due to a curse, Jaya had to endure being in
[GITA:10964] 230                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:10965] Shishupala’s body. When Shishupala was killed by Lord Krishna, Jaya
[GITA:10966] attained the Lord, while the demoniac soul was relegated to the eternal hell.

[GITA:11189] Comments: In the next few verses, the Lord explains the difference
[GITA:11190] in rewards experienced by ritualists (those who perform Vedic rituals with
[GITA:11191] the expectation o f specific outcomes), and His unconditional devotees .
[GITA:11192] Later, verse 9. 24 indicates that the Lord consumes the fruits of all rituals
[GITA:11193] whether they are performed by ritualists or unconditional devotees. If that
[GITA:11194] is so, why is there a difference in the final reward? The difference is due to
[GITA:11195] the approach and attitu de in performing such rituals. Ritualists perform
[GITA:11196] Vedic rituals to propitiate other deities with the expectation of rewards such
[GITA:11197] as worldly riches while on earth, heavenly worlds hereafter etc. They do
[GITA:11198] submit all rituals to the Lord Himself, but their acti vities are not without
[GITA:11199] expectation. On the other hand, unconditional devotees of the Lord perform
[GITA:11200] all activities as an offering to the Lord with utmost devotion and without
[GITA:11201] any expectations. The difference in final rewards is due to the difference in
[GITA:11202] their approach. Previously in verse 7.23 , it was indicated that ritualists only
[GITA:11203] experience temporary fruits. These two verses clarify the meaning of
[GITA:11204] temporary fruits by stating that ritualists do reach the heavenly worlds
[GITA:11205] hereafter, enjoy the privileges there a nd after exhaustion of  credits
[GITA:11206] eventually return to earth (in another birth).

[GITA:11298] Comments: As the Lord is supreme and is the eventual object of all

[GITA:11310] Bhagavata, the Lord is seen accepting with pleasure even ordinary

[GITA:11333] dhyana meditation. Offering some fruit refers to the act of performing
[GITA:11334] duties without any expectations o f rewards. Offering water refers to the
[GITA:11335] teary eyes that one experiences because of intense, unconditional prayer to
[GITA:11336] the Lord.

[GITA:11374] side effects from activities performed and will pave the way for liberation.
[GITA:11376] Verse 9.28 describes the attributes of bondage ( bandha) and
[GITA:11377] liberation (moksha) which are part of the eight attributes indicated earlier.

[GITA:11389] The Lord never hates sincere devotees and likewise, He never protects
[GITA:11390] enemies who knowingly hate Him.

[GITA:11418] Comments: The supremacy of devotion is exemplified in these
[GITA:11419] verses. A similar concept was discussed previously in verse 4.36 where it
[GITA:11420] was indicated that right knowledge will absolve even those who are
[GITA:11421] indulging in misdeeds. Here the Lord is clarifying that such people who
[GITA:11422] have conviction in the Lord Almighty’s supremacy over all other deities
[GITA:11423] and indeed over everything in the universe, will soon get back on the right
[GITA:11424] track and achieve His grace. The discussion here applies to pious souls who
[GITA:11425] due to various reasons such as a curse have strayed onto the wrong path.
[GITA:11427] Souls eligible for liberation who have indulged in sinful activities
[GITA:11428] will have to pay for their misdeeds (such as misery in hell) but due to their
[GITA:11429] innate nature will eventually get back to the right path, develop devotion to
[GITA:11430] the Lord and achieve liberation. Sri Rayaru [GV] clarifies that deities and
[GITA:11431] sages who by nature are pious ( sattvic) may also indulge in misdeeds.  This
[GITA:11432] could happen when they have accumulated positive credits ( punya) beyond
[GITA:11433] their eligibility. They would then experience a reduction in such credits by
[GITA:11434] indulging in misdeeds out of compulsion such as a curse . They would
[GITA:11435] however not have to experience he ll as their misdeeds were beyond their
[GITA:11436] control.

[GITA:11510] Summary of Chapter 9
[GITA:11512] While the Lord has infinite auspicious forms, attributes, activities
[GITA:11513] etc., there are eight activities of the Lord that directly impact living beings.
[GITA:11514] These are – creation ( srishti), sustenance ( sthiti), dissolution ( laya),
[GITA:11515] regulation ( niyamana), knowledge ( jnana), ignorance ( ajnana), bondage
[GITA:11516] (bandha), and liberation ( moksha). Together they are called Janmadi
[GITA:11517] ashtaka and they are covered in this chapter. This chapter is called ‘ Raja
[GITA:11518] Vidya Yoga ’ as it teaches these import ant concepts about the Lord. The
[GITA:11519] Lord provides the context for the teachings in  this chapter in verses 9.1,
[GITA:11520] 9.2, and 9.3 where He resolves to imp art both general knowledge (acquired
[GITA:11521] through scriptures  - jnana) and special, divine knowledge about Himself
[GITA:11522] (vijnana). The attribute of sthiti (sustenance) among the eight major
[GITA:11523] attributes of the Lord as they relate to livi ng beings is covered in verses
[GITA:11524] 9.4 – 9.6. In verses 9.7 and 9.8, the Lord’s attributes of creation ( srishti)
[GITA:11525] and dissolution ( laya) are covere d and in 9.10, His attribute of regulation
[GITA:11526] (niyamana) of the universe is discussed. Verse 9.13 describes the attribute
[GITA:11527] of knowledge ( jnana) as it pertains to pious souls , and verses 9.11, 9.12
[GITA:11528] pertain to the attribute of false knowledge ( ajnana) of demoniac souls. In
[GITA:11529] verse 9.1 , the Lord resolved to impart Arjuna both  jnana the general
[GITA:11530] knowledge obtainable through scriptures and very special knowledge about
[GITA:11531] Himself (vijnana). The Lord describes such general knowledge in 12 verses
[GITA:11532] from 9.4 to 9.15 and in four  verses 9.16 to 9.19 , the Lord instructs special,
[GITA:11533] divine knowledge (vijnana) which identifies His presence in all entities, all
[GITA:11534] activities, all sounds and indeed in everything. In verses 9.20 to 9.25, the
[GITA:11535] Lord explains the difference in rewards experienced  by ritualists (those
[GITA:11536] who perform Vedic rituals with expectation s on outcome), and His
[GITA:11548] Chapter 9                                                                                                                                        243
[GITA:11550] unconditional devotees. The supremacy of the path of devotion is described
[GITA:11551] in verses 9.26 – 9.29. Verse 9.28 allude s to the attributes of bondage
[GITA:11552] (bandha) and liberation  (moksha). Verses 9.30 – 9.31 state that even if
[GITA:11553] pious souls indulge in misdeeds (due to some compulsion such as a curse)
[GITA:11554] they will eventually get back to the right path and move towards liberation.
[GITA:11555] In 9.34 the Lord concludes this chapter by instructing Ar juna to focus his
[GITA:11556] mind exclusively on Him, since performing prescribed duties with
[GITA:11557] unconditional devotion will lead one to liberation.
[GITA:11559] >>&& B{V Zd_mo@Ü`m`… &&
[GITA:11560] End of Chapter 9

[GITA:11574] Chapter 10 - Divine Manifestations
[GITA:11576] Chapter Introduc tion: Number ten signifies fullness. It is very
[GITA:11577] fitting that the Lord details His greatness in this tenth chapter  of 42 verses.
[GITA:11578] In the 6 th chapter, the Lord provided details of dhyana meditation, and in
[GITA:11579] the last verse of Chapter 9 the Lord taught that one should concentrate and
[GITA:11580] focus the mind exclusively on Him to achieve everlasting bliss ( moksha).
[GITA:11581] For one to develop such firm conviction in meditation, one needs to be
[GITA:11582] fully aware of the Lord’s greatness and attributes. It is also necessary for
[GITA:11583] one to devel op a mental picture of the Lord to focus the mind during
[GITA:11584] meditation. The Lord details many of  His glorious forms from verse 10.21
[GITA:11585] to 10.38 , to aid in meditation. Some of the Lord’s attributes and special
[GITA:11586] presence in activities and enti ties were briefly des cribed in 5.29, 7.8, 9.16
[GITA:11587] etc. More details on these concepts are provided in this grand chapter.

[GITA:11619] Z _o {dXw… gwaJUm… à^d§ Z _hf©`… Ÿ&
[GITA:11620] Ah_m{X{h© XodmZm§ _hfuUm§ M gd©e… Ÿ&& 2 Ÿ&&
[GITA:11622] Even g roups of deities and great sages do not have complete
[GITA:11623] knowledge of My pa ramount qualities or about the creation of this
[GITA:11624] universe. I am the reason for the existence of all deities, all sages and
[GITA:11625] indeed every being, and I am beginningless. (10.2)
[GITA:11627] Comments: The Lord states that even deities and great sages do not
[GITA:11628] know about His greatness and powers completely , which implies that no
[GITA:11629] one in the universe knows the Lord fully. While He is the cause for the
[GITA:11630] creation of the universe and indeed for everyone’s existence, the Lord
[GITA:11631] Himself has no creator. He existed always and will continu e to exist
[GITA:11632] forever. Sri Rayaru in GV  cautions that one should not conclude  that the
[GITA:11633] reason for not knowing about His beginning is due to the difficulty in
[GITA:11634] obtaining such knowledge. The fact is that He is birthless and He always
[GITA:11635] existed. This is different from the incomplete knowledge that one has about
[GITA:11636] His act of creation which occurred, but one cannot completely comprehend.
[GITA:11637] Sri Rayaru provides three interpretations based on Sri Madhw acharya’s GB
[GITA:11638] for the phrase ‘na me vidhuhu ’ (no one knows Me) as follows  - (i) deities
[GITA:11639] and great sages do not understand My greatness fully; (ii) deities and great
[GITA:11640] sages do not understand My act of the creation of the universe completely;
[GITA:11641] (iii) deities and great sages do not fully understand that I have no
[GITA:11642] beginning. Sri Rayaru also quotes  a Brahma Sutra (2.3.9) which states
[GITA:11643] that the Lord is birthless and hence has no beginning.

[GITA:11648] One who knows Me as eternal, is not subject to birth.  The controller

[GITA:11665] Comments: The word anadi has an interesting i nterpretation by Sri
[GITA:11666] Rayaru in GV . A superficial meaning of anadi is one without beginning.
[GITA:11667] However, the Lord precedes this word by ajam (one without birth) , which
[GITA:11668] also means one without beginning. Dividing the word anadi as ana and adi
[GITA:11669] leads to two interpretations.  Ana means activity, adi is beginning, so anadi
[GITA:11670] means the one who is the cause of activity in everyone. Also, ana means
[GITA:11671] the deity mukhya prana (vayudeva) and hence anadi can also be interpreted
[GITA:11672] as the one who existed even before the deity mukhya prana . This
[GITA:11673] interpretation is also consistent with the Vedic quote in  the Purusha
[GITA:11674] Sookta which states – pranaad vayur ajayatha  (during the process of
[GITA:11675] creation, the deity Vayudeva arose out of the Lord’s breath).

[GITA:11714] During the period o f the previous Manu, I created the seven great
[GITA:11715] sages, the deities who emanated from the mind of  Brahma, and the four
[GITA:11716] Manu deities. Their progeny in turn populated the universe. (10.6)
[GITA:11718] Comments: The Lord stated previously that He is the cause for the
[GITA:11719] creation of all living beings. Here He is describing the details of such a
[GITA:11720] creation. The Lord initially created the seven great sages (Mareechi, Atri,
[GITA:11721] Angeerasa, Pulastya, Pulaha, Kratu, V asishta). Sri Rayaru in GV  explains
[GITA:11722] that Manu also means one endowed with  knowledge and hence Manu
[GITA:11723] deities also are all deities starting from four faced Brahma. The Lord
[GITA:11724] initially created Brahma and through him all other deities were created. The
[GITA:11725] progeny of the seven sages and the deities then populated the universe. The
[GITA:11726] reference to four types of Manu deities indicate s the categorization of
[GITA:11727] deities into four categories like human beings  described previously in
[GITA:11728] chapter 4 (4.13).  Brahmanas, kshatriyas, vyshyas and shudras are the four
[GITA:11729] classes of deities. Brahma belongs to the category of Brahmana . Deities
[GITA:11730] such as Vayudeva, Seshadeva, Rudradeva, Garuda, Indra are Kshat riyas
[GITA:11731] etc. It was clarified in 4.13  that the four categories in society are based on
[GITA:11732] the innate nature and talent of souls and , no category is superior to another.
[GITA:11733] In fact 4.13  uses the word varna which means colour. Thus, the four
[GITA:11734] categories are different like colours are different and one should not
[GITA:11735] confuse them with the caste system prevalent in society. The fact that these
[GITA:11736] types of categories exist even among deit ies is proof that one should not
[GITA:11737] grade people based on their classification.

[GITA:11897] Comments: After hearing about the Lord’s greatness and attributes
[GITA:11898] in brief, Arjuna  is now curious and interested in learning more. He states
[GITA:11899] that great sages and deities have praised the Lord’s attributes and the Lord
[GITA:11900] Himself has reiterated them. Further, Arjuna knows that even great deities
[GITA:11901] are not capable of fully knowing the Lord who is the creator of even
[GITA:11902] Brahma and Rudra (indicated by the use of  the Lord’s name Keshava in
[GITA:11903] 10.14, where ka refers to Brahma and Isha refers to Rudra, and Keshava is
[GITA:11904] in fact the one who created both Brahma and Rudra). Only the Lord knows
[GITA:11905] His forms fully. Arjuna further states that for one to meditate on the Lord, it
[GITA:11906] is important for one to visualize His forms. Hence, Arjuna would like to
[GITA:11907] learn about the Lord’s majestic forms. In 10.16, Arjuna requests the Lord to
[GITA:11908] teach him fully about His forms. Arjuna is never satisfied with any amount
[GITA:11909] of the sweet nectarine words of t he Lord.  In 10.16, Arjuna uses the term
[GITA:11910] vibhuti while referring to the Lord’s form. Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that
[GITA:11911] vibhuti has two different meanings. Firstly, vibhuti = vividhatayaa
[GITA:11912] bhootayaha meaning different forms of the Lord such as Rama, Krishna
[GITA:11913] etc., and secondly vibhuti = vishishtaha bhootayaha , meaning the form of
[GITA:11914] the Lord that bestows superiority to a specific entity or quality among its
[GITA:11915] peers. These will be detailed in later verses.

[GITA:11938] The Lord said:  O Arjuna, Superior among Kurus! I will tell you

[GITA:11940] (10.19)
[GITA:11942] O Gudakesha (Arjuna, one who has conquered sleep)! I am
[GITA:11943] omnipresent, I exist in the heart s of all living beings, and I power their
[GITA:11944] existence. I am responsible for the creation, sustenance, and dissolution of
[GITA:11945] all beings. (10.20)
[GITA:11947] Comments: The Lord is pleased with Arjuna’s sincerity and
[GITA:11948] curiosity and resolves to teach him about His majestic forms. The Lord
[GITA:11949] confirms that He has infinite forms. This seems to be in response to
[GITA:11950] Arjuna’s request in 10.16, where he wanted to learn about the Lord’s forms
[GITA:11951] fully (without leaving anything out). After all, not even great deities know
[GITA:11952] fully about the Lord’s forms or attributes. In 10.20, the Lord states that
[GITA:11953] while He has special presence in many entities , He is present in everyone’s
[GITA:11954] hearts, and He is the cause for the creation, the sustenance, and the
[GITA:11955] dissolution of the universe.
[GITA:11957] In the next 18 verses from 10.21 to 10.38, the Lord explains in detail
[GITA:11958] His specific, majestic forms. This group of verses is one of the mos t
[GITA:11959] important parts of the Gita.
[GITA:11961] Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that vibhuti roopa (divine manifestations)
[GITA:11962] are of two types – direct forms and hidden forms. The Lord describes both
[GITA:11963] types of manifestations. Direct form refers to His forms of Rama, Krishna,
[GITA:11964] Vyasa, Kapila etc., while the hidden forms refer to the Lord’s form resident
[GITA:11965] in specific objects that gives them supremacy. The hidden forms are of
[GITA:11966] three types: (i) supreme among similar objects, (ii) supreme among
[GITA:11967] dissimilar objects wh ich share a common conditi on, and (iii) supreme
[GITA:11968] among objects except for an obvious leader. These categories are identified
[GITA:11980] Chapter 10                                                                                                                                     253
[GITA:11982] in Sri Madhwacharya’s GTN  referring to an ancient work , the Vibhuti
[GITA:11983] Tattva. These categories will be identified in later verses. Also, Sri Rayaru
[GITA:11984] uses shabda nishpatti (word derivation) to indicate the specific attribute of
[GITA:11985] the Lord signified by the name of the chosen superior entity in each class.
[GITA:11987] Am{XË`mZm_h§ {dîUwÁ`m}{Vfm§ a{da§ew_mZ² Ÿ&

[GITA:11990] Among the twelve Adityas, I a m Vishnu. Among all radiant objects,
[GITA:11991] I am Ravi (Sun). I am Marichi among the Marut deities. I am The Moon

[GITA:11993] Marichi, and the Moon, I grant them superiority among their peers). (10.21)
[GITA:11995] Comments: Among the twelve children of Aditi, the Lord is Vishnu
[GITA:11996] (Vishnu = vyaptatvaat sarveshu pratishtatvaat  = the one who pervades the
[GITA:11997] universe and is resident in all). Among all luminous objects, He is Ravi
[GITA:11998] (rashmi yukto  = one who is full of infini te glow). Among the 49 Marut
[GITA:11999] deities He is Marichi ( marinam charayati  = the one who moves clouds).
[GITA:12000] Among stars, He is Shashi/Moon ( shashaha asya aasteeti = one who is full
[GITA:12001] of happiness).
[GITA:12003] In this verse, one can see examples of the different categories of t he
[GITA:12004] Lord’s manifestations. Vishnu is one of His direct manifestations. The
[GITA:12005] other three entities identified – Ravi, Marichi, Shashi are indirect
[GITA:12006] manifestations. Also, Ravi (Sun) is chosen as supreme among similar
[GITA:12007] radiant entities, while Shashi (the Moon) is indicated as supreme among the
[GITA:12008] stars. The Moon is not a star. However, it is the brightest object in the night
[GITA:12009] sky. This is an example of a superior object among dissimilar objects
[GITA:12010] (Moon and Stars) that share a common condition ( the night sky).  The
[GITA:12011] Lord’s special presence in the chosen superior object is signified by the
[GITA:12012] Lord’s attribute as explained by Sri Rayaru in GV through word derivation.
[GITA:12013] For example, Ravi is the worldly name one uses for the Sun, but primarily
[GITA:12014] Ravi means the one who is full of infini te glow, a reference to  the Lord
[GITA:12015] Almighty. This discussion applies to all other superior forms  as well.

[GITA:12413] is known to be superior among the Pandavas.
[GITA:12415] As per Sri Madhwacharya’s GTN, the above entities are identified as
[GITA:12416] having the special presence of the Lord as cases to illustrate their
[GITA:12417] superiority a mong other subcategories within a main category. This was
[GITA:12418] explained in the comment section of verses 10.19 and 10.20 , where it was
[GITA:12419] stated that the supremacy of the Lord among His hidden forms is of three
[GITA:12420] types: (i) supreme among similar objects, (ii) supre me among dissimilar
[GITA:12421] objects who share a common condition, and (iii) supreme among objects
[GITA:12422] except for an obvious leader. For example, among deities, after the Lord,
[GITA:12423] the order of gradation is Sri Lakshmi, Brahma, Vayu, Saraswathi, Bharati,
[GITA:12424] Sesha, Garuda, Rudra, Varuni, Sowparni, Parvati and then Indra. However,
[GITA:12425] Indra is superior among the deities in Swarga Loka (heaven).

[GITA:12496] O  Arjuna! What use is it for you to know about My majestic forms?

[GITA:12503] His infinite forms. There will be more description about the Lord’s
