[GITA:12507] Summary of Chapter 10
[GITA:12509] In this chapter, the Lord details His forms and presence in many
[GITA:12510] entities, attributes in response to Arjuna’s ques tions which a ppeared in
[GITA:12511] verses 10.12 to 10.18 . Arjuna was keen to learn about the Lord’s divine
[GITA:12512] glories and countless manifestations as one needs to form a mental image
[GITA:12513] of the Lord to visualize Him during concentrated meditation. The Lord
[GITA:12514] identifies His divine manifest ations and special presence in entities which
[GITA:12515] gives them superiority. These a re described in 18 verses from 10.21 to
[GITA:12516] 10.38. Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that vibhuti roopa (divine manifestation)
[GITA:12517] is of two types – direct forms and hidden forms. Direct form ref ers to His
[GITA:12518] forms of Vishnu, Rama, Krishna, Vyasa, Kapila etc., while hidden forms
[GITA:12530] Chapter 10                                                                                                                                     265
[GITA:12532] refer to the Lord’s presence in specific entities that gives them supremacy.
[GITA:12533] The superiority among the hidden forms are of three types: (i) supreme
[GITA:12534] among similar objects, (ii) supreme among dissimilar objects which share a
[GITA:12535] common condition, and (iii) supreme among objects except for an obvious
[GITA:12536] leader. Also, Sri Rayaru uses shabda nishpatti (word derivation) to indicate
[GITA:12537] the specific attribute of the Lord signified by the name o f the chosen
[GITA:12538] superior entity in each class.  In verse 10.21 , He identifies Ravi (sun) as the
[GITA:12539] entity that is superior among similar objects, namely luminaries. In the
[GITA:12540] same verse, the Lord also identifies Shashi ( Moon) as superior among stars.
[GITA:12541] The Moon is not a star. However, the Moon and the stars share the common
[GITA:12542] attribute of being visible in the night sky. In that sense, the Moon is
[GITA:12543] superior to the stars. This is an example of an entity that is superior amon g
[GITA:12544] dissimilar objects. In verse 10.22 , He identifi es sama veda  as superior
[GITA:12545] among the Vedas. However, it is well known that Rig veda is the superior.
[GITA:12546] So, the interpretation here is that the Lord is identifying Sama veda among
[GITA:12547] the Vedas except for the obvious leader (namely Rig Veda ). This is also
[GITA:12548] seen in verse 10.25, where the Lord identified japa (meditation) as superior
[GITA:12549] among the forms of worship where one knows that jnana (knowledge) is
[GITA:12550] the supreme form. In addition to such entities (both sentient and inert such
[GITA:12551] as mountains, rivers etc.), the Lord also signifies His presence in qualities
[GITA:12552] and attributes  such as fame, memory, intellect, tolerance etc.,  as seen in
[GITA:12553] verse 10.34 , and also in activities such as gambling in 10.36. In verse
[GITA:12554] 10.16, Arjuna had requested the Lord to teach him completely about His
[GITA:12555] majestic forms and manifestations , and after describing His d ivine
[GITA:12556] manifestations in verses 10.21 to 10.38, the Lord declares in verse 10.40 ,
[GITA:12557] that His forms are infinite , implying that no one can completely
[GITA:12558] comprehend Him.  The Lord concludes His sermon on His majestic forms
[GITA:12559] by cautioning Arjuna that he should not assume that the Lord’s various
[GITA:12560] forms are limited to those described in this chapter because they are infinite
[GITA:12561] and expansive. This is a prelude to the description of the Lord’s universal
[GITA:12562] form (next chapter).

[GITA:12579] Chapter 11 - The Lord’s Universal Form
[GITA:12581] Chapter Introduction:  This chapter of 55 verses is termed Vishwa
[GITA:12582] Roopa Darshana m (The Lord’s Universal Form). In the concluding ver se
[GITA:12583] of the previous chapter , the Lord declar es that He has presence in
[GITA:12584] everything in the universe and just a minute fraction of His energy causes
[GITA:12585] superiority in many objects. The Lord also indicates that previous teachings
[GITA:12586] provide only a glimpse of His powe rs. This chapter conveys more details
[GITA:12587] about His forms. After listening to the Lord’s teachings on His divine
[GITA:12588] manifestations, His amazing activities in terms of creation of the universe
[GITA:12589] etc., Arjuna is naturally curious to behold the Lord’s omnipotent form.  The
[GITA:12590] Lord grants Arjuna’s wish by giving him Divine Vision before exhibiting
[GITA:12591] His grand, Universal form which is the quintessential feature of this
[GITA:12592] chapter. The description of the Lord’s Universal Form mirrors the
[GITA:12593] description in the Purusha Sookta (the Nature of Cosmic Being), from  the
[GITA:12594] Rig Veda which is considered the primordial group of hymns that gave rise
[GITA:12595] to the entire  span of  Vedic literature. In that sense this chapter is like a
[GITA:12596] commentary on the Purusha Sookta. This chapter also has a soulful prayer
[GITA:12597] by Arjuna on seeing the Lord’s universal form. While the Lord had
[GITA:12598] previously taught Arjuna about His greatness and attributes, the act of
[GITA:12599] physically seeing the Lord’s universal form completely solidifies Arjuna’s
[GITA:12600] conviction in Sri Krishna’s teachings.

[GITA:13040] warriors dying in the war as  indicated here. Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that

[GITA:13042] Universal Form. The sa me Divine Vision also gave Arjuna the ability to
[GITA:13043] see things that would happen in the future.
[GITA:13045] Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that deities who have Divine Vision can
[GITA:13046] view things with infinite precision. In the epic Vishnu Dharma, there is an
[GITA:13047] episode related to K ing Puroorava and the Ashwini deities who visit him.
[GITA:13048] The King requests them to wait a short while as he wants  to see them after
[GITA:13049] taking a shower and dressing himself in his royal clothes  and ornaments.
[GITA:13050] The deities see him later and laugh at him. The King as ks the deities the
[GITA:13051] reason for their reaction. They say that even though the King took just
[GITA:13052] some time to get himself dressed; he had grown a little older during that
[GITA:13053] time. The implication here is that though everyone grows old every minute
[GITA:13054] of the day,  no one can see or feel the minute changes in their bodies. But
[GITA:13055] the Ashwini deities because of their divine eyesight were able to see even
[GITA:13056] the minutest change in the King’s body during the time that he took to dress
[GITA:13057] himself.

[GITA:13311] indwelling in them as indicated by the meanings above.

[GITA:13557] O Parantapa! Only by single minded devotion can one understand

[GITA:13562] obtain this vision of the Lord? This verse answers by stating that one needs
[GITA:13563] to surrender to Him with sincere, unconditional, unparalleled devotion to
[GITA:13575] 288                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:13576] experience a di rect vision of the Lord. The Lord uses the adjective
[GITA:13577] ‘ananya’ meaning unparalleled or incomparable to describe the path of
[GITA:13578] devotion. This implies that one should consider the path of devotion to be
[GITA:13579] superior to all other paths such as the path of knowledge,  the path of action,
[GITA:13580] donating to charity etc. This also means that these other paths are also
[GITA:13581] required for one to realize the Lord but are not sufficient in themselves.
[GITA:13582] They must be accompanied by single pointed devotion.
[GITA:13584] This verse has been recognized b y Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha in
[GITA:13585] BGS as summarizing this entire chapter. Reference to the word ‘ drashtum’
[GITA:13586] (to see) signifies the vision of the Lord’s Universal Form. This verse also
[GITA:13587] identifies unparalleled devotion as the way to experience divine vision.
[GITA:13588] Hence, this verse is indeed a summary of this entire chapter.

[GITA:13603] Summary of Chapter 11
[GITA:13605] After listening to the Lord’s teachings on His divine manifestations,
[GITA:13606] His amazing activities in terms of creation of the universe etc., in  the
[GITA:13607] previous chapter, Arjuna is naturally curious to physically see the Lord’s
[GITA:13608] form. The Lord now exhibits His grand, Universal form which is the core
[GITA:13609] of this chapter termed Vishwa Roopa Darshana  (Vision of The Lord’s
[GITA:13621] Chapter 11                                                                                                                                          289
[GITA:13623] Universal Form). The Lord  empowers Arjuna with  divine vision as one
[GITA:13624] cannot view  Him with ordinary eyes (11.8). Arjun a views the Lord’ s
[GITA:13625] amazing, incredible, Universal Form spanning the entire universe with
[GITA:13626] countless heads, limbs etc. The descriptions of the Lord’s Universal Form
[GITA:13627] mirrors that in the Rig Vedic hymn, the Purusha Sookta. Arjuna describes
[GITA:13628] the grand sight and compares the Lord’s energy to that of thousands of
[GITA:13629] rising suns (11.12). He can see the entire universe sheltering inside the
[GITA:13630] Lord including all the deities starting from four faced Brahma (11.15). He
[GITA:13631] also sees many deities entering the Lord and praying to  the Lord with
[GITA:13632] utmost humility (11.21). Everyone is frightened on seeing the Lord’s
[GITA:13633] terrifying form. The Lord indicates in 11.32  that He (taking the name of
[GITA:13634] Kala) is about to perform the act of destroying the evil forces  who had
[GITA:13635] caused the rise of immorali ty in the world. This was the reason for His
[GITA:13636] frightening form. The Lord further tells Arjuna that He had already killed
[GITA:13637] all the leaders of the Kaurava army excepting  a few, thereby clearing
[GITA:13638] Arjuna’s doubts about winning the war. Waging the war is now a for mality
[GITA:13639] for Arjuna (11.33). Arjuna, after seeing the Lord’s form states that while he
[GITA:13640] feels blessed, he continues to be terrified and threatened by the Lord’s
[GITA:13641] frightening form. He is also remorseful that he ha s not treated Krishna with
[GITA:13642] proper respect as he was not fully aware of His greatness (11.41) and asks
[GITA:13643] for forgiveness (11.44). Arjuna also requests Krishna to appear again in His
[GITA:13644] earlier form that he was used to seeing (11.46). The Lord states that it is
[GITA:13645] exceedingly difficult for anyone to experience a direct vision of His
[GITA:13646] Universal Form. Even great deities strive extremely hard to experience
[GITA:13647] such a vision (11.52). Undertaking even difficult tasks such as diligent
[GITA:13648] study of the Vedas, performing difficult rituals, donating to charity etc.,
[GITA:13649] will not help o ne to experience such a direct vision, unless they are
[GITA:13650] accompanied by unparalleled, pure, unconditional devotion to the Lord
[GITA:13651] (11.54). The last few verses in this chapter act as a bridge to the next
[GITA:13652] chapter which focusses on the path of devotion.

[GITA:13669] Chapter 12 - The Path of Devotion
[GITA:13671] Chapter Introduction: This chapter of 20 verses is known as Bhakti
[GITA:13672] Yoga (The Path of Devotion). In chapter 10, the Lord described His special
[GITA:13673] presence in beings a nd objects which gave them superiority among peers ,
[GITA:13674] and in chapter 11 the Lord revealed His Universal Form to Arjuna to
[GITA:13675] convince him of His strength and powers. The Lord also states that it is
[GITA:13676] exceedingly difficult for one to behold a vision of His Universal Form and
[GITA:13677] Arjuna was indeed fortunate to have been granted that Divine Vision. In the
[GITA:13678] concluding verses of chapter 11, the Lord declares that sincere devotion
[GITA:13679] towards Him is the best way for a seeker to reach Him. This chapter
[GITA:13680] expands on the concept of d evotion and is hence termed the Path of
[GITA:13681] Devotion. In verse 7.23, it was stated that those who propitiate other deities
[GITA:13682] will achieve only temporary fruits and not everlasting bliss. However, in
[GITA:13683] the scriptures it is stated that the Lord’s consort Goddess Mahalakshmi who
[GITA:13684] is ever liberated is worshipped by all deities from Brahma onwards and that
[GITA:13685] she grants liberation to the eligible. A natural question that would arise is
[GITA:13686] about the effects of propitiating Goddess Lakshmi who is also known to
[GITA:13687] grant moksha to de votees. Arjuna (on behalf of other seekers) seeks
[GITA:13688] clarification on the benefits of propitiating Goddess Lakshmi who is the
[GITA:13689] governing deity for the principle of  the unmanifest ( avyakta). The Lord
[GITA:13690] responds to Arjuna’s questio n in verses 12.2 to 12.7  of this chapter and
[GITA:13691] concludes that worshipping Lord Narayana is an easier way to attain
[GITA:13692] moksha than pleasing Mahalakshmi. Further, Lakshmi operates under the
[GITA:13693] Lord Almighty’s control. One should propitiate Sri Lakshmi and other
[GITA:13694] deities as part of the Lord’s entoura ge for maximum effect. Bhakti or
[GITA:13695] devotion is focusing one ’s mind on the Lord. The Lord teaches us methods
[GITA:13696] of worshipping Him through action ( karma yoga ), through knowledge
[GITA:13697] (jnana yoga ), through meditation ( dhyana yoga ) and through devotion
[GITA:13698] (bhakti yoga ). T he last eight verses in this chapter describe the
[GITA:13699] characteristics of an ideal devotee who is dear to the Lord.
[GITA:13713] Chapter 12                                                                                                                                       291
[GITA:13715] Worshipping Goddess Mahalakshmi and Lord Almighty
[GITA:13717] AOw©Z CdmM &
[GITA:13718] Ed§ gVV`wº$m `o ^º$mñËdm§ n`w©nmgVo Ÿ&
[GITA:13719] `o Mmß`ja_ì`º§$ Vofm§ Ho$ `moJ{dÎm_m… Ÿ&& 1 Ÿ&&
[GITA:13721] Arjuna said:  Some seekers propitiate the Lord Almighty with
[GITA:13722] extreme devotion and some others focus on worshipping Goddess
[GITA:13723] Mahalakshmi (also known as akshara, avyakta ), the imperishable,
[GITA:13724] unmanifest principle of divinity. Among these, which group ha s a better
[GITA:13725] understanding of the path to liberation? (12.1)
[GITA:13727] Comments: In chapter 7, verse 7.23 , the Lord clearly stated that
[GITA:13728] propitiating other deities will only yield temporary fruits and not the
[GITA:13729] permanent bliss experienced in moksha. In verse 11.55 , the Lord indicated
[GITA:13730] that one should consider Him the supreme entity and surrender to Him with
[GITA:13731] unconditional devotion to achieve liberation. However, in many instances
[GITA:13732] in the Vedas, it is clearly stated that Goddess Lakshmi also grants
[GITA:13733] liberation. Further, she i s superior to all other deities such as Brahma  and
[GITA:13734] Rudra and  is responsible for the crea tion of the universe. In verse 7.5 , it
[GITA:13735] was stated that Goddess Lakshmi controls all inert nature. She is superior to
[GITA:13736] all other deities as she is ever liberated and has an imperishable existence
[GITA:13737] (indicated by the adjective akshara in this verse). Given these facts, while
[GITA:13738] some seekers  focus exclusively on the Lord Almighty , others focus on
[GITA:13739] worshipping Goddess Lakshmi. A natural question one would have is about
[GITA:13740] the best path for the seeker, given that both the Lord (directly) and Goddess
[GITA:13741] Lakshmi (indirectly) are known to lead one to salvation.
[GITA:13743] The Easier Path to Liberation
[GITA:13745] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:13746] _æ`mdoí` _Zmo `o _m§ {ZË``wº$m CnmgVo Ÿ&
[GITA:13747] lÕ`m na¶monoVmñVo _o `wº$V_m _Vm… Ÿ&& 2 Ÿ&&
[GITA:13759] 292                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:13760] The Lord said:  In My opinion, those seekers who worship Me with
[GITA:13761] supreme faith, and conduct their prescribed duties and meditation with the
[GITA:13762] mind immersed in Me, are superior. (12.2)
[GITA:13763] Comments: The Lord responds to Arjuna’s question in the following
[GITA:13764] six verses, 12.2 – 12.7. In this verse, He categorically states that those who
[GITA:13765] propitiate Him with supreme devotion have a better understanding of the
[GITA:13766] path to liberation compared to those who focus only on propitiating
[GITA:13767] Goddess Lakshmi, the imperishable, unmanifest principle. The Lord
[GITA:13768] provides detailed reasoning for this in the following verses.
[GITA:13770] `o Ëdja_{ZX}í`_² Aì`º§$ n`w©nmgVo Ÿ&
[GITA:13771] gd©ÌJ_{MÝË`§ M Hy$Q>ñW_Mb§ Y«wd_² Ÿ&& 3 Ÿ&&

[GITA:13776] The immutabl e, unmanifest principle does not perish; is beyond
[GITA:13777] description and pervades everywhere; it is beyond comprehension, has no
[GITA:13778] limited form like the sky , and is eternal. Those who worship this principle
[GITA:13779] with control over the senses, with mental equanimity and desiring the
[GITA:13780] welfare of everyone will also attain Me. (12.3) (12.4)
[GITA:13781] Comments: Verse 12.3  lists eight superio r attributes of Goddess
[GITA:13782] Lakshmi – imperishable, indefi nable, unmanifest, omnipresent,
[GITA:13783] incomprehensible, immutable, constant, and eternal. As per the  scriptures,
[GITA:13784] propitiating Goddess Lakshmi will also lead one to liberation. These verses
[GITA:13785] clarify that those who propitiate Goddess Lakshmi who has these superior
[GITA:13786] attributes will also attain the Lord , but indirectly. Those who propitiate
[GITA:13787] Goddess Lakshmi mus t have strict sense control, mental equanimity, and
[GITA:13788] desire welfare for all.

[GITA:13811] It takes great effort to  propitiate the unmanifest principle  properly.
[GITA:13812] Attaining the final goal of eternal bliss is exceedingly difficult for one
[GITA:13813] following the path of propitiating only this principle. (12.5)
[GITA:13814] O Partha! One who surrenders all activities to Me, considering Me as
[GITA:13815] the Supreme One, worshipping Me with single minded devotion and
[GITA:13816] focusing the mind on Me will be able to cross the ocean of death bound
[GITA:13817] samsara, through My grace. (12.6) (12.7)
[GITA:13818] Comments: The Lord clarifies that achieving liberation by only
[GITA:13819] propitiating the unmanifest principle is exceedingly difficult. Sri
[GITA:13820] Madhwacharya in his GB states many reasons for this which are explained
[GITA:13821] by Sri Rayaru in GV.
[GITA:13823]  Goddess Lakshmi operates under the control of the Lord as stated in
[GITA:13824] 7.5, 15.17  and hence propitiating only her is an indirect path to
[GITA:13825] liberation.
[GITA:13826]  One must observe extremely strict measures in terms of controlling

[GITA:13828] dilution in these stipulations will hinder a seeker in obtaining
[GITA:13829] Goddess Lakshmi’s grace for achieving liberation. These stipulations
[GITA:13830] are detailed in verses 6.7, 6.8 etc.
[GITA:13831]  Propitiating the Lord is easier as He pardons devotees who are
[GITA:13832] unable to adhere strictly to stipulations in worship. The Lord will
[GITA:13844] 294                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:13845] ensure that such devotees will, in due course of time, overcome their
[GITA:13846] shortcomings (6.40).
[GITA:13847]  One who propitiates the Lord Almighty with the same effort that
[GITA:13848] would be spent in propitiating Goddess L akshmi will achieve
[GITA:13849] liberation sooner.
[GITA:13851] Sri Madhwacharya in GB  quotes passages from  the Sama Veda
[GITA:13852] (Madhuchhandasa and Ayasya branches) to support these interpretations.
[GITA:13853] Sri Vidyamanya Teertha in his GPM  states that those who only propitiate
[GITA:13854] Goddess Lakshmi may get distracted by the wealth that they may receive
[GITA:13855] from her which makes it very hard for such seekers to exert control over
[GITA:13856] their mind and senses.
[GITA:13858] In conclusion, worshipping the Lord directly is an easier way to attain
[GITA:13859] liberation compared to the indi rect way of pleasing the Lord through
[GITA:13860] Goddess Lakshmi. It must be noted that one must worship Goddess
[GITA:13861] Lakshmi and other deities such as Vayudeva, Rudra etc. also, but with a
[GITA:13862] conviction that all these deities are part of the Lord’s entourage. It should
[GITA:13863] also be noted that in the benedict ion of Gita Vivruti  [GV], Sri Rayaru
[GITA:13864] explicitly states – ‘Lakshmi Narayanam Natva ….’  which translates to – I
[GITA:13865] offer my obeisance to Goddess Lakshmi and Lord Narayana.

[GITA:13894] Focus your mind exclusively on Me. If this is not possible, direct

[GITA:13912] Comments: After having established that the bes t path for a devotee

[GITA:13914] that would arise is about the best way to do that. In these four verses, the
[GITA:13915] Lord describes a progressive method for a devotee to worship Him with
[GITA:13916] singular m ental focus. In verse 12.8 , the Lord states the superiority of
[GITA:13917] meditation with mental concentration ( dhyana yoga ) as previously
[GITA:13918] described in Chapter 6. If one is not able to achieve this, then one should
[GITA:13919] try learning about the Lord through scriptural studi es ( jnana yoga -
[GITA:13920] paroksha). If these are not possible, a devotee should practice repeatedly to
[GITA:13921] achieve these  (12.9). If for some reason, one is not able to perform such
[GITA:13922] practice, then the Lord states in 12.10 , that the devotee should at least
[GITA:13923] engage in phy sical activities that would please Him (such as worshipping
[GITA:13935] 296                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:13936] Him with flowers, service, cha rity etc.) as these activities are not taxing on
[GITA:13937] the mind and intellect. For those who do not have deep conviction in the
[GITA:13938] Lord, but would rather focus on propitiating other deities, the Lord states in
[GITA:13939] 12.11 that such a devotee should at least perform this propitiation without
[GITA:13940] expectations and submit the fruits of such action to Him. In verse 7.22 , the
[GITA:13941] Lord states  that even those who propitiate other deities will receiv e their
[GITA:13942] rewards only through the Lord Himself.
[GITA:13943] Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha in his BGS identifies 12.8  as the core
[GITA:13944] verse in this chapter. Here the Lord has indicated that the best path for a
[GITA:13945] devotee to attain liberation is through direct propitiation of Him with
[GITA:13946] singular mental focus (meditation) on Him. Thus, this verse contains the
[GITA:13947] core principles of this chapter.

[GITA:13952] Acquiring proper knowledge is better than repe titions of actions

[GITA:13961] steps. The final destination for every living being is to attain liberation
[GITA:13962] from bondage, a state where one would experience eternal bliss. The way to
[GITA:13963] attain moksha is by realizing direct vision and direct knowledge of the  Lord
[GITA:13964] (aparoksha jnana ). Such direct knowledge is achievable for one who is

[GITA:13966] Such meditation is possible for someone who has learnt about the Lord

[GITA:13980] Chapter 12                                                                                                                                       297
[GITA:13982] studies to obtain an understanding of the Lord. One will be able to focus
[GITA:13983] ones minds on meditation and scriptural studies , if one involves oneself in
[GITA:13984] activities that please Him (such as worshipping the Lord, service to society,
[GITA:13985] charity etc.).

[GITA:14144] Summary of Chapter 12
[GITA:14146] In chapter 10, the Lord described His divine presence in beings and
[GITA:14147] objects which give them superiority among their peers , and in chapter 11,
[GITA:14148] the Lord revealed His Universal Form to Arjuna to convince him of His
[GITA:14149] strength and powers. The Lord also state d that it is exceedingly difficult for
[GITA:14150] one to achieve the vision of His Universal Form and that Arjuna was
[GITA:14162] Chapter 12                                                                                                                                       301
[GITA:14164] indeed fortunate to have been granted that Divine Vision. In the concluding
[GITA:14165] verses of cha pter 11, the Lord declares that sincere devotion towards Him
[GITA:14166] is the best way for a seeker to reach Him. This chapter expands on the
[GITA:14167] concept of devotion and is hence termed the Path of Devotion.
[GITA:14169] In verse 7.23, it was stated that those who propitiate other deities will
[GITA:14170] achieve only temporary fruits and not  everlasting bliss. However, in the
[GITA:14171] scriptures it is stated that the Lord’s consort, Goddess Mahalakshmi who is
[GITA:14172] ever liberated is worshipped by all deities from Brahma onwards and she
[GITA:14173] grants liberation to the eligible. A natural question that would arise is about
[GITA:14174] the effects of propitiating Goddess Lakshmi who is also known to grant
[GITA:14175] moksha to devotees. Arjuna (on behalf of other seekers) seeks clarification
[GITA:14176] on the benefits of propitiating Goddess Lakshmi wh o is the governing deity
[GITA:14177] for the principle of the unmanifest ( avyakta). The Lord responds to
[GITA:14178] Arjuna’s question in verses 12.2 to 12.7  of this chapter and concludes that
[GITA:14179] worshipping Lord Almighty Narayana is an easier way to attain moksha
[GITA:14180] and pleasing Mahalakshmi is difficult. Further, Lakshmi operates under the
[GITA:14181] Lord’s control. One should propitiate Goddess Lakshmi and other deities as
[GITA:14182] part of the Lord’s entourage for maximum benefit.
[GITA:14184] Bhakti or devotion is focusing one ’s mind on the Lord. In verses
[GITA:14185] 12.8 – 12.12, The Lord teaches Arjuna the methods of expressing devotion
[GITA:14186] using facilities such as intellect, studying, performing prescribed duties etc.
[GITA:14187] The last eight verses in this chapter describe the characteristics of an ideal
[GITA:14188] devotee who is dear to the Lor d. Many of these characteristics were stated
[GITA:14189] in previous chapters and are consolidated here in a unified manner for easy
[GITA:14190] reference.

[GITA:14208] Chapter 13 - The Field and The Knower of the Field
[GITA:14210] Chapter Introduction: This chapter of 35 verses is termed Kshetra
[GITA:14211] Kshetrajna Yoga (The Field and the Knower  of the Field).  As indicated in
[GITA:14212] the introductory chapter, Sri Rayaru  in GV  has provided an excellent
[GITA:14213] categorization of the 18 chapters in Gita by dividing them into 3 groups of
[GITA:14214] 6 chapters each. Chapters 7 -12 dealt primarily with the topic of the Lord’s
[GITA:14215] attributes and greatness as seen in Chapter 10 (The Lord’s Divine
[GITA:14216] Manifestations), Chapter 11 (The Lord’s Universal Form) etc. After all, the
[GITA:14217] goal of  every living being is to realize the Lord to achieve liberation.
[GITA:14218] Chapters 1-6 discussed the various means for one to realize the Lord, such
[GITA:14219] as the path of knowledge, the path of action, the path of devotion etc. The se
[GITA:14220] last six chapters  (Chapter 13 to 18)  expand on some of the important
[GITA:14221] concepts covered in the previous chapters. In chapter 2, verses 2 -12
[GITA:14222] onwards, the attributes of individual souls were described. In chapters 10,
[GITA:14223] 11, 12 etc., the Lord’s forms, attributes and grea tness were discussed. In
[GITA:14224] verse 7.4 , the attributes of eightfold  inert nature were discussed. Arjuna
[GITA:14225] now wants to understand more about the interrelationships between the
[GITA:14226] three entities – the Lord Almighty, individual souls, and inert  nature. The
[GITA:14227] Lord responds to Arjuna’s questions on the entities in verses 13.2 to 13.24 .
[GITA:14228] The interrelationship s between these three entities form the philosophical
[GITA:14229] basis for the principle of fivefold differences (pancha bheda).
[GITA:14231] The Field and The Knower of the Field
[GITA:14233] AOw©Z CdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:14234] àH¥$qV nwéf§ M¡d j¡Ì§ joÌk_od M Ÿ&
[GITA:14235] EVÛo{XVw{_ÀN>m{_ kmZ§ ko`§ M Ho$ed Ÿ&& 1 Ÿ&&
[GITA:14237] Arjuna said:  O Keshava! I would like to know more about – inert
[GITA:14238] nature, the individual, the field of activity, the knower of the field of
[GITA:14239] activity, knowledge, and the object of knowledge. (13.1)
[GITA:14251] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     303
[GITA:14253] Comments: Arjuna requests details on the following six topics –
[GITA:14254] prakruti (inert nature) and purusha (individual soul), kshetra (field of
[GITA:14255] activity) and kshetrajna (one who fully knows about kshetra), jnana
[GITA:14256] (knowledge and prerequisites to obtain knowledge) and jneya (the one who
[GITA:14257] is to be known). In verses 13.2 to 13.7 , the Lord provides details on kshetra
[GITA:14258] and kshetrajna and verses 13.8 to 13.19 cover the topics of jnana and jneya.
[GITA:14259] Verses 13.20 to 13.24  are related to prakruti and purusha. The remaining
[GITA:14260] verses describe the interaction and interrelationships among these entities.
[GITA:14262] The word purusha can refer to both the individual soul ( jeevatma)
[GITA:14263] and the Lord Almighty (paramatma) based on the context of its use, as seen
[GITA:14264] from verses 13.22 where it refers to the individ ual soul and 13.23 , where it
[GITA:14265] refers to the Lord. Sri Rayaru in GV  clarifies that the wor d purusha in this
[GITA:14266] verse refers to the individual soul. Also, the word jnana which ordinarily
[GITA:14267] refers to knowledge should be taken to mean the method to obtain
[GITA:14268] knowledge. This will be evident from  the Lord’s response in verses 13.8 to
[GITA:14269] 13.12, where the Lord identifies 20 different characteristics needed to
[GITA:14270] obtain knowledge.
[GITA:14272] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:14273] BX§ eara§ H$m¡ÝVo` joÌ{_Ë`{^Yr`Vo Ÿ&
[GITA:14274] EVÚmo do{Îm V§ àmhþ… joÌk B{V V{ÛX… Ÿ&& 2 Ÿ&&
[GITA:14276] The Lord said:  O Son of Kunti!  This body  made of inert nature  is
[GITA:14277] the field of activity. One who has a good understanding of the constituents
[GITA:14278] of this field of activity is the knower. (13.2)
[GITA:14280] Comments: The Lord uses the word shareera (physical body) to
[GITA:14281] identify the entity that forms kshetra (the field of activity) , based of word
[GITA:14282] derivation. Here, shareera = shar (the entity subject to feelings) + eera (the
[GITA:14283] entity owing its existence to the Lord). The knower of the field of activity
[GITA:14284] is termed kshetrajna, the o ne who knows kshetra which is derived from
[GITA:14285] ksheeyate (the entity with indwelling Lord Almighty).

[GITA:14361] The field of activity is comprised of the following - the five basic
[GITA:14362] elements of nature (earth, water, fire, spa ce, air), principles of
[GITA:14363] individuation, consciousness, intellect and the three qualities of nature
[GITA:14364] which comprise the unmanifest. Along with these , there are eleven sense
[GITA:14365] organs (five organs of perception, five organs of action and mind), five
[GITA:14366] objects of the sense organs ( form, smell, sound, taste, touch), emotions of
[GITA:14367] desire, disdain, pleasure, pain, the physical body, mental propensity, and
[GITA:14368] determination (all these entities have governing deities). (13.6) (13.7)
[GITA:14370] Comments: The Lord describes the composition  of the field of
[GITA:14371] activity. It contains both physically observable elements such as the five
[GITA:14372] basic elements of nature, inner faculties, and qualities/attributes. All these
[GITA:14373] make up a personality. The unmanifest entity is comprised of the three
[GITA:14374] qualities of n ature, namely, sattv (pious), rajas (passion), and tamas
[GITA:14375] (ignorance). The principle of intellect is one of the four inner faculties ,
[GITA:14376] which are mind ( manas), intellect ( buddhi), individuation (ahankara), and
[GITA:14377] memory ( chitta). The mind causes confusion, and the intellect helps in
[GITA:14378] discrimination.
[GITA:14391] 306                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:14392] In verse 13.34 , the Lord had also indicated that He would describe
[GITA:14393] the entities that govern the components of the field of activity. They are
[GITA:14394] governed by deities who cause the entities to act. The deities who control
[GITA:14395] the components of the field of activity are described by Sri Rayaru in GV
[GITA:14396] as follows -
[GITA:14398] (i) The five basic elements of nature: space (Ganap athy), air
[GITA:14399] (Mareechi), fire (Vahni), water (Varuna), and earth (Dhara Devi)
[GITA:14400] (ii) The four cosmic principles: avyakta - unmanifest (Lakshmi),
[GITA:14401] mahat – cosmic intelligence (Brahma), ahankara - individuation (Rudra),
[GITA:14402] buddhi - intellect (Parvati)
[GITA:14403] (iii) The mind (Skanda, Indra, Aniruddha – son of Kama)
[GITA:14404] (iv) 5 sense organs of perception): ear (Moon), skin (Marut), eyes
[GITA:14405] (Sun), tongue (Varuna), nose (Ashwini twins)
[GITA:14406] (v) 5 sense organs of action: voice (Agni), hands (Maruts), Feet
[GITA:14407] (Yagna, Shambhu), excretory organs (Yama), organs of reproduction
[GITA:14408] (Shiva, Manu)
[GITA:14409] (vi) 5 objects of sense organs: sound, touch, form, taste, smell
[GITA:14410] (five  children of Shiva)
[GITA:14412] The above 25 principles result in the ef fects of emotions indicated in
[GITA:14413] 13.7. The governing entities for these effects are:  Desire (Sreedevi and
[GITA:14414] Bharatidevi), disdain (Kali), sadness (Dwapara), happiness (Mukhya
[GITA:14415] Vayu), determination and boldness (Saraswati, Bharati), mental propensity
[GITA:14416] (Sreedevi), physical Body (other deities)
[GITA:14417] The relative gradations o f these governing deiti es were alluded to in
[GITA:14418] verse 3.42 . All these deities operate under the control of the Lord as
[GITA:14419] indicated previously in verse 3.43.
[GITA:14420] A note on the principles of mahat and buddhi: Many times, the term
[GITA:14421] buddhi is used to refer to both mahat and buddhi. However, mahat and
[GITA:14422] buddhi are different principles with mahat referring to cosmic intelligence
[GITA:14434] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     307
[GITA:14436] and buddhi referring to normal intelligence. In that sense, mahat, whose
[GITA:14437] governing deity is Brahma , is responsible for special, divine knowledge
[GITA:14438] (vijnana - aparoksha), and buddhi whose governing deity is Parvati is
[GITA:14439] responsible for acquired knowledge ( jnana - paroksha). The concepts of
[GITA:14440] jnana and vijnana were covered in Chapter 7. Also, many principles have
[GITA:14441] multiple governing deities, with one primary governing deity and one or
[GITA:14442] more secondary deities. In all cases, the Lord is the controlling deity.

[GITA:14545] elements of nature (air, space). This is a way of indicating that the Lord is
[GITA:14546] above and beyond the influence of nature.

[GITA:14694] Comments: In the next five verses 13.20 – 13.24, the Lord answers
[GITA:14695] Arjuna’s question from verse 13.1 regarding prakruti (nature) and purusha
[GITA:14707] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     313
[GITA:14709] (being). Prakruti can mean both insentient nature and sentient nature.
[GITA:14710] Likewise, purusha can mean both the individual soul and the Supreme Soul
[GITA:14711] (Lord Almighty). The appropriate interpretation depends on the context in
[GITA:14712] which these words are used. Verse 13.6 describes  prakruti (nature), and
[GITA:14713] verse 13.7 describes its transformations. These constitute the physical body
[GITA:14714] and personality of purusha (the living being – individual soul). Both nature
[GITA:14715] and individual souls have no beginning and have always existed.

[GITA:14732] living beings and for the experience of their emotions, Goddess Lakshmi

[GITA:14777] The Lord resides in all individuals and is a witness to their activities.
[GITA:14778] He activates and propels every action based on a soul’s innate abilities. He
[GITA:14779] consumes the fruits of all activities, and He is omnipotent. (13.23)
[GITA:14781] Comments: Verse 13.4 raises many questions on the field of
[GITA:14782] activity, the knower etc. One of the questions was about the entity who
[GITA:14783] governs the field of activity. The Lord answers this question by stating that
[GITA:14784] He is the entity that governs all activit ies in all beings, and He is also the
[GITA:14785] consumer of all these activities. The previous verse 13.22 indicated that
[GITA:14786] interactions with the effects of the qualities of nature determine the future
[GITA:14787] birth of an individual. This verse clarifies that the qualities of  nature are
[GITA:14788] material causes and the instrumental cause is the Lord. As stated in
[GITA:14800] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     315
[GITA:14802] comments to verse 13.20 , the word purusha can refer to either a living
[GITA:14803] being, or the Lord Almighty and the appropriate interpretation depends on
[GITA:14804] the context. In this verse, purusha refers to the Lord due to the use of the
[GITA:14805] adjective para (supreme).

[GITA:14810] One who understands that the individual souls and the Supreme One
[GITA:14811] are different, who understand s nature (sentient and insentient) and acts
[GITA:14812] accordingly, will no t be reborn regardless of one ’s state and condition
[GITA:14813] during one’s lifetime. (13.24)
[GITA:14815] Comments: Verses 13.20 to 13.23 described the interaction between
[GITA:14816] purusha (living being) and prakriti (sentient and insentient nature).
[GITA:14817] Together with previous verses which described the interaction of these
[GITA:14818] entities with the Lord, one can understand the relationship among these
[GITA:14819] three entities. The Lord states that one who has a proper understanding of
[GITA:14820] these concepts will achieve liberation even if one has strayed onto wrong
[GITA:14821] paths in one’s lifetime. Many times, even the learned ones due to force of
[GITA:14822] circumstances (such as a curse) might stray away from the right path. Such
[GITA:14823] beings will in due course of time, through the Lord’s grace, get back to the
[GITA:14824] right path and move towards liberation.

[GITA:14832] Some visualize the Lord residing in their bodies through their
[GITA:14833] intellect and through meditation. Some visualize the Lord through the path
[GITA:14834] of knowledge. Some visualize the Lord in their duties (Work is Worship).

[GITA:14847] 316                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:14849] Those who cannot visualize the Lord throu gh the above means ,
[GITA:14850] worship the Lord by learning about Him from scholars. Even those, who
[GITA:14851] rely only on acquiring knowledge about the Lord through listening to
[GITA:14852] scriptures, will cross this ocean of worldly affliction. (13.26)
[GITA:14854] Comments: Since one needs to ex perience a direct vision of the
[GITA:14855] Lord to attain divine, spiritual knowledge, this verse identifies the different
[GITA:14856] paths taken by seekers in their spiritual journey. Some visualize the Lord
[GITA:14857] through concentrated meditation ( dhyana). Some visualize the Lord
[GITA:14858] through intense study, contemplation, and analysis of scriptures  (jnana).
[GITA:14859] Some visualize the Lord through performance of prescribed duties without
[GITA:14860] expectations (karma).
[GITA:14862] Sri Rayaru in GV quotes Sri Madhwacharya’s GTN  for a second
[GITA:14863] interpretation of this verse . Some sages visualize the Lord in their hearts
[GITA:14864] through meditation and through their innate talent ( pratibha) of novel
[GITA:14865] interpretations of scriptures. Deities , through their innate talent of
[GITA:14866] discovering newer interpretations of scriptures , can visualize the  Lord
[GITA:14867] without a need for vocal instruction from their superiors. Some who are
[GITA:14868] superior among  rulers perform their prescribed duties such as protecting
[GITA:14869] their citizens during attac k from enemies  and performance of sacrifices
[GITA:14870] (such as Ashwamedha). They visual ize the Lord who appears before them
[GITA:14871] to consume their offerings during such sacrifices.
[GITA:14873] Verse 13.26 addresses the situation of those who are not as talent ed
[GITA:14874] as the deities indicated in 13.25 . Such seekers also benefit greatly from
[GITA:14875] learning about the Lord through vocal instructions from their teachers and
[GITA:14876] can ultimately cross the ocean of worldly miseries. This indicates the power
[GITA:14877] of shravana or vocal instruction. Deities starting from Brahma have
[GITA:14878] gradations in not only their physical form but also in their innate talent. For
[GITA:14879] example, Lord Brahma and Lord Vayudeva are endowed with 32 superior
[GITA:14880] qualities in their physical form. Other deities have lesser superior qualities
[GITA:14881] in their physical form s. Likewise, Lord Brahma  and Vayu have the highest
[GITA:14893] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     317
[GITA:14895] innate talent ( pratibha) among all living beings and can visualize and
[GITA:14896] meditate on the Lord without any explicit vocal instruction. But it is
[GITA:14897] observed that even these great deities are often listening to Vedic teachings
[GITA:14898] from the Lord. They do this as a respect to the Lord to earn His grace and
[GITA:14899] to develop even deeper conviction in their understanding of Him.

[GITA:14906] O Superior among the Bharatas! Know that all entities in the
[GITA:14907] universe, movable and immovable, are created out of the union of sentient
[GITA:14908] nature and the Lord Almighty. (13.27)
[GITA:14910] Comments: The Lord continues t o answer the question posed in
[GITA:14911] 13.27 regarding the field of activity, its origins, its transforma tions etc. This
[GITA:14912] verse describes the process of creation of living beings. The union of
[GITA:14913] kshetrajna (the Lord Almighty) and kshetra (the sentient nature embodied
[GITA:14914] by Goddess Lakshmi) results in the creation of all entities in the universe.
[GITA:14915] The word kshetra which was previously interpreted to mean the physical
[GITA:14916] body of living beings can also be interpreted to mean Goddess Lakshmi. It
[GITA:14917] should be noted that in a later verse 14.3 , the Lord explicitly indicates that
[GITA:14918] He and His consort are responsible for the creation of all living beings.

[GITA:14960] All activities of living being s are performed by the Lord Almighty

[GITA:14964] Comments: This verse clarifies that the difference in birth situati ons
[GITA:14965] experienced by living beings is primarily due to their differing innate
[GITA:14966] natures (and resulting activities) and not due to any partiality on the p art of
[GITA:14967] the Lord. Sri Rayaru in GV  quotes the Brahma Sutra (2.1.35) to support
[GITA:14968] the argument that the Lord does not exhibit partiality towards anyone.
[GITA:14970] This verse also describes the doership of activities perform ed by
[GITA:14971] living beings. Rayaru in GV  provides two interpretations for this verse
[GITA:14972] based on the phrase ‘ atmanam akartaram’. It was stated previously in
[GITA:14984] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     319
[GITA:14986] comments on verse 6.5 , that the word ‘ atma’ has many meanings and the
[GITA:14987] two meanings applicable here are – individual soul and Supreme Soul
[GITA:14988] (Lord Almighty). With these two meanings, the phrase ‘ atmanam
[GITA:14989] akartaram’ can be interpreted as follows  - Ones who are consi dered truly
[GITA:14990] knowledgeable are aware that -
[GITA:14992] (i) the Lord who activates the individual beings to perform their
[GITA:14993] activities is Himself not activated by anyone else (akartaram)
[GITA:14995] (ii) living beings cannot perform any activities independently
[GITA:14996] (akartaram)
[GITA:14998] This important verse is identified by Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha in
[GITA:14999] his BGS as comprising the core concepts in this chapter.

[GITA:15004] One who  realizes that multitudes of different living beings exist

[GITA:15011] ‘pritak’ (different) when describing various living organisms ( bhootanam),
[GITA:15012] refers to the varying nature of individual souls ( jiva-jiva bheda ) which is
[GITA:15013] one of the essentia l features of the pancha bheda (the fivefold differences)
[GITA:15014] principle. This will be explained at the end of this chapter.

[GITA:15030] 320                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:15031] He is imperishable. Hence the Lord, even thoug h existing inside an
[GITA:15032] individual will not be impacted by the defects of that individual. The
[GITA:15033] activities of individuals do not taint the Lord. (13.32)
[GITA:15034] Summary: The previous verse alluded to the difference s amongst
[GITA:15035] individual souls and between individual soul s and the Lord. This verse
[GITA:15036] purports to answer many questions that may arise from superficial
[GITA:15037] interpretations in scriptures that seem to indicate identity among individual
[GITA:15038] souls and the Lord. Sri Rayaru in GV quotes Sri Madhwacharya’s GTN and
[GITA:15039] advances five arguments to illustrate the difference between individual
[GITA:15040] souls and the Lord.
[GITA:15042] 1. This verse uses the word ‘ shareerastha’ to refer to individual souls
[GITA:15043] who have physical bodies comprised of the elements of nature and
[GITA:15044] are subject to birth. The Lord is referred to as ‘ anadi’ (birthless).
[GITA:15045] This concept was described in 10.3.
[GITA:15046] 2. Individual souls are influenced by the three qualities of nature ( guna)
[GITA:15047] as indicated in verses 13.20 to 13.22. The Lord is referred to as
[GITA:15048] ‘nirguna’ (the one beyond the three qualities of nature). This concept
[GITA:15049] is discussed in 7.13 and 14.19.
[GITA:15050] 3. This verse uses the word ‘ shareerastha’ to refer to individual souls
[GITA:15051] who have physical bodies comprised of the elements of nature and
[GITA:15052] hence are subject to decay and death. The Lord is referred to as
[GITA:15053] ‘avyaya’ (imperishable). This conce pt was discussed previously in
[GITA:15054] 2.17.
[GITA:15055] 4. The Lord independently causes the activities of individual souls who
[GITA:15056] by themselves cannot perform any activity. The Lord’s activities are
[GITA:15057] not with any expectations as indicated by the phrase ‘ na karoti’. The
[GITA:15058] Lord has no obligation  to perform any activities.  This concept was
[GITA:15059] indicated in 3.22.
[GITA:15060] 5. Even though the Lord is the cause of activities in everyone, He
[GITA:15061] Himself is not tainted by the actions of individual souls as indicated
[GITA:15073] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     321
[GITA:15075] by the phrase ‘na lipyate’. This was also indicated in verses 4.14, 9.9
[GITA:15076] and 13.30.
[GITA:15078] `Wm gd©JV§ gm¡úå`mX² AmH$me§ Zmon{bß`Vo Ÿ&
[GITA:15079] gd©ÌmdpñWVmo Xoho VWm@@Ë_m Zmon{bß`Vo && 33 &&
[GITA:15081] Just as space that pervades everywhere and touches everything  is not
[GITA:15082] tainted by anything, the Lord li kewise is pervading everywhere and in
[GITA:15083] everyone, but is never tainted. (13.33)
[GITA:15085] Comments: This verse provides an example to illustrate the concept
[GITA:15086] of the Lord not getting tainted by anyone’s activities which was addressed
[GITA:15087] in the previous verse. Space exists  everywhere, in the minutest of objects
[GITA:15088] and outside in the entire universe. However, it does not take on the
[GITA:15089] attributes of those objects. Likewise, the Lord who resides in every being is
[GITA:15090] not impacted by the attributes and activities of these beings. A simi lar
[GITA:15091] example was employed previously in verse 9.6.

[GITA:15102] inhabitants.
[GITA:15104] The Fivefold Difference
[GITA:15106] joÌjoÌk`moaod_² AÝVa§ kmZMjwfm Ÿ&
[GITA:15107] ^yVàH¥${V_moj§ M `o {dXw`m©pÝV Vo na_² Ÿ&& 35 Ÿ&&
[GITA:15119] 322                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:15121] One who can, through the eyes of knowledge, clearly understand the
[GITA:15122] difference between the field of  activity, the knower of the field of activity
[GITA:15123] and the method to achieve liberation from nature’s bondage, will surely
[GITA:15124] attain the Lord’s abode. (13.35)
[GITA:15126] Comments: The Lord concludes His teachings in this chapter by
[GITA:15127] summarizing that one , who by following th e methods in 13.8 to 13.12  can
[GITA:15128] attain proper knowledge about the field of activity and the knower of
[GITA:15129] activity, and the differences between them will indeed attain the Lord
[GITA:15130] whose special attributes and differences from individual souls and inert
[GITA:15131] objects were identified in various verses such as 13.32 to 13.34 . This verse
[GITA:15132] uses the term antaram (difference) to indicate the difference between
[GITA:15133] kshetra (living beings and nature) and the kshetrajna (the Lord Almighty).
[GITA:15135] The relationship between the three entities in the universe, namely
[GITA:15136] individual souls, inert nature, and the Lord Almighty described in this
[GITA:15137] chapter can be viewed as an explanation for the concept of fivefold
[GITA:15138] differences (pancha bheda), which is one of the foundational principles of
[GITA:15139] the philosophy of Sri Madhwacharya. The fivefold difference s among – (i)
[GITA:15140] inert objects, (ii) among individual souls, (iii) between individual soul s and
[GITA:15141] inert objects, (iv) between the Lord and  individual souls, and (v) between
[GITA:15142] the Lord and  inert objects. Verses 13.6 and 13.7 enumerated the different
[GITA:15143] components of nature that impact an individual’s personality. These
[GITA:15144] indicated the differences among the ine rt components of nature. Verse
[GITA:15145] 13.22 indicates that individual soul s experience different types of births
[GITA:15146] based on their interaction with the qualities of nature, and verse 13.31
[GITA:15147] refers to different living beings and hence they describe the difference that
[GITA:15148] exists be tween individual souls. Verses 13.20 and 13.21  describe the
[GITA:15149] impact of inert nature on living beings, highlighti ng the difference between
[GITA:15150] individual souls and inert objects. Verse 13.19 indicates  the difference
[GITA:15151] between inert nature and the Lord Almi ghty and verse 13.34  clarifies the
[GITA:15152] difference between the individual soul and the Lord Almighty.
[GITA:15166] Chapter 13                                                                                                                                     323
[GITA:15168] Summary of Chapter 13
[GITA:15170] As indicated in the intro ductory chapter, Sri Rayaru in GV  has
[GITA:15171] provided an excellent categorization of the 18 chapters of Gita by dividing
[GITA:15172] them into 3 groups of 6 chapters each. The last six chapters  (13 – 18)
[GITA:15173] provide details on some of the important c oncepts covered in the previous
[GITA:15174] chapters. In chapter 2, verses 2 -12 onwards, the attributes of individual
[GITA:15175] souls were described. In chapters 10, 11, 12 etc., the Lord’s forms,
[GITA:15176] attributes and grea tness were discussed. In verse 7.4 , the attributes of
[GITA:15177] eightfold inert nature were discussed. Arjuna now wants to understand
[GITA:15178] more about the interrelationships among the three entities – the Lord,
[GITA:15179] individual souls, and inert nature. This chapter provides clarification on this
[GITA:15180] topic and forms the philosophical basis for  the principle of fivefold
[GITA:15181] differences. In verse 13.1 , Arjuna requests details on the following six
[GITA:15182] topics – prakruti (inert nature) and purusha (individual soul), kshetra (field
[GITA:15183] of activity) and kshetrajna (one who fully knows about kshetra), jnana
[GITA:15184] (procedure to obtain knowledge) and jneya (the one who is to be known).
[GITA:15185] In verses 13.2 to 13.7 , the Lord provides details on kshetra and kshetrajna
[GITA:15186] and verses 13.8 to 13.19  cover the topics of  jnana and jneya. Verses 13.20
[GITA:15187] to 13.24 are related to prakruti and purusha. The remaining verses describe
[GITA:15188] the interaction and interrelationship s between these entities. The
[GITA:15189] relationship among the three entities in the universe, namely the individual
[GITA:15190] souls, inert nature that the Lord described in this chapter can be viewed a s
[GITA:15191] an explanation for the concept of fivefold differences ( pancha bheda )
[GITA:15192] which is one of the foundational principles of the philosophy of Sri
[GITA:15193] Madhwacharya.

[GITA:15196] End of Chapter 13
[GITA:15208] 324                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita

[GITA:15210] Chapter 14 - Division of Qualities
[GITA:15212] Chapter Introduction: This chapter of 27 verses is termed
[GITA:15213] Gunatraya Vibhaga Yoga  (Division of Qualities). This chapter has details
[GITA:15214] on the three qualities of nature ( sattv – pious, rajas – passion, tamas –
[GITA:15215] ignorance) which define one s personality. These concepts were introduced
[GITA:15216] in chapter 3 (3.5) and are expanded here. The c reation of the universe
[GITA:15217] through sentient Mother Nature is described. The ways in which the three
[GITA:15218] qualities bind a person are also explained. The method to escape from the
[GITA:15219] clutches of the three qualities are described . The previous chapter had a
[GITA:15220] discussion on the interaction s between inert nature, the individual soul, and
[GITA:15221] the Lord. Verse 13.22 indicates  the impact of the three qualities of nature
[GITA:15222] on living beings. Activities of  living beings are influenced by the three
[GITA:15223] qualities of nature and such activities entangle them. This chapter provides
[GITA:15224] details on the three qualities of nature in terms of their origin, influence,
[GITA:15225] impact and more importantly, the method to overcome them.
[GITA:15227] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:15228] na§ ^y`… àdú`m{_ kmZmZm§ kmZ_wÎm__² Ÿ&
[GITA:15229] `ÁkmËdm _wZ`… gd} nam§ {g{Õ{_Vmo JVm… Ÿ&& 1 Ÿ&&
[GITA:15231] BX§ kmZ_wnm{lË` __ gmYå`©_mJVm… Ÿ&
[GITA:15232] gJ}@{n ZmonOm`ÝVo àb`o Z ì`WpÝV M Ÿ&& 2 Ÿ&&
[GITA:15234] The Lord said:  O Arjuna! There is one more important principle
[GITA:15235] which I will teach you now. Great sages have attained liberation by
[GITA:15236] understanding this concept. (14.1)
[GITA:15238] One who realizes this knowledge will attain My abode and will not
[GITA:15239] be reborn during the next cycle of creation. Also, they will not suffer
[GITA:15240] during the next cycle of dissolution. (14.2)
[GITA:15253] Chapter 14                                                                                                                                        325
[GITA:15255] Comments: For one to get freed from bondage and achieve
[GITA:15256] liberation, it is important to understand the ways that one gets influenced
[GITA:15257] by the three qualities of nature. The Lord had resolved to impart suc h
[GITA:15258] knowledge to Arjuna in verse 2.39 and expand ed on th e concepts
[GITA:15259] introduced in verse 3.5. In verse 14.1 , the Lord states that seekers who
[GITA:15260] understood this concept previously had attained liberation , and hence it is a
[GITA:15261] proven path. In vers e 14.2, the Lord states the rewards for those who attain
[GITA:15262] this knowledge during their spiritual journey. Such seekers will attain
[GITA:15263] moksha, which is identified as the state where one does not suffer from
[GITA:15264] worldly miseries that impact living beings who are subject to repeated
[GITA:15265] births and deaths. In that sense, t he state of moksha is identified as
[GITA:15266] ‘sadharmya’ (in an extremely limited  sense, somewhat like the state of the
[GITA:15267] Lord who is never subject to any miseries).
[GITA:15269] Origin of the Three Qualities

[GITA:15277] O Bharata! Mother Nature (Goddess Mahalakshmi) is My consort, in
[GITA:15278] whose womb I place the embryo, from which the process of creation of all
[GITA:15279] beings starts. (14.3)
[GITA:15281] O Son of Kunti! For all living beings born in various species, Mother
[GITA:15282] Nature is the mother, and I am the father planting the seeds. (14.4)
[GITA:15284] Comments: In these two verses, the Lord describes the process of

[GITA:15286] His consort, Goddess Mahalakshmi who is the governing deity of nature.
[GITA:15287] This aspect was briefly  described previously in verse 13.27 . Inert nature
[GITA:15288] and its components were prev iously identified in verse 7.4 . Sri Rayaru in
[GITA:15300] 326                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:15301] [GV] clari fies that the interaction described in this verse applies to every
[GITA:15302] cycle of creation of the universe. Further, this applies to all categories of
[GITA:15303] living beings such as deities (angels), humans, and demons.

[GITA:15310] O Arjuna, Mighty Armed One! The three attributes, namely virtue
[GITA:15311] (sattva), passion ( rajas) and ignorance ( tamas) are born out of insentient
[GITA:15312] nature. These attributes tightly bind individua l souls which intrinsically do
[GITA:15313] not perish ( the governing deities for these three attributes are Sridevi,
[GITA:15314] Bhoodevi and Durgadevi which are forms of Goddess Mahalakshmi).
[GITA:15315] (14.5)
[GITA:15317] Comments: After describing the interaction between the Lord
[GITA:15318] Almighty and His co nsort, Goddess Mahalakshmi in the previous verse,
[GITA:15319] this verse outlines the process by which the three qualities of nature bind an
[GITA:15320] individual soul. Goddess Mahalakshmi, in her three forms of Sri, Bhoo, and
[GITA:15321] Durga governs the three qualities, namely virtue (sattva), passion ( rajas)
[GITA:15322] and ignorance ( tamas), respectively. In general, all living creatures are
[GITA:15323] entangled by these three qualities. Specifically, Goddess Sridevi binds
[GITA:15324] deities (angels), Goddess Bhoodevi binds humans, and Goddess Durgade vi
[GITA:15325] binds demons. Sr i Rayaru in GV  clarifies that souls who are in moksha
[GITA:15326] after liberation are not entangled by these qualities. The binding applies
[GITA:15327] only to beings who are not yet liberated. This is implied using the word
[GITA:15328] dehina (those with physical bodies). Liberated souls d o not have physical
[GITA:15329] bodies.

[GITA:15354] O Anagha (Arjuna, One without sins)! The quality of sattva is pure

[GITA:15356] diseases. It helps connect one with pure knowledge and bliss . (14.6)
[GITA:15358] O Son of Kunti! The quality of  rajas creates obsession and
[GITA:15359] attachment. It causes the feelings of desire and expectations with respect to
[GITA:15360] pursuing objects of sense pleasure. It binds one with passion ( sensory
[GITA:15361] pursuits). (14.7)
[GITA:15363] O Bharata! The quality of tamas is responsible for covering one with
[GITA:15364] ignorance. It can create delusion in everyone. It is responsible for
[GITA:15365] forgetfulness, lethargy, and excessive sleep. (14.8)

[GITA:15368] entanglement of the three qualities ( sattva, rajas, tamas ) on deities,
[GITA:15369] humans, and demons, respectively. It must be noted that even deities who
[GITA:15370] are destined for liberation will be bound by the quality of sattv till they
[GITA:15371] achieve divine, spiritual knowledge and attain liberation through the grace
[GITA:15372] of the Lord.

[GITA:15624] The Lord said:  O Son of Pandu! One who has transcended the three
[GITA:15625] qualities of nature ( gunas) neither abhors the light of knowledge, activity,
[GITA:15626] and delusion when th ey occur, nor crave s for them when they cease , OR,
[GITA:15627] On worldly issues, such people do not despise knowledge (due to sattva),
[GITA:15628] activity (due to rajas) or ignorance (due to tamas). But on the issue of the
[GITA:15629] Lord’s attributes, they crave for knowledge ( due to sattv) and activity (due
[GITA:15630] to rajas) and abhor delusion (due to tamas). (14.22)
[GITA:15632] Comments: The Lord responds to Arjuna’s questions about the traits
[GITA:15633] of those who overcome the influence of the three qualitie s in the following
[GITA:15634] four verses 14.22 to 14.25 . Many of t he abilities and attributes stated here
[GITA:15635] have been previously described in verses 2.55 to 2.59, 5.18 to 5.20, 6.7 to
[GITA:15636] 6.9, 12.13 to 12.30, 13.8 to 13.12 etc., while enumerating the characteristics
[GITA:15637] of seekers who are on the right spiritual path. The abilities  and attributes
[GITA:15638] described in these verses must be viewed in the context of one ’s
[GITA:15639] relationship with the three qual ities of nature. Sri Rayaru in GV  provides
[GITA:15640] the inner meanings of these verses  based on Sri Madhwacharya’s GB and
[GITA:15641] GTN.
[GITA:15643] The three qualities of n ature exist in two modes – gross and subtle.
[GITA:15644] The gross aspect of the three qualities of sattv, rajas and tamas leads one to
[GITA:15645] indulge in the respective pursuits of spiritual knowledge, sensory pleasure
[GITA:15646] and harmful lethargy. The subtle aspects of these three qualities result in
[GITA:15647] one displaying keen interest (due to sattv), some interest (due to rajas), and
[GITA:15648] disdain (due to tamas) respectively in learning about the Lord’s auspicious
[GITA:15649] attributes. One who has conquered the three qualities of nature does not
[GITA:15650] treat wi th contempt the outcomes of activities related to worldly matters.
[GITA:15651] However, with regard to learning about the Lord’s attributes, such a person
[GITA:15663] 334                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:15664] desires the impact of subtle aspects of sattv and rajas and abhors the impact
[GITA:15665] of tamas.
[GITA:15667] Sri Rayaru in GV  provides another meaning for this verse : One who
[GITA:15668] has conquered the three qualities of nature does not envy those who have
[GITA:15669] attained divine, spiritual knowledge due to sattv and does not wish for the
[GITA:15670] return of lost ignorant knowledge.

[GITA:15759] qualities of nature which bind a living being , and states that pure devotion

[GITA:15770] Comments: The previous verse states that a devotee who has

[GITA:15773] spiritual path will first reach the abode of Goddess Lakshmi and with Her
[GITA:15774] grace will be liberated in the abode  of Lord Almighty. This is the state
[GITA:15775] where the liberated souls will experience unending, uncorrupted bl iss.
[GITA:15777] Summary of Chapter 14
[GITA:15779] As indicated in the introductory section, the third set of chapters
[GITA:15780] (from Chapter 13 to 18), provide more details on specific concepts
[GITA:15781] discussed in the earlier sets of chapters. The previous chapter had a
[GITA:15782] discussion on the interaction between   inert nature, the individual soul, and
[GITA:15783] the Lord, and indicated the impact of the three qualities of nature, namely
[GITA:15784] sattv (piety), rajas (passion), and tamas (ignorance) on living beings.
[GITA:15785] Activities of living  beings are influenced by the t hree qualities of nature
[GITA:15786] and such activities entangle them. For one to get freed from bondage and
[GITA:15787] achieve liberation, it is important to understa nd the way  that one gets
[GITA:15788] influenced by the three qualities of nature. This chapter provides details on
[GITA:15789] the thre e qualities of nature in terms of their origin (verses 14.3 -14.4),
[GITA:15801] Chapter 14                                                                                                                                        337
[GITA:15803] entanglement (verses 14.5 –14.8), impact and result (verses 14.11 -14.18).
[GITA:15804] Verse 14.19 clarifies that the Lord Almighty controls the three qualities of
[GITA:15805] nature and is beyond their reach. The Lord also states in 14.21 that a seeker
[GITA:15806] should strive to traverse beyond these three qualities to achieve liberation.
[GITA:15807] In verses 14.22 to 14.27, the Lord enumerates the traits of those who escape
[GITA:15808] entanglement by these three qualities and eventually reach His abode.
[GITA:15810] && B{V MVwX©emo@Ü`m`… &&
[GITA:15811] End of Chapter 14

[GITA:15825] Chapter 15 – Theology of The Supreme Being
[GITA:15827] Chapter Introduction:  This chapter of 20 verses is known as
[GITA:15828] Purushottama Yoga  (Theology of The Supreme Being) . This chapter is
[GITA:15829] principally concerned with the establishment of the principle of the Lord
[GITA:15830] Almighty’s supremacy and hence is termed Purushottama Yoga  where
[GITA:15831] uttama means Supreme and purusha means Being. This chapter is
[GITA:15832] considered by many to have the core teachings of the en tire Gita. The Gita
[GITA:15833] has 700 verses spread over 18 chapters.  Chapter 15 which has 20 verses ,
[GITA:15834] interestingly has 700 letters (15 verses  have 32 letters  each and the
[GITA:15835] remaining 5 verses  have 44 letters  each)! This gives credence to the
[GITA:15836] argument of this chapter ’s importance based on numerology. While the
[GITA:15837] Lord had previously described the components of the universe such as
[GITA:15838] living beings, inert objects, and the Lord, in this chapter , He illustrates the
[GITA:15839] interrelations among them using the example of a banyan tree. The Lord
[GITA:15840] had indicated His presence in  living beings previously, especially within
[GITA:15841] their hearts in  verses 9.4, 10.20, and 13.18 . This chapter provides more
[GITA:15842] details on the aspects of His presence in living beings. Further, in the
[GITA:15843] previous chapter 13.24 , it was stated that a seeker who understands the
[GITA:15844] relationship between the Lord ( purusha) and nature will eventually achieve
[GITA:15845] liberation. This chapter provides more details on the attributes of the Lord
[GITA:15846] (purusha). In verse 15, the Lord explicitly states His pre sence in everyone
[GITA:15847] and declares that He is the primary subject matter of the Vedas. In verses
[GITA:15848] 16 to 20, the Lord emphatically describes Himself as the Supreme Being ,
[GITA:15849] different from all other beings, thereby convincingly establishing the
[GITA:15850] philosophy of duali sm ( dvaita) which was popularized by Sri
[GITA:15851] Madhwacharya and other seers in his lineage such as Sri Jaya Teertha and
[GITA:15852] Sri Raghavendra Teertha.
[GITA:15869] Chapter 15                                                                                                                                       339
[GITA:15871] The Tree of the Universe
[GITA:15873] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:15874] D$Üd©_yb_Y…emI_² AídËW§ àmhþaì``_² Ÿ&
[GITA:15875] NÝXm§{g `ñ` nUm©{Z `ñV§ doX g doX{dV² Ÿ&& 1 &&
[GITA:15877] The Lord said:  The eternal banyan tree of the Universe is
[GITA:15878] characterized by the following  - The Lord is like the earth that supports the
[GITA:15879] tree, Mother nature is the root of the tree. The 8 principles of nature are the
[GITA:15880] branches of the tree. The tree is eternally transforming like a running
[GITA:15881] stream. The Vedas are the leaves of this tree.  One who knows these, knows
[GITA:15882] the Vedas.
[GITA:15884] Comments: This enigmatic verse describes the universe using the
[GITA:15885] example of a banyan tree. One must carefully analyze eac h word to
[GITA:15886] understand the inner meanings in  this verse. Sri Rayaru in his GV based on
[GITA:15887] Sri Madhwacharya’s GB and GTN  provides an excellent interpretation for
[GITA:15888] this verse using the word derivation approach of Sanskrit.
[GITA:15890] Firstly, the word ‘oordhwa’ is derived from ‘uttamatvaat’ and means
[GITA:15891] ‘one that is superior ’. Further, in the Vedas, Lord Vishnu is described as
[GITA:15892] ‘oordhwa’, hence it refers to Lord Almighty Vishnu. Thus, Lord Vishnu is
[GITA:15893] the foundational component for the tree and hence represents the earth that
[GITA:15894] supports the tree. Sentient nature and its three qualities are governed by the
[GITA:15895] Lord’s consort Mahalakshmi who is superior to all other entities in the
[GITA:15896] universe and hence represents the three roots of this Tree of the Universe.
[GITA:15897] The word ‘adha’ means inferior an d represents the 8 principles of nature
[GITA:15898] (the 5 elements of physical nature and the principles of mahat -
[GITA:15899] consciousness, ahankara - individuation, and buddhi - intellect). These 8
[GITA:15900] principles and their governing deities are like the branches of this Tree of
[GITA:15901] the Universe. The tree is termed ashwattha (continuously transforming) and
[GITA:15902] avyaya (eternal). The word ‘ ashwattha’ can be derived in two ways.
[GITA:15903] (i) a + shwa + ttha , where shwa means ‘tomorrow’ a + shwa means ‘not
[GITA:15915] 340                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:15916] tomorrow’. Hence this word means that the state of the tree tomorrow is not
[GITA:15917] the same as it is today, which implies that the Universe is continuously
[GITA:15918] transforming. This is compared to a stream of running water, where water
[GITA:15919] is eternally running as a stream, but the content of water at any place at any
[GITA:15920] time is not the same as it is in  a previous instant. (ii) ashwattha is derived
[GITA:15921] from the word ‘ ashwa’ which means ‘horse’. A horse is constantly in
[GITA:15922] motion and does not stay still. Similarly, the universe is continuously in
[GITA:15923] motion. It should also be noted t hat previously in chapter 10 (10.26), the
[GITA:15924] Lord had stated that among all trees, He has a special presence in
[GITA:15925] ‘ashwattha’ (the banyan tree). The Vedas are like leaves of this tree. Just as
[GITA:15926] the leaves bloom and give rise to flowers and fruits, seekers who le arn the
[GITA:15927] Vedas will earn the fruits such as worldly riches and ultimately, moksha
[GITA:15928] (the Lord’s abode).
[GITA:15930] AYümoÜdª àg¥VmñVñ` emIm
[GITA:15931] JwUàd¥Õm {df`àdmbm… Ÿ&
[GITA:15932] AYü _ybmÝ`ZwgÝVVm{Z
[GITA:15933] H$_m©Zw~ÝYr{Z _Zwî`bmoHo$ Ÿ&& 2 &&
[GITA:15935] The branches of this Tree of the Universe are nourished by the three
[GITA:15936] qualities of nature and extend both above and below. The sprouts represent
[GITA:15937] the objects of sensory perception. The roots represent the Lord, sentient
[GITA:15938] nature, and inert nature. Nature along with its three qualities of sattv, rajas,
[GITA:15939] and tamas entangles living beings. Just like the roots of a tree are
[GITA:15940] responsible for the fruits grown, the rewards based on actions in this world
[GITA:15941] are due to  the Lord, sentient nature and the three qualities represented by
[GITA:15942] the roots. (15.2)
[GITA:15944] Comments: This verse co ntinues the description of the Tree of the
[GITA:15945] Universe and is even more enigmatic than the previous verse. In  the
[GITA:15946] previous chapter (14.5), it was stated that Goddess Mahalakshmi in her
[GITA:15947] three forms of Sri, Bhoo, and Durga controls the ‘gunas’, the three qualities
[GITA:15948] of nature (sattv, rajas, tamas). This verse states that the five basic elements
[GITA:15949] of nature and the three principles represented by the branches of this tree
[GITA:15961] Chapter 15                                                                                                                                       341
[GITA:15963] are influenced by the three qualities of nature  (gunas). Hence, the roots
[GITA:15964] which represent sentient and inert nature are superior to the branches which
[GITA:15965] represent the elements of nature and the three principles  (mahat, ahankara,
[GITA:15966] buddhi). The three qualities of nature (sattv, rajas, tamas ) are like  new
[GITA:15967] roots. The three principles and the five basic elem ents of nature present in a
[GITA:15968] living being are responsible for the objects of sensory perception which are
[GITA:15969] pursued by living beings. This was described previously in verses
[GITA:15970] 14.11 – 14.13. These objects of sensory pursuits are represented by the
[GITA:15971] sprouts whic h emanate from the branches of the tree. The sprouts have
[GITA:15972] temporary existence just like the experience of sensory pleasures by living
[GITA:15973] beings.
[GITA:15975] Sri Rayaru in GV  states that the above interpretation of the
[GITA:15976] components of the Tree of the Universe is based on t he description in the
[GITA:15977] Bhallava branch of the Vedas which states that the Lord who supports the
[GITA:15978] Tree of the U niverse is not part of the tree but is distinct from it.  The
[GITA:15979] components of the banyan tree (and their governing deities) in these two
[GITA:15980] verses can now be summarized as follows:
[GITA:15982] Earth (supporting the tree) = The Lord Almighty
[GITA:15983] Roots = Sentient and inert nature
[GITA:15984] New roots = The three qualities of nature
[GITA:15985] Branches = The five basic elements of nature , and the three
[GITA:15986] principles
[GITA:15987] Sub-branches = Physical bodies of living beings
[GITA:15988] Leaves = The Vedas
[GITA:15989] Flowers, Fruit = Worldly desires, Liberation
[GITA:15991] These two verses appear to illustrate the concepts of gradations
[GITA:15992] among various d eities described previously in 3.42  with the help of a
[GITA:15993] Banyan tree.

[GITA:16014] This tree is constantly evolving (like a flowing stream) and does not
[GITA:16015] stagnate; hence cannot be seen. It has neither beginning nor end. One
[GITA:16016] should chop this tree with the sharp weapon of firm detachment (as the tree
[GITA:16017] has very strong roots ), to separate the hidden roots from other parts of the
[GITA:16018] tree (one should use the strong weapon of devotion and detachment to
[GITA:16019] understand the distinction between the Lord, Nature and the individual
[GITA:16020] souls). (15.3)
[GITA:16022] Comments: After having described the structure of the Tree of the
[GITA:16023] Universe in previous verses, this verse states the action that a seeker needs
[GITA:16024] to take to progress on the spiritual path. The tree is constantly evolving as
[GITA:16025] new sprouts, lea ves, flowers, and fruits bloom and the old ones wither.
[GITA:16026] However, the earth and the strong roots do not wither. Similarly, the
[GITA:16027] entities in the universe such as living beings and inert objects are constantly
[GITA:16028] changing but the Lord and Mother Nature who are  represented by  the
[GITA:16029] strong, foundational roots of this tree, are not subject to any change and do
[GITA:16030] not perish. This verse clarifies that the Lord who pervades all and is
[GITA:16031] invisible during the beginning and end of the universe (during the time
[GITA:16032] epoch kalpa) continues to be invisible during its lifetime. These conc epts
[GITA:16033] were previously stated in 9.7 and 9.10 . To completely understand the
[GITA:16034] Lord’s greatness, a seeker must chop this tree with a strong, sharp weapon
[GITA:16035] to be able to separate the tree from its foundation and understand its roots.
[GITA:16036] That sharp weapon is described as asanga = a + sanga . This word can be
[GITA:16037] interpreted in two ways – (i) asanga = detachment (as sanga means
[GITA:16038] attachment) which implies that one should detach oneself from worldly
[GITA:16039] matters, and (ii) asanga = involvement in activities pleasing to the Lord, as
[GITA:16040] the letter a represents the Lord. This concept is clarified by Sri
[GITA:16041] Prabhanjanacharya in GM.

[GITA:16109] That destination is illuminated neither by the Sun nor by the Moon

[GITA:16113] Comments: The Lord describes the characteristics of His abode. The
[GITA:16114] world that we live in is illuminated by  the Sun (during daytime), the Moon
[GITA:16115] (during nighttime), and by fire. The Lord’s abode is vastly different. The
[GITA:16116] Lord is self -illuminating, and He does not need any external entities to

[GITA:16122] The eternal individual soul inside the physical body of beings is like
[GITA:16123] an infinitesimal fr action of Me (similar in being eternal but distinct ly
[GITA:16124] separate in attributes and capabilities). The individual soul directs the six
[GITA:16125] sense organs (including the mind) towards objects of pleasure, propelled by

[GITA:16131] present inside the physical bodies of individual soul s. This concept was

[GITA:16144] Chapter 15                                                                                                                                       345
[GITA:16146] like the individual soul as both are eternal in nature, but this fraction of the
[GITA:16147] Lord is vastly different and superior to all individual souls. This concep t is
