[GITA:16149] Madhwacharya’s GB states that a fraction or amsha of the Lord is of two
[GITA:16150] types – (i) bhinna amsha  (fraction that is different ) and (ii) swaroopa
[GITA:16151] amsha (intrinsic fraction, as in the case of the Lord’s various incarnations).
[GITA:16152] The fraction of the Lord present in living beings is like the individual soul
[GITA:16153] in the sense that a firefly is like the Sun, as both are illuminating objects but
[GITA:16154] are vastly different in attributes and capabilities.

[GITA:16159] At the time a soul enter s a body and at the time it leaves, the Lord
[GITA:16160] carries the sense organs (in a subtle form) into and out of the body, just like
[GITA:16161] a gentle, blowing wind carries the fragrance of flowers. (15.8)
[GITA:16163] Comments: Does an individual soul by itself direct attention
[GITA:16164] towards objects of sense pleasure? This verse is a continuation of the
[GITA:16165] previous verse and states that it is the Lord Almighty resident in living
[GITA:16166] beings who causes pursuit of sense pleasures. The Lord is always present in
[GITA:16167] living beings. When a soul leaves the physical body, the Lord causes the
[GITA:16168] sense organs of perception to travel along with the soul. Sense organs here
[GITA:16169] refer to the ir subtle form and not t he gross organs that one can see in a
[GITA:16170] physical body. The process of the subtle sense organs carried along with a
[GITA:16171] departing soul out of a physical body is compared to a gently blowing wind
[GITA:16172] that carries the fragrance of a flower. No one can see the fragrance  being
[GITA:16173] carried by the wind, but one can smell the fragrance. The flower does not
[GITA:16174] lose its fragrance even though  the wind carried a part of it. In the Brahma
[GITA:16175] Sutra (3-1- 4), it is stated that when a soul leaves the body and the body is
[GITA:16176] consumed by the elements of nature (such as fire), the sense organs also get
[GITA:16177] consumed. How can this be reconciled with the statement that the Lord
[GITA:16178] carries the sense organs alon g with the soul? Sri Rayaru in GV  clarifies by
[GITA:16179] stating that the Lord carries the subtle sense organs (a fraction of  the
[GITA:16191] 346                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:16192] physical sense organs) as per this verse and the Brahma Sutra is referring
[GITA:16193] to the gross sense organs.

[GITA:16214] This verse is identified by Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha in his BGS  as
[GITA:16215] representing the core concepts of this chapter. This verse establishes the
[GITA:16216] relationship between the Lord Almighty, the individual souls, and inert
[GITA:16217] objects (sense organs of all living beings). It also establishes the supremacy

[GITA:16221] objects. While the sense organs of perception are identified here, they are
[GITA:16222] governed by deities whose order of gradatio n was identified previously in

[GITA:16224] recognize this as the core verse for this chapter.

[GITA:16334] drunk. Every food article that one consumes belongs to one o f these
[GITA:16335] categories. The Lord, in the name of Vaishwanara resides in living beings
[GITA:16336] in the form of jatara agni (abdominal fire). Sri Rayaru in GV  clarifies that
[GITA:16337] the deity Mukhya Prana in the forms of prana and apana, powered by the
[GITA:16338] Lord, helps in the process  of food consumption and digestion which
[GITA:16339] includes distribution of energy in food to various parts of the body.

[GITA:16348] I reside in the hearts of all living beings. I am responsible for
[GITA:16349] memory, knowledge, and any loss of knowledge. I am the primary purport
[GITA:16350] of the Vedas. I am the author of Vedanta. I am the only one who knows all
[GITA:16351] the Vedas. (15.15)
[GITA:16353] Comments: This is one of the most important verses in the Gita as it
[GITA:16354] summarizes many of the key teachings related to the attributes and
[GITA:16355] greatness of the Lord. In this verse, the Lord emphatically declares that He
[GITA:16356] is resident in all living beings (within their hearts) and causes them to attain
[GITA:16357] knowledge and lose knowledge. The Vedas are scriptural texts that are
[GITA:16358] vocally passed on from one generation to the next. They are not authored
[GITA:16359] by anyone, human or divine. Various passages in the Vedas superficially
[GITA:16360] appear to propitiate deities such as Agni (fire), Varuna (water) etc. The
[GITA:16361] Lord clarifies here that the Vedas primarily describe Him alone (and
[GITA:16362] describe other deities secondarily). The Lord does not state that He is the
[GITA:16363] author of the Vedas, but states that He is the author of Vedanta. Sri Rayaru
[GITA:16364] in GV clarifies that Vedanta means vedanaamanto nirnayo  (the definitive
[GITA:16365] summary of the Vedas), in other words, the Brahma Sutras . This is
[GITA:16377] 350                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:16378] consistent with the historical fact that the Brahma Sutras were composed
[GITA:16379] by Lord Vedavyasa, wh o is another form of the Lord. Sri Rayaru in GV
[GITA:16380] also quotes the Bhagavata (11.21.42), where Lord Krishna teaches
[GITA:16381] Uddhava that He alone knows the Vedas fully.

[GITA:16386] There are two types of dependent souls in the Universe, kshara and

[GITA:16394] types of dependent individual souls. Living beings are described as kshara
[GITA:16395] as they have perishable physical bodies. Even liberated souls have had
[GITA:16396] perishable bodies previously. The one without  a perishable body ( akshara)
[GITA:16397] is termed kootastha which means space (which is eternal).  This was stated
[GITA:16398] previously in 2.17 . The only dependent, sentient entity in the universe

[GITA:16435] all souls). Sri Rayaru in GV  quotes the Shweta Upanishat (6.13) to

[GITA:16490] O Anagha (Arjuna, the one without sins)! I have taught you the most

[GITA:16492] to have acquire d the ultimate spiritual knowledge  (aparoksha jnana ) and
[GITA:16493] will be liberated. (15.20)
[GITA:16495] Comments: This chapter started with a couple of enigmatic verses

[GITA:16497] unambiguous characterization of the principle of duality. One who clearly
[GITA:16498] understands these confidential principles will attain direct, divine
[GITA:16499] (aparoksha) knowledge and will achieve eternal bliss.
[GITA:16501] These last 5 verses 15.16 – 15.20 unambiguously establish the
[GITA:16502] relationship between the Lord Almighty, individual souls, and the inert
[GITA:16503] universe with the clear conclusion that the Lord Almighty is supreme
[GITA:16504] among and different from all individual souls and inert objects. The term
[GITA:16516] Chapter 15                                                                                                                                       353
[GITA:16518] Purushottama (the supreme personality) is described in these verse s and
[GITA:16519] forms the basis for the title of this wonderful chapter - ‘Purushottama
[GITA:16520] Yoga’. Sri Madhwacharya quotes these 5 verses extensively in his works
[GITA:16521] such as Vishnu Tattva Vinirnaya, Mayavada Khandana, Sadachara
[GITA:16522] Smriti in addition to his two commentaries on the Gita.
[GITA:16524] Summary of Chapter 15
[GITA:16526] This chapter of 20 verses and 700 letters is considered by many to be
[GITA:16527] the most important chapter in the entire Gita, and the one that summarizes
[GITA:16528] all its 700 verses. This chapter is principally concerned with the
[GITA:16529] establishment of the principle of the Lord Almighty’s superiority and hence
[GITA:16530] is termed Purushottama Yoga  where uttama means supreme and purusha
[GITA:16531] means the Being. The relationship between the inert universe, individual
[GITA:16532] souls and the Lord Almighty were previously discu ssed. In this chapter,
[GITA:16533] these fivefold differences are explained with the ex ample of a banyan tree.
[GITA:16534] Verses 15.1 and 15.2  describe the structure of the tree. This description is
[GITA:16535] enigmatic, and one can appreciate the explana tion provided by Sri Rayaru
[GITA:16536] in GV  to help understand the real meaning of these verses. The
[GITA:16537] correspondence between the components of the tree and the entities in the
[GITA:16538] universe are as follows: Earth (supporting the tree) = The Lord Almighty;
[GITA:16539] Roots = Sentient and inert nature; New roots = The t hree qualities of
[GITA:16540] nature; Branches = The five basic elements of nature; Sub -branches =
[GITA:16541] Physical bodies of living beings; Leaves = The Vedas; Flower s,
[GITA:16542] Fruit = Worldly desires, Liberation. Using the analogy of a banyan tree,
[GITA:16543] these two verses appear to illus trate the concepts of gradations among
[GITA:16544] various d eities described previously in 3.42 . Verses 15.3 – 15.5 describe
[GITA:16545] the manner in which a seeker needs to approach the concepts in the Tree of
[GITA:16546] the U niverse to understand the nature of the Lord. Verses 15.6 to 15 .14
[GITA:16547] describe some specific attributes of the Lord such as omnipresence  and
[GITA:16548] omniscience. Verse 15.15  is one of the most famous verses in the Gita in
[GITA:16549] which the Lord emphatically declares His presence in the hearts of all
[GITA:16550] living beings and states that He is k nowable through the Vedas. Verses
[GITA:16551] 15.16 to 15.20  establish the relationship between the Lord Almighty,
[GITA:16563] 354                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:16564] individual souls, and the inert universe with the clear conclusion that the
[GITA:16565] Lord Almighty is supreme among and different from all individual souls
[GITA:16566] and in ert objects. These verses are distinguished by their clarity and
[GITA:16567] simplicity, which is different from the enigmatic nature of the initial few
[GITA:16568] verses. The term Purushottama (the supreme personality) is described in
[GITA:16569] these verses and forms the basis for the ti tle of this wonderful
[GITA:16570] chapter - ‘Purushottama Yoga’.

[GITA:16596] Chapter 16 – The Divine and the Demoniac
[GITA:16598] Chapter Introduction:  This chapter of 24 verses is known as
[GITA:16599] Daivasura Sampat Vibhaga Yoga  (Division of the Divine and the
[GITA:16600] Demoniac). This chapter delves deep into types of human nature. In  the
[GITA:16601] previous chapters, there were  many references to pious, virtuous people
[GITA:16602] with divine nature  and to people with demoniac nature. This c hapter
[GITA:16603] provides more details on human traits. These traits  are intrinsic to an
[GITA:16604] individual. One cannot judge people based on the external appearance,
[GITA:16605] position in society etc . In the pr evious chapter, verse 15.5  described the
[GITA:16606] methods to achieve divine, spiri tual knowledge and liberation. Verse 15.11
[GITA:16607] described those who can achieve self -realization and those who cannot.
[GITA:16608] These are the characteristics of divine and demoniac natures, respectively.
[GITA:16609] Some of these characteri stics were described in verses 9.11 to 9.1 4 also.
[GITA:16610] This chapter provides more details on the divine and demoniac
[GITA:16611] characteristics which help a seeker to inculcate divine attributes and avoid
[GITA:16612] association with demoniac ones. Hence this chapter is a logical extension to
[GITA:16613] the previous chapter.

[GITA:17058] Summary of Chapter 16
[GITA:17060] Some of the characteristics of the divine and the demoniac were
[GITA:17061] described in chapter 9, verses 9.11-14. This chapter provides more details
[GITA:17062] on these characteristics.  People with divine nature s typically exhibit the
[GITA:17063] following traits: honesty, straightforwardne ss, compassion, gentleness,
[GITA:17064] sense control, peace of mind, pleasing personality, helpfulness, anger
[GITA:17065] control, purity in body and mind, charit able nature . These are covered in
[GITA:17066] verses 16.1-3. Those with demoniac nature s are characterized by some of
[GITA:17067] these trait s: arrogance, anger, obstina cy, attachment to worldly pleasures,
[GITA:17068] disrespect towards  teachers and elders, conceit, cruel ty, hypocri sy etc.
[GITA:17069] These are described in verses 16.7 -18. The destination for those with
[GITA:17070] demoniac conduct (a result of their demoniac nature) is described in verses
[GITA:17071] 16.19-21. Verses 16.22-23 describe the methods for one to overcome
[GITA:17072] demoniac tendencies. This chapter concludes in verse 16.24 with Lord
[GITA:17073] Krishna declaring that one needs to resort to the scriptures to discriminate
[GITA:17074] between right and wrong actions.

[GITA:17091] Chapter 17 - The Threefold Faith
[GITA:17093] Chapter Introduction:  This chapter of 28 verses is termed
[GITA:17094] Shraddhatraya Vibhaga Yoga  (The Threefold Faith). In the previous
[GITA:17095] chapters, especially in chapter 14, the nature of individuals influenced by
[GITA:17096] the qualities of sattv, rajas, tamas  was stated in many places. This chapter
[GITA:17097] has more details on the concept of threefold faith. In chapter 14, verse
[GITA:17098] 14.19, it was stated that all activities are influenced by the combination of
[GITA:17099] the three qualities of inert nature and that the Lord Almighty is beyond
[GITA:17100] these attributes and hence is not influenced by them . Everyone has faith or
[GITA:17101] belief about the purpose of life. This belief is born out of t heir innate
[GITA:17102] nature. In this chapter, more details on the impact of the innate qualities of
[GITA:17103] living beings are described , especially on issues such as faith, food habits,
[GITA:17104] austerity, and charitable giving. While chapter 14 dealt with the impact of
[GITA:17105] the three q ualities of nature on living beings, this chapter deals with the
[GITA:17106] three types of faith that are intrinsic to all living beings.
[GITA:17108] The Threefold Faith
[GITA:17110] AOw©Z CdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:17111] `o emó{d{Y_wËg¥Á` `OÝVo lÕ`m@pÝdVm… Ÿ&
[GITA:17112] Vofm§ {Zð>m Vw H$m H¥$îU gÎd_mhmo aOñV_… Ÿ&& 1Ÿ&&
[GITA:17114] Arjuna said: O Krishna! Some worship and perform sacrifices with
[GITA:17115] sincerity, but without knowing scriptural procedures. What is their
[GITA:17116] conviction? Is it sattvic (virtuous), rajasic (passion) or tamasic
[GITA:17117] (ignorance)? (17.1)
[GITA:17119] Comments: In the last verse of the pre vious chapter 16.24, the Lord
[GITA:17120] stated that the scriptures are the guidelights for a seeker to discriminate
[GITA:17121] between right and wrong deeds. Arjuna wants to know about those who do
[GITA:17133] Chapter 17                                                                                                                                          367
[GITA:17135] not know about scriptural procedures. If they perform deeds with sincerity,
[GITA:17136] would they be sattvic, rajasic or tamasic?
[GITA:17138] Outwardly, the phrase śāstravidhim uts ṛjya seems to refer to those
[GITA:17139] who ignore the procedures indicated in  the scriptures. Sri Rayaru in GV
[GITA:17140] based on Sri Madhwacharya’s GB states that this phrase refers to those who
[GITA:17141] do not have knowledge about scriptural procedures. After all, not everyone
[GITA:17142] has access to the scriptures, yet they also perform meditation, charity etc.,
[GITA:17143] based on their belief system. The question that Arjuna is asking is about the
[GITA:17144] nature of their activities. This will be clear after Lord’s response in the next
[GITA:17145] two verses.
[GITA:17147] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:17148] {Ì{dYm ^d{V lÕm Xo{hZm§ gm ñd^mdOm Ÿ&
[GITA:17149] gmpÎdH$s amOgr M¡d Vm_gr Mo{V Vm§ l¥Uw Ÿ&& 2Ÿ&&
[GITA:17151] The Lord said:  Living beings are predisposed (based on their innate
[GITA:17152] nature) into one o f three qualities - sattvic, rajasic or tamasic. Listen to
[GITA:17153] their description. (17.2)
[GITA:17155] Comments: Every soul has  an intrinsic nature that defines its
[GITA:17156] predisposition. The Lord describes such predisposition.
[GITA:17158] gÎdmZwê$nm gd©ñ` lÕm ^d{V ^maV Ÿ&
[GITA:17159] lÕm_`mo@`§ nwéfmo `mo `ÀN´>Õ… g Ed g… Ÿ&& 3 Ÿ&&
[GITA:17161] O Bharata! Everyone’s faith is conditioned according to the innate
[GITA:17162] nature of their soul. Everyone has some faith, and that faith defines one ’s
[GITA:17163] personality. (17.3)
[GITA:17165] Comments: Intrinsic predisposition in living beings defines their
[GITA:17166] faith. It is this  faith that is the basis of one ’s attitudes, personality, and
[GITA:17167] activities. When one is liberated, one’s state will be based on one’s intrinsic
[GITA:17179] 368                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:17180] predisposition (sattvic, rajasic, or tamasic). Sri Rayaru in GV  clarifies that
[GITA:17181] despite one’s intrinsic predisposition, one may exhibit other characteristics
[GITA:17182] to a small extent based on the impact of one’s environment. Intrinsic
[GITA:17183] predisposition in souls is like the feature of magnetism in magnets which
[GITA:17184] naturally attracts iron but no other metals. Magnetism in that sense is an
[GITA:17185] intrinsic quality that cannot be separated from a magnet.  Sri Madinur
[GITA:17186] Vishnu Teertha in his BGS has identified this verse as representing the core
[GITA:17187] concepts in this chapter  as it identifies the root cause that determines one’s
[GITA:17188] faith.

[GITA:17234] Habits of Food, Rituals, Austerity and Charity
[GITA:17236] AmhmañËd{n gd©ñ` {Ì{dYmo ^d{V {à`… Ÿ&
[GITA:17237] `kñVnñVWm XmZ§ Vofm§ ^oX{__§ ewUw Ÿ&& 7 &&
[GITA:17239] Food preferred by living beings are also of three types. Likewise, are
[GITA:17240] sacrificial rituals, austerity , and charitable activities. Listen  to their
[GITA:17241] classification. (17.7)
[GITA:17243] Comments: The innate nature of living beings impact s their lives in
[GITA:17244] terms of food habi ts, perform ance of daily rituals , and even their attitude
[GITA:17245] and approach towards charitable giving. These are explained in detail in
[GITA:17246] verses 17.8 to 17.22.
[GITA:17248] As per  the Chandogya Upanishat  (6.5.1), food items have three
[GITA:17249] components – gross, middle part and subt le part. The gross part is normally
[GITA:17250] excreted, the middle part gives nourishment to the body and the subtle part
[GITA:17251] impacts the mind. Hence, the type of foo d consumed not only impacts one s
[GITA:17252] physical health, but also has an impact on one’s mental health.
[GITA:17254] Types of Food Habits
[GITA:17256] Am`w…gÎd~bmamo½`gwIàr{V{ddY©Zm… Ÿ&
[GITA:17257] añ`m… िèन½Ym… pñWam öÚm Amhmam… gmpÎdH${à`m… Ÿ&& 8 &&
[GITA:17270] 370                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:17271] Sattvic (virtuous) people like food items that are pleasant,
[GITA:17272] nourishing, sweet, tasty, and are easy to digest. They enhance longevity,
[GITA:17273] vitality, and health, and induce happiness and good nature. (17.8)
[GITA:17275] Comments: ‘You are what you eat’ is a famous saying which
[GITA:17276] indicates that ones nature is defined by one ’s food habits. Those wi th
[GITA:17277] sattvic nature prefer food items that promote health and longevity. These
[GITA:17278] food items are endowed with four basic characteristics which make them
[GITA:17279] tasty (rasyāḥ), juicy (snigdhāḥ), nourishing (sthirā), and hearty (hṛdyā). An
[GITA:17280] example of nourishing (sthirā) food is ghee which stays in the blood stream
[GITA:17281] for a long-time giving strength to the individual. Hearty ( hṛdyā) food items
[GITA:17282] are those (ex: sweet dishes) whi ch not only give joy while they are
[GITA:17283] consumed but also create craving. Moderate amount s of such healthy, tasty
[GITA:17284] food promote health  and wellbeing, and induce good nature. Sri
[GITA:17285] Vidyasagara Madhava  Teertha gives the example of a lamp that requires
[GITA:17286] both the wick  (batti) and ghee/oil to give light. Similarly, a body needs
[GITA:17287] ghee for nourishment which helps to light one’s intellect.
[GITA:17289] H$Q²d>måbbdUmË`wîUVrúUê$j{dXm{hZ… Ÿ&
[GITA:17290] Amhmam amOgñ`oï>m Xw…IemoH$m_`àXm… Ÿ&& 9 &&
[GITA:17292] Rajasic (passionate) people like food items that are extremely
[GITA:17293] bitter/spicy, acidic, salty, hot, pungent , sour, and burnt. These result in
[GITA:17294] misery and discomfort at the time of consumption, and disease later. (17.9)
[GITA:17296] Comments: This verse describes the food habits of the rajasic.
[GITA:17297] While food items which are sou r, salty e tc., are also essential for one ’s
[GITA:17298] wellbeing, they need to be consumed in moderation. When consumed in
[GITA:17299] excess (atī), they result in misery at the time of consumption. Long term ill
[GITA:17300] effects include onset of diseases. For example, while salt is an essential
[GITA:17301] source of sodium for the body, excess intake of salt over a prolonged period
[GITA:17302] is known to result in high blood pr essure. Sri Rayaru in GV  clarifies that
[GITA:17303] these food items when consumed in moderation and without resulting in
[GITA:17304] discomfort or disease, can be considered sattvic.
[GITA:17316] Chapter 17                                                                                                                                          371
[GITA:17318] `mV`m_§ JVag§ ny{V n`w©{fV§ M `V² Ÿ&
[GITA:17319] CpÀN>ï>_{n Mm_oÜ`§ ^moOZ§ Vm_g{à`_² Ÿ&& 10 &&
[GITA:17321] Tamasic (demoniac) people like food items that are stale,
[GITA:17322] decomposed, foul, leftover, leavings of others, and impure. (17.10)
[GITA:17324] Comments: This verse describes the types of food items that appeal
[GITA:17325] to the tamasic. Impure food items include prohibited  ones such as alcohol.
[GITA:17326] These food items are unhealthy regardless of the amount that is consumed.
[GITA:17328] Types of Ritual Sacrifices
[GITA:17330] A\$bmH$m{¬{^`©kmo {d{YÑï>mo ` BÁ`Vo Ÿ&
[GITA:17331] `ï>ì`_odo{V _Z… g_mYm` g gmpÎdH$… Ÿ&& 11 &&

[GITA:17339] Ritual sacrifices, performed whole heartedly as per the scriptures and

[GITA:17342] O Superior among the Bharatas! Ritual sacrifices performed with

[GITA:17366] Those with tamasic natures perform such rituals with ulterior motives and
[GITA:17367] never donate to those less fortunate.

[GITA:17500] Concept of Om, Tat, Sat
[GITA:17502] ›  VËg{X{V {ZX}emo ~«÷U{ó{dY… ñ_¥V… Ÿ&
[GITA:17503] ~«m÷UmñVoZ doXmü `kmü {d{hVm… nwam Ÿ&& 23 &&
[GITA:17505] In the scriptures, the Lord is addressed with three principal names -
[GITA:17506] Om (omnipresent), Tat (one who is known indirec tly, through the Vedas)
[GITA:17507] and Sat (full of infinite auspicious attributes). The Lord made available the
[GITA:17508] Vedas and Vedic sacrifices and powered the intellect of priests to perform
[GITA:17509] them. (17.23)
[GITA:17511] Comments: Sattvic living beings perform all their activities,
[GITA:17512] especially ritual sacrifices, austerity, and charitable giving as a worship and
[GITA:17513] offering to the Lord. It is important for one to remember the Lord before
[GITA:17514] undertaking such activities. The next four verses state that the scriptures
[GITA:17515] address the Lord with three  succinct, yet powerful adjectives, Om, Tat and
[GITA:17516] Sat. These have special meanings. Om which is derived from ‘ otam
[GITA:17517] protaha’ refers to the one who indwells (and supports) the universe. Tat
[GITA:17518] means one who pervades  the Gunas ( qualities). It also means one who
[GITA:17519] cannot be comprehended by the sense organs and can only be known
[GITA:17520] through the scriptures. Sat refers to the Lord who is devoid of any defects
[GITA:17521] and is full of infinite, auspicious attributes.
[GITA:17523] Vñ_mXmo{_Ë`wXmöË` `kXmZVn…{H«$`m… Ÿ&
[GITA:17524] àdV©ÝVo {dYmZmoº$m… gVV§ ~«÷dm{XZm_² Ÿ&& 24 &&
[GITA:17526] V{XË`Z{^g§Ym` \$b§ `kVn…{H«$`m… Ÿ&
[GITA:17527] XmZ{H«$`mü {d{dYm… {H«$`ÝVo _mojH$m{¬{^… Ÿ&& 25 &&
[GITA:17529] gØmdo gmYw^mdo M g{XË`oVËà`wÁ`Vo Ÿ&
[GITA:17530] àeñVo H$_©{U VWm gÀN>ãX… nmW© `wÁ`Vo Ÿ&& 26 &&
[GITA:17543] 376                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:17544] Hence, the activities of ritual sacrifice, austerity, and charity
[GITA:17545] performed as per the scriptures are always initiated by invoking the
[GITA:17546] primordial syllable ‘Om’, as a prayer to the Lord Almighty. (17.24)
[GITA:17548] Those desirous of achieving eternal bliss and not interested in
[GITA:17549] temporary heavenly pleasures perform sacrifices, penances, and charity as
[GITA:17550] an offering to the Lord described by the word ‘ Tat’, as one who is to be
[GITA:17551] understood indirectly (through the scriptures). (17.25)
[GITA:17553] O Partha! The Lord’s name, ‘Sat’, is used to represent existence and
[GITA:17554] goodness. It is also used to denote auspicious activities. (17.26)
[GITA:17556] Comments: These three verses describe the impact of invoking the
[GITA:17557] Lord’s names Om, Tat, Sat at the time of performing activities such as
[GITA:17558] ritual sacrifices, austerity, and charitable giving. Invoking the Lord’s name
[GITA:17559] Om, ensures th at these activities will be rendered sattvic. Before chanting
[GITA:17560] any hymn, one must precede it with Om, which renders the hymn fruitful.
[GITA:17561] Likewise, one must complete chanting of hymns with Om in the end, else
[GITA:17562] any blessings that would accrue from the hymn would be lost.
[GITA:17564] When one invokes the Lord’s name Tat, one is reminded that the
[GITA:17565] Lord is knowable indirectly (through the scriptures) and that one should
[GITA:17566] perform activities without expectations of temporary rewards.
[GITA:17568] Invoking the Lord’s name Sat will remind a seeker to be aware of the
[GITA:17569] Lord’s infinite, auspicious attributes, and activities such as the creation of
[GITA:17570] the universe.
[GITA:17572] In summary, invoking the phrase Om, Tat, Sat  at the time of
[GITA:17573] performing virtuous activities will help a seeker develop a virtuous attitude
[GITA:17574] and approach to them.

[GITA:17595] The strong conviction that one has in performing sacrifices, p enances

[GITA:17599] O Partha! Sacrifices performed, charity given, and austerities

[GITA:17608] offering to the Lord will indeed help a seeker reach the Lord’s abode.
[GITA:17609] Activities that are performed with ulterior mo tives for societal recognition,
[GITA:17610] without following scriptural procedures and without offering to the Lord
[GITA:17611] are inauspicious and will neither help in this world nor in afterlife. Hence
[GITA:17612] faith and sincerity are very essential when performing activities.
[GITA:17614] Summary of Chapter 17
[GITA:17616] In this chapter the Lord identifies the three divisions of faith - sattvic,
[GITA:17617] rajasic and tamasic which influence the attitudes and activities of living
[GITA:17618] beings. These attributes are innate ( swabhava) to individual souls. The
[GITA:17619] impact of these attributes on activities such as worship, food habits, ritual
[GITA:17620] sacrifices, austerity, and charitable services are described. Verses 17.4 to
[GITA:17621] 17.7 describe the mode of propiti ation of living beings. Verses 17.8 to
[GITA:17633] 378                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:17634] 17.10 describe food habits. V erses 17.11 to 1 7.13 identify ritual sacrifices
[GITA:17635] based on one’s innate attributes. Verses 17.14 to 17.19  describe one’s
[GITA:17636] approach to austerity and meditation. Verses 17.20 to 17.22  address the
[GITA:17637] issue of charitable giving. Verses 17.23 to 17.27 describe the approach
[GITA:17638] towards ritual sacrifices and penance performed by sattvic beings desirous
[GITA:17639] of moksha, with special explanation on Om, Tat, and Sat, the three principal
[GITA:17640] names of the Lord Almighty.

[GITA:17659] Chapter 18 - Liberation and Renunciation
[GITA:17661] Chapter Introduction:  This c hapter of 78 verses  is termed
[GITA:17662] Mokshasanyasa Yoga  (Liberation and Renunciation) . It starts with a
[GITA:17663] discussion on the subtle differences between renunciation ( sanyasa) and
[GITA:17664] relinquishment of rewards  from labour ( tyaga). The types of rewards from
[GITA:17665] actions are also discussed. The five prerequisites of performing any action
[GITA:17666] are identified. Different types of knowledge, action, doers, intellect,
[GITA:17667] determination, and happiness are also discussed. Additional details are
[GITA:17668] provided on four societal categories of people which were briefly indicated
[GITA:17669] in 4.13 . The concept of liberation ( moksha) is discussed  in detail  in this
[GITA:17670] chapter. The first 55 verses contain discussion s on the topics identified so
[GITA:17671] far. The Lord co ncludes His sermon in the next 17 verses. Arjuna responds
[GITA:17672] to Lord Krishna’s entire teaching in verse 73. Sanjaya, who has been
[GITA:17673] describing the proceedings in the war to King Dhrutarashtra  concludes his
[GITA:17674] commentary in the remaining 5 verses. Arjuna starts by requesting Krishna
[GITA:17675] to explain the difference between renunciation ( sanyasa) and
[GITA:17676] relinquishment  (tyaga) as both seem to imply the same. The Lord provides
[GITA:17677] answers to Arjuna’s questions with a detailed description of the various
[GITA:17678] aspects of renunciation and r elinquishment. This chapter expands on the
[GITA:17679] concept of doership, provides more details on  the influence of the three
[GITA:17680] qualities of nature and gives additional explanation on societal categories.
[GITA:17681] There is further an elaborate discussion on the methods to achieve salvation
[GITA:17682] (moksha). The Lord also describes the glory of the Gita.

[GITA:17702] Arjuna said:  O Krishna, Mighty Armed One! O Hri shikesha! O
[GITA:17703] Slayer of Demon Keshi!  I would like to understand the difference between
[GITA:17704] renunciation and relinquishment. (18.1)
[GITA:17706] Comments: In verse 5.2, it was stated that renunciation ( sanyāsa) is
[GITA:17707] essential to attain liberation ( moksha), and in verse 12.12  relinquishment
[GITA:17708] (tyāga) was lauded as a superior means to attain liberation ( moksha).
[GITA:17709] Arjuna wants to know the  difference between these two approaches. The
[GITA:17710] Lord provides a detailed response to Arjuna in verses 18.2 to 18.12.
[GITA:17712] lr^JdmZwdmM Ÿ&

[GITA:17719] The Lord said:  Learned ones say that renunciation is the
[GITA:17720] abandonment of activities performed for the sake of desired outcomes. The
[GITA:17721] experienced say that relinquishment is forsaking of fruits of any action.
[GITA:17722] (18.2)
[GITA:17724] The wise declare that engaging in desire ridden activities should  be
[GITA:17725] relinquished as they entangle a soul. Others say that one should never
[GITA:17726] abandon activities such as ritual sacrifice, charity, and penance. (18.3)
[GITA:17728] Comments: The Lord identifies four principles in these verses – (i)
[GITA:17729] abandonment of activities performed for mundane desires (ii) forsaking any
[GITA:17730] rewards from action (except the lofty goal of earning the Lord’s grace) (iii)
[GITA:17731] abandonment of activities which entangle one , and (iv) non -abandonment
[GITA:17732] of prescribed activities of ritual sacrifices, charity, and aust erity. Sri
[GITA:17733] Madhwacharya in GB and GTN  clarifies that all these principles are
[GITA:17734] required for one to make progress in one’s spiritual journey. The use of
[GITA:17746] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           381
[GITA:17748] terms ‘ kavayo’ (learned ones), ‘ vicakṣaṇāḥ’ (the experienced),
[GITA:17749] and‘manīṣiṇaḥ’ ( the wise) to describe the propon ents of these four
[GITA:17750] principles is proof that all four are desirable qualities in a seeker.

[GITA:17764]  As per verse 18.2, relinquishment is forsaking rewards of activities.
[GITA:17765]  As will be seen in verse 18.6, relinquishment is forsaking ownership
[GITA:17766] in activities.
[GITA:17767]  As will be seen in verse 18.17, relinquishment is not assuming
[GITA:17768] independent doership in activities.

[GITA:17792] One should never abandon performing prescribe d ritual sacrifices,

[GITA:17809] ascetics, is donating their time and knowledge to those in need. Austerity ,
[GITA:17810] for ascetics , is observing strict rituals such as celibacy, fasting etc. Those
[GITA:17811] who do not have access to Vedic knowledge perform ritual sacrifice in the
[GITA:17812] form of prayers and bhajans  on the Lord, and austerity for them is being
[GITA:17813] truthful, fasting etc.

[GITA:17839] Renouncing prescribed duties is never appropriate. Avoiding such
[GITA:17840] actions out of ignorance is tamasic. (18.7)
[GITA:17842] Abandonment of  prescribed duties under  the pretext of stress and
[GITA:17843] physical difficulty is rajasic. No one can earn the Lord’s grace through
[GITA:17844] such renunciation. (18.8)
[GITA:17846] O Arjuna! Performing prescribed duties without attachment to
[GITA:17847] actions and without expectations is sattvic renunciation. (18.9)
[GITA:17849] Comments: In these verses, the Lord identifies the types of
[GITA:17850] renunciation practice d by different people , based on their intrinsic nature.
[GITA:17851] Some completely ignore performing prescribed duties out of ignorance or
[GITA:17852] false knowledge. Such renunciation is tamasic (nescient). There are so me
[GITA:17853] who are aware of their prescribed duties but find excuses such as bodily
[GITA:17854] discomfort to avoid doing them. Their abandonment is rajasic and does not
[GITA:17855] earn the Lord’s grace. The sattvic consider their prescribed duties as an
[GITA:17856] obligation and perform them without attachment and expectations. Their
[GITA:17857] renunciation of attachment to activities and rewards is sattvic and is to be
[GITA:17858] followed by everyone.

[GITA:17883] A sattvic renouncer is one who neither despises unpl easant activities
[GITA:17884] nor craves for pleasant activities, one who offers all activities to the Lord,
[GITA:17885] one who is pious by nature, one who has understood the Lord, and one who
[GITA:17886] has no doubts about the nature of the Lord and the Universe. (18.10)
[GITA:17888] One with a physi cal body can never completely renounce all
[GITA:17889] activities (as even breathing is an activity). One who has relinquished the
[GITA:17890] fruits of labour is the ideal tyagi. (18.11)
[GITA:17892] Those who perform activities with expectations will experience
[GITA:17893] either pleasant, or unpleasa nt, or mixed rewards after they leave this world.
[GITA:17894] This does not apply to those who perform duties without expectations.
[GITA:17895] (18.12)
[GITA:17897] Comments: These three verses provide more details on the
[GITA:17898] characteristics of renunciation based on the nature and approach of  the
[GITA:17899] seeker.  As per Rayaru in GV, verse 18.10  identifies five characteristics of
[GITA:17900] a sattvic renunciant as one who (i) does not abandon prescribed duties that
[GITA:17901] may be momentarily unpleasant, (ii) does not crave for activities that may
[GITA:17902] be momentarily pleasant, ( iii) has a pious nature, (iv) has understood
[GITA:17903] properly the Lord’s prowess, and (v) has no doubts regarding the
[GITA:17904] distinction between the universe and the Lord Almighty. Verse 18.11
[GITA:17905] counters a position that some hold that a ren ouncer should forsake all
[GITA:17906] activities. This verse states that for a living being , it is impossible to
[GITA:17907] forsake all activities, as even breathing is a type of activity. An ideal
[GITA:17908] renouncer is one who forsakes the rewards from actions and  not actions
[GITA:17909] themselves. Verse 18.12  explains the distin ction between a seeker who
[GITA:17910] performs activit ies with expectations o f   rewards and one who performs
[GITA:17911] prescribed duties with no expectations. The former one experience s three
[GITA:17912] different types of destinations in afterlife: downfall, heavenly rewards, and
[GITA:17913] rebirth in this world (depending on the approach and nature of their
[GITA:17914] activities such as tamasic, sattvic, rajasic ). However, one who performs
[GITA:17915] prescribed duties forsaking rewards will not experience these types of
[GITA:17916] destinations. Sri Rayaru in GV clarifies that tho se seekers who have
[GITA:17928] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           385
[GITA:17930] achieved self -realization and do not have any obligations to perform
[GITA:17931] activities, will achieve higher bliss in salvation depending on the extent of
[GITA:17932] their activities.  As indicated in 18.2 , renunciation is the abandonment of
[GITA:17933] activities performed for the sake of desired outcomes, and relinquishment is
[GITA:17934] forsaking of fruits of any action. Superior seekers who have achieved
[GITA:17935] self-realization have both these ch aracteristics (renunciation and
[GITA:17936] relinquishment).
[GITA:17938] Pre-requisites for Activities
[GITA:17940] n#m¡Vm{Z _hm~mhmo H$maUm{Z {Z~moY _o Ÿ&
[GITA:17941] gm§»`o H¥$VmÝVo àmoº$m{Z {gÕ`o gd©H$_©Um_² Ÿ&& 13 &&
[GITA:17943] A{Yð>mZ§ VWm H$Vm© H$aU§ M n¥Wp½dY_² Ÿ&
[GITA:17944] {d{dYmü n¥WŠMoï>m X¡d§ M¡dmÌ n#m__² Ÿ&& 14 &&
[GITA:17946] earadmL²>‘Zmo{^`©V² H$_© àma^Vo Za… Ÿ&
[GITA:17947] Ý`mæ`§ dm {dnarV§ dm n#m¡Vo Vñ` hoVd… Ÿ&& 15 &&
[GITA:17949] O Arjuna, Mighty Armed One! There are five pre -requisites for
[GITA:17950] completion of any activity as enumerated in the Sankhya scripture. Learn
[GITA:17951] them from Me. (18.13)
[GITA:17953] They are as follows - the place for conducting activity (such as body,
[GITA:17954] earth), the performer (human, divine), the apparatus (sense organs, fire),
[GITA:17955] resulting rituals (meditation, prayer) and divinity (the Lord ). (18.14)
[GITA:17957] Whatever activity one performs through the body or the mind or
[GITA:17958] speech, whether it is right or wrong, that activity will require  the above five
[GITA:17959] pre-requisites for completion. (18.15)
[GITA:17961] Comments: As performance of activities is mandatory for everyone,
[GITA:17962] it is important to understand the prerequisites for performing them. These
[GITA:17963] verses identify the five prerequisites for action. Sri Raya ru in GV clarifies
[GITA:17975] 386                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:17976] that these are as per the Sankhya scripture which was composed by the
[GITA:17977] Lord in the form of Kapila . Verse 18.14 identifies the five prerequisites ,
[GITA:17978] and verse 18.15 clarifies that these five prerequisites are essential for
[GITA:17979] performing any activity, be it physical, vocal, or mental.
[GITA:17981] The concept of prerequisites for activities can be illustrated with an
[GITA:17982] example. Let us take the case of a seeker practicing meditation ( dhyana).
[GITA:17983] Following are the five prerequisites –
[GITA:17985] (i)      place = physical body
[GITA:17986] (ii)      performer = living being (dependent performer)
[GITA:17987] (iii) apparatus = living being’s mind
[GITA:17988] (iv) resulting ritual = focusing the mind
[GITA:17989] (v)      divinity = Lord Almighty (who powers everyone’s actions).
[GITA:17991] For example , in the case of one cooking rice, these five aspects
[GITA:17992] are – place (kitchen), performer (cook), apparatus ( utensils, stove),
[GITA:17993] resulting ritual (rice), and divinity (Lord who powers this activity).
[GITA:17995] Awareness of Doership
[GITA:17997] VÌ¡d§ g{V H$Vm©a_² AmË_mZ§ Ho$db§ Vw `… Ÿ&
[GITA:17998] ní`Ë`H¥$V~w{ÕËdmÞ g ní`{V Xw_©{V… Ÿ&& 16 &&
[GITA:18000] `ñ` Zmh§H¥$Vmo ^mdmo ~w{Õ`©ñ` Z {bß`Vo Ÿ&

[GITA:18003] Hence the unwise one, who foolishly considers  self to be the sole
[GITA:18004] performer of any action, is indeed devoid of proper knowledge. (18.16)
[GITA:18006] One who is not under the delusion of being the sole performer and
[GITA:18007] has no expectation on the outcome of action, will not be termed a killer
[GITA:18008] even if that person has killed while performing prescribed duties. Such a
[GITA:18009] person is not tainted with any sin. (18.17)
[GITA:18021] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           387
[GITA:18023] Comments: These two verses amplify t he need for one to be aware
[GITA:18024] of the concept of doership. As there are five clear prerequisites for the
[GITA:18025] creation of  any activity, no one should be under the delusion of sol e,
[GITA:18026] independent doership. Verse 18.17  goes a step further and states that a
[GITA:18027] seeker who is not under the delusion of independent doership and performs
[GITA:18028] prescribed activities with no expectations of rewards , will not be tainted by
[GITA:18029] any sin, even if that activity involve s destruction of population. This
[GITA:18030] statement can raise issues as to how one ca n be absolved of great sins that
[GITA:18031] normally accompany such destructive activities. Sri Rayaru in GV based on
[GITA:18032] Sri Madhwacharya’s GB and Sri Jaya Teertha’s PD  clarifies this concept
[GITA:18033] with concrete examples. Lord Rudra (who governs the act of universe’s
[GITA:18034] dissolution) and Lord Yama (the deity of death) are associated with
[GITA:18035] destruction. However, these deities perform these activities as directed by
[GITA:18036] the independent, omniscient Lord Almighty and have no delusion that they
[GITA:18037] are performing these on their own. Hence , they are not tainted by any sin.
[GITA:18038] However, deity Indra who kills Vrutasura , was tainted with some sin as his
[GITA:18039] actions were accompanied by ego.
[GITA:18041] Concept of Doership
[GITA:18043] kmZ§ ko`§ n[akmVm {Ì{dYm H$_©MmoXZm Ÿ&
[GITA:18044] H$aU§ H$_© H$V}{V {Ì{dY… H$_©g§J«h… Ÿ&& 18 &&
[GITA:18046] The motivations for any activity are three-fold - knowledge about the
[GITA:18047] activity (jnana), effort (prayatna), and the performer of the activity (jeeva).
[GITA:18048] The three main pre -requisites for any activity are - the apparatus, the
[GITA:18049] resulting ritual, and the doer. (18.18)
[GITA:18051] Comments: This verse describes the concept of doership where the
[GITA:18052] motivations for performing any activity are indicated, along with the
[GITA:18053] prerequisites fo r such activities. While verse 18.14  described the five
[GITA:18054] prerequisites for performing any activity, these five are summarized into 3
[GITA:18055] types – the apparatus  (which combines the place of operation and the
[GITA:18056] material utilities) , the resulting ritual and the doer  (which combines the
[GITA:18068] 388                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:18069] independent doer and divinity , both referring to the Lord Almighty) . In
[GITA:18070] addition to the pr erequisites that are essential for one to perform any
[GITA:18071] activity, one also needs motivation to engage in that activity. This verse
[GITA:18072] identifies the 3 motivators as – knowledge about the activity to be
[GITA:18073] performed (jnana), effort  (prayatna) that one needs to put in and the
[GITA:18074] performer of the activity  (jeeva). The performer of the activity is the living
[GITA:18075] individual who acts based on the power granted by the Lord. The individual
[GITA:18076] being is not an independent doer but acts under the control and supervision
[GITA:18077] of the independent Lord. The concept of doership is ex plained in detail by
[GITA:18078] Rayaru in GV based on Sri Madhwacharya’s GB and GTN . This topic was
[GITA:18079] covered previously in comments for verse 5.14.
[GITA:18081] One of the questions that arises is about prescribed duties mandated
[GITA:18082] in the scr iptures. Do they apply to the Lord, individual souls, or inert
[GITA:18083] matter? Sri Rayaru in GV  explains that by the process of elimination, one
[GITA:18084] can conclude that prescribed duties apply only to individuals. This is
[GITA:18085] because inert matter cannot act, and the Lord Almighty has no obligation or
[GITA:18086] mandate to act  (verse 3.22). Now, one can question the feasibility of a
[GITA:18087] living being as a doer, while the real doer is described as the Lord
[GITA:18088] Almighty. Sri Rayaru clarifies that while the Lord is the independent doer ,
[GITA:18089] living beings are dependent doers. In this sense, the mandates prescribed in
[GITA:18090] the scriptures apply to living beings who can perform activities based on
[GITA:18091] the material strength and powers granted to them by the Lord.  If the Lord
[GITA:18092] as the independent doer is responsible for  all activities, what is the role of
[GITA:18093] living beings? Living beings have an intrinsic intent ( iccha) to achieve
[GITA:18094] salvation which leads them to make attempts (prayatna). By the grace of
[GITA:18095] the Lord, they are given the ability to perform actions. Hence, living bei ngs
[GITA:18096] are responsible for their actions.
[GITA:18098] kmZ§ H$_© M H$Vm© M {ÌY¡d JwU^oXV… Ÿ&
[GITA:18099] àmoÀ`Vo JwUg§»`mZo `WmdÀN¥>Uw VmÝ`{n Ÿ&& 19 &&
[GITA:18112] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           389
[GITA:18114] As per Sankhya scriptures, knowledge, activity, and the doer are of
[GITA:18115] three types and are differentiated based on their natural attr ibutes. Listen to
[GITA:18116] the explanation with attention. (18.19)
[GITA:18118] Comments: After having described the prerequisites for actions and
[GITA:18119] the concepts of doership, the Lord provides  a detailed explanation on the
[GITA:18120] categories of the three aspects of action – knowledge, resulting activity, and
[GITA:18121] the doer. These aspects are influenced by the three qualities of nature,
[GITA:18122] namely sattv, rajas, and tamas. The Lord also states the scriptural basis for
[GITA:18123] this classification as Vedic Sankhya.

[GITA:18138] states that He is present in everyone’s hearts. Hence, the reference in this
[GITA:18139] verse to the entity residing in everyone , the Lord Almighty Himself. The
[GITA:18140] concept describe d in this verse  was also stated previously in 13.17 and
[GITA:18141] 5.18.

[GITA:18410] Happiness arising out of the interaction between the sense organs
[GITA:18411] and the objects of gratification, which initially feels like nectar and turns
[GITA:18412] out to be poisonous in the end, is rajasic. (18.38)
[GITA:18414] Happiness arising out of excessive sleep, lethargy, and forgetfulness,

[GITA:18418] happiness. Rajasic happiness is that which is experienced bodily through
[GITA:18419] the sense organs. This excludes the happiness one feels during deep sleep
[GITA:18420] (sushupti) as one does not have awareness  of sense objects in this state.
[GITA:18421] Examples of tamasic happiness are those experienced due to indulgence in
[GITA:18433] 396                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:18434] prohibited substance s which are known to be addictive  as well as
[GITA:18435] unhealthy.

[GITA:18455] example, deities have a higher proportion of sattv. Sages have a mixture of
[GITA:18456] sattv and rajas. Ancestral deities ( pitrus) and heavenly musicians

[GITA:18458] categorization among  deities based on their innate nature was addressed

[GITA:18644] verses 14.3, 14.27 and 18.54 . As this chapter is about renunciation and
[GITA:18645] liberation, the Lord d escribes the sequential steps for attaining liberation

[GITA:18648] is to attain the abode of Mahalakshmi, and finally reach the abode of the

[GITA:18661] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           401

[GITA:18664] Mahalakshmi.

[GITA:18710] without any material expectations.

[GITA:18830] O Arjuna! The omnipotent Lord, residing in the hearts of all
[GITA:18831] machine-like bodies of living beings, propels them to perform various
[GITA:18832] activities through His own free will. (18.61)

[GITA:18846] Comments: In the previous verses the Lord stated that one achieves
[GITA:18847] liberation through His grace. In this verse , the Lord goes a step further and
[GITA:18848] states that He is present in the hearts of all living beings  and propels them
[GITA:18849] into action. The Lord uses the word ‘yantrā’ (machine) to describe  the
[GITA:18850] physical bodies of living beings. Just as a machine relies on an engine for
[GITA:18851] running, every physical body depends on its heart for proper functioning.
[GITA:18852] The Lord states that He resides in the hearts  of all living beings . This
[GITA:18853] concept was also discussed in verse 15.15 , where the Lord had state d that
[GITA:18854] He resides in everyone’s hearts.
[GITA:18856] Sri Vidyamanya Teertha in his GPM  states that this single verse can
[GITA:18857] be considered to contain the core principles of the entire Gita on the basis
[GITA:18858] of the logic  of ‘sthalee pulaka nyaya ’ (where one needs to examine only
[GITA:18859] one grain of rice to verify if the entire pot of rice is cooked).

[GITA:18904] contemplating on them. This will be clear after a review of Arjuna’s
[GITA:18905] response in 18.73 where he states that he would act as per Krishna’s words
[GITA:18906] (kariṣye vacanaṁ tava) and not as per his own wishes.
[GITA:18908] gd©JwøV_§ ^y`… e¥Uw _o na_§ dM… &
[GITA:18909] Bï>mo@{g _o ÑT>{_{V VVmo dú`m{_ Vo {hV_² Ÿ&& 64 &&
[GITA:18911] Listen to some more of this Supreme principle which is extremely
[GITA:18912] confidential. I am continuing My supreme teaching to you as you are very
[GITA:18913] dear to Me. (18.64)
[GITA:18915] Comments: After having concluded His teachings on the ways and
[GITA:18916] means ( prameya = principles) for one to traverse the spiritual path, the
[GITA:18917] Lord now gives Arjuna the concrete steps ( sadhana = actions) that he needs
[GITA:18918] to take to achieve success here and hereafter.  Previously in 12.20, the Lord
[GITA:18919] has identified the characteristics of a devotee who is dear to Him. By
[GITA:18920] declaring in this verse that Arjuna is dear to Him, the Lord is confirming
[GITA:18921] that Arjuna has all the desirable traits of an ideal devotee.

[GITA:18939] The Ultimate Commandment
[GITA:18941] _Ý_Zm ^d _Øº$mo _ÚmOr _m§ Z_ñHw$é Ÿ&
[GITA:18942] _m_od¡î`{g gË`§ Vo à{VOmZo {à`mo@{g _o Ÿ&& 65 &&
[GITA:18944] As you are dear to Me, i mmerse your mind in Me. Place your
[GITA:18945] devotion in Me . Propitiate only Me. Prostrate before Me. I promis e you
[GITA:18946] truthfully that you will reach My abode. (18.65)
[GITA:18948] Comments: The Lord instructs Arjuna to worship only Him with the
[GITA:18949] four-way procedure – through the mind, through devotion, through
[GITA:18950] propitiation and through salutation. By using the word ‘satyaṁ’, the Lord is
[GITA:18951] assuring Arjuna that there should not be any doubt in his mind about him
[GITA:18952] achieving liberation.
[GITA:18954] Sri Madinur Vishnu Teertha in BGS  has identified this verse as
[GITA:18955] containing the essence of this entire chapter. Arjuna was asking for specifi c
[GITA:18956] directions from Krishna as he was indecisive about the war. In this verse,
[GITA:18957] the Lord specifically directs Arjuna to worship Him through the four -way
[GITA:18958] procedure and confirms that Arjuna would achieve moksha following this
[GITA:18959] path. Hence this verse can be consi dered as the core verse of this chapter
[GITA:18960] (which is known as moksha sanyasa yoga).
[GITA:18962] gd©Y_m©Z² n[aË`Á` _m_oH§$ eaU§ d«O Ÿ&
[GITA:18963] Ah§ Ëdm gd©nmnoä`mo _moj{`î`m{_ _m ewM… Ÿ&& 66 &&
[GITA:18965] Renounce all activities (not related to the Lord  or performed with
[GITA:18966] expectations of te mporary rewards) completely and surrender exclusively
[GITA:18967] to Me. I will liberate you from  all your sins and grant you bliss. Do not
[GITA:18968] lament. (18.66)
[GITA:18970] Comments: This is a continuation of the previous verse where the
[GITA:18971] Lord had instructed Arjuna to engage in exclusive four-way worship of
[GITA:18972] Him. One should not interpret ‘sarvadharmān parityajya’ to mean that one
[GITA:18984] 408                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:18985] should renounce all activities. The Lord had instructed Arjuna many times
[GITA:18986] to focus on performing the prescribed duty of waging the war (verse s
[GITA:18987] (2.37), (4.42), (11.33)) . Also, Sri Madhwacharya in GB  reminds one that
[GITA:18988] the Lo rd Himself had stated in verse 18.11  that re nouncing activities
[GITA:18989] (tyaga)  mean relinquishing rewards from activities.
[GITA:18991] Sri Vidyesha Teertha in his book, Prana Tattva in the Gita [GPH],
[GITA:18992] provides an alternate interpretation for this verse based on the word
[GITA:18993] derivation of ‘māmekaṁ’ as ma + me + kam , where ma = do not; me = to
[GITA:18994] Me, ka = Vayudeva. In comments to verse 11.40 , it was indicated that the
[GITA:18995] word ‘sarva’ also refers to the Lord Almighty (based on the Lord’s
[GITA:18996] attribute of omnipresence) and this interpretation is supporte d by
[GITA:18997] Upanishads and Vishnu Sahasra Nama . Hence, sarva dharma  refers to
[GITA:18998] Dharmic activities related to the Lord. The reference to the deity Vayudeva
[GITA:18999] here is in recognition of his status as supreme among all living beings
[GITA:19000] (jivas). In comments to verse 1.31, Sri Rayaru in GV  interpreted the word
[GITA:19001] ‘keshava’, referring to Lord Krishna as one who controls even deities ‘ ka’
[GITA:19002] (Brahma, Vayudeva) and ‘ isha’ (Rudra). Now, w ith th e above word
[GITA:19003] derivation for ‘ māmekaṁ’, verse 18.66 can also be interpreted as
[GITA:19004] follows – “Do not renounce Dharmic activities (related to the Lord) ,
[GITA:19005] surrender to Vayudeva and Me. I will liberate you from all your sins and
[GITA:19006] grant you bliss. Do not lament”.
[GITA:19008] Eligibility for Studying the Gita
[GITA:19010] BX§ Vo ZmVnñH$m` Zm^º$m` H$XmMZ Ÿ&
[GITA:19011] Z Mmewlyfdo dmÀ`§ Z M _m§ `mo@ä`gy`{V Ÿ&& 67 &&
[GITA:19013] Do not impart this knowledge to one who does not practice austerity.
[GITA:19014] Never teach this to one who is not devoted to Me  and to one who does not
[GITA:19015] serve one ’s teachers. This should never ever be taught to one who has
[GITA:19016] hatred towards Me. (18.67)
[GITA:19029] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           409
[GITA:19031] Comments: This verse identifies four characteristics of those who
[GITA:19032] are unsuitable for receiving the teachings of the Gita. Sri Rayaru in GV
[GITA:19033] provides an interesting interpretation for  the use of the word ‘ cā’ (which
[GITA:19034] means ‘and’) in this verse to relate these four characteristics. This word
[GITA:19035] implies progressive harm in teaching the Gita to such categories of people.
[GITA:19036] Teaching those who are not austere is harmful. Teaching those who do not
[GITA:19037] serve teachers/elders is more harmful than teaching those who are not
[GITA:19038] austere. Teaching those who are not devoted to the Lord is even more
[GITA:19039] harmful than teaching those who do not serve teachers/elders. Finally,
[GITA:19040] teaching those who have hatred towards the Lo rd is most harmful.  The use
[GITA:19041] of the word ‘ kadācana’ (meaning ‘never’) indicates that even if someone
[GITA:19042] were to preach the Gita to those who may not be sufficiently austere or
[GITA:19043] may not adequately serve their elders/teachers, it should never be taught to
[GITA:19044] those not devoted to the Lord.

[GITA:19081] clarify that the deities also impart the knowledge of the Gita and they will

[GITA:19143] AOw©Z CdmM Ÿ&
[GITA:19144] Zï>mo  _moh… ñ_¥{Vb©ãYm ËdËàgmXmÝ_`m@À`wV Ÿ&

[GITA:19147] Arjuna said:  O Achyuta! My delusion is dis pelled. Through Your
[GITA:19148] grace, my sense of duty has been restored. I stand with deep conviction ,
[GITA:19149] with all my doubts removed. I will execute Your command. (18.73)
[GITA:19151] Comments: In this verse Arjuna responds to Lord Krishna
[GITA:19152] enthusiastically by stating  that his delusion has dissipated, and he is now
[GITA:19153] firmly convinced about his duty of waging the war to protect his citizens.
[GITA:19154] There are three important points that must be noted here -
[GITA:19156] (i) The Lord had asked Arjuna in the previous verse if Arjuna  had
[GITA:19157] listened to His sermon with attention and got all his doubts removed.
[GITA:19169] 412                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19170] Arjuna states that his doubts have been cleared because of the Lord’s grace
[GITA:19171] (tvatprasādāt). This implies that in addition to one 's effort, one needs the
[GITA:19172] Lord’s grace to succeed in any venture
[GITA:19174] (ii) Arjuna indicates that his sense of duty has been awakened. This
[GITA:19175] implies that Arjuna (who is an incarnation of deity Indra and  was well
[GITA:19176] versed in divine knowledge)  had knowledge  about his prescribed duties,
[GITA:19177] but that knowledge had been temporarily lost. Hence, he is stating that his
[GITA:19178] memory of divine knowledge has returned (smṛtir labdhā)
[GITA:19180] (iii) In verse 18.63, it was stated that the Lord’s concluding direction
[GITA:19181] to Arjuna stated in ‘yathecchasi tathā kuru’ was a rhetorical direction from
[GITA:19182] Him. It was by no means  granting Arjuna the freedom to do what he
[GITA:19183] wished. In this verse, A rjuna does not state that he would act as per his
[GITA:19184] wishes but that he would act as per the Lord’s words  - ‘kariṣye vacanaṁ
[GITA:19185] tava’. This confirms that the direction f rom Krishna to Arjuna in verse
[GITA:19186] 18.63 was indeed rhetorical.  Acting as per the Lord’s words is  the real
[GITA:19187] meaning of sharanagati (surrender) indicated in 18.66.

[GITA:19260] 414                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19261] It is my  firm belief that wherever there is the presence of Lord
[GITA:19262] Krishna (the Lord of all Yogas) and Arjuna, the holder of the bow, there
[GITA:19263] will be abundance of wealth, victory, glory, and everlasting justice. (18.78)
[GITA:19265] Comments: Sensing Dhrutarashtra’s curiosity abo ut the side that
[GITA:19266] won the war, Sanjaya indirectly answers the king by stating that the side
[GITA:19267] that has Krishna and Arjuna will always be victorious.
[GITA:19269] This verse can also be interpreted to indicate victory for the side that
[GITA:19270] had the presence of Lord Krishna an d deity Vayudeva. HH Sri Vidyasagara
[GITA:19271] Madhava Teertha provides the following explanation  for interpreting this
[GITA:19272] verse as indicating primarily the presence of deity Vayudeva along with
[GITA:19273] Lord Krishna.  As the Gita is a direct teaching by Lord Krishna, only
[GITA:19274] Vayudeva (who is superior most among the individual souls) can
[GITA:19275] comprehend the teachings fully. Arjuna, who has an instance of Indra can
[GITA:19276] receive the teachings in the Gita only because of special powers granted to
[GITA:19277] him by Vayudeva. Sri Madhwacharya has stated in  MBTN, Chapter 12,
[GITA:19278] verse 129 that Vayudeva had a special presence in Arjuna in the form of
[GITA:19279] ‘Veera’. In a conversation between Hanuman (a direct of incarnation of
[GITA:19280] Vayudeva) and Bheema (another incarnation of Vayudeva) in  the
[GITA:19281] Mahabharata, Hanuman assures Bheem a that during the Mahabharata
[GITA:19282] war, he would be present on the flag of Arjuna’s chariot and destroy the
[GITA:19283] enemies by a mere roar. This is the reason for Arjuna being referred to as
[GITA:19284] ‘kapi dwaja’ (verse 1.20). This incident is narrated by Sri Madhwacharya
[GITA:19285] in MBTN, chapter 22, verse 288 . The phrase ‘yatra pārthodhanurdharaḥ’
[GITA:19286] in this verse can also be derived as ‘ yatra pārtho adhanurdhara ḥ’, where
[GITA:19287] partha (son of Kunti) can be a reference to Bheema and adhanurdharaḥ is
[GITA:19288] an adjective that can be applied to Bheema as one who can fight a war
[GITA:19289] without any weapon (as dhanus means weapon). Atharva Upanishat (4.5)
[GITA:19290] compares a bow to the primordial syllable Om (which is the root of all
[GITA:19291] knowledge), the arrow to the mind of a seeker and the Lord Almighty to the
[GITA:19292] target, imp lying that one must focus one ’s mind on the Lord using the
[GITA:19293] wisdom of the Vedas to reach Him. Sri Madhwacharya in  his commentary
[GITA:19294] on Taittireeya Upanishat , interprets Bheema as the holder of all Vedic
[GITA:19306] Chapter 18                                                                                                                                           415
[GITA:19308] knowledge and hence the word ‘ dhanurdharaḥ’ (holder of bow) can be
[GITA:19309] interpreted to mean Bheema [GPH]
[GITA:19311] Now, the verse 18.78  can also be interpreted as follows - It is my
[GITA:19312] firm belief that wherever there is the presence of Lord Krishna (the Lord of
[GITA:19313] all Yogas), and Vayudeva, there will be a bundance of wealth, victory,
[GITA:19314] glory, and everlasting justice.

[GITA:19329] Concluding Benedictory Verse  (Gita Vivruti) : Sri Raghavendra

[GITA:19335] Summary of Chapter 18
[GITA:19337] This chapter has 78 verses. The first 55 verses contain the
[GITA:19338] conversation between Arjuna and Krishna regarding clarifications on
[GITA:19339] concepts previously covered in other chapters. The Lor d concludes His
[GITA:19340] teaching in the next 17 verses. Arjuna thanks the Lord in the 73rd verse. The
[GITA:19341] last 5 verses have concluding remarks from Sanjaya. Arjuna begins by
[GITA:19353] 416                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19354] asking Krishna what the difference between renunciation ( saṁnyāsa) and
[GITA:19355] relinquishment (tyāga) was, as both seem to imply the same. In verse (5.2),
[GITA:19356] it was stated that renunciation ( sanyāsa) was essential to attain liberation
[GITA:19357] (moksha), and in verse 12.12 , relinquishment ( tyāga) was lauded as a
[GITA:19358] superior means to attain liberation ( moksha). Arjuna wan ts to know about
[GITA:19359] relative merits of these two approaches. The Lord provides answers to
[GITA:19360] Arjuna’s questions with a detailed description of the various aspects of
[GITA:19361] renunciation and relinquishment in verses 18.2 to 18.12 . In chapter 5
[GITA:19362] (verses 14, 15) the concep t of doership of activities was briefly described.
[GITA:19363] This aspect is expa nded in this chapter in verses 18.13 to 18.18 . In chapter
[GITA:19364] 2, verse 45, it was stated that a seeker must strive to understand the inner
[GITA:19365] meanings of rituals indicated in the Vedas and not just accept the
[GITA:19366] superficial meaning. This point is elaborated in this chapter. In chapter 14,
[GITA:19367] the influence and impact of the three qualities  of nature on living beings
[GITA:19368] was discussed. In this chapter, additional aspects of the qualities of na ture
[GITA:19369] are elaborated in verses 18.19 to 18.39. Previously, in verse 4.13 , the Lord
[GITA:19370] identified the categorization of the society based on the innate nature and
[GITA:19371] activities of individuals. In this chapter, this c oncept is elaborated in verses
[GITA:19372] 18.40 to 18.48. Verses 18.49 to  18.55 provide details of the methods for
[GITA:19373] one to achieve salvation ( moksha), as that is the goa l of all living beings.
[GITA:19374] Verses 18.68 to 18.71  describes the glory of the Gita (more details on
[GITA:19375] Gita’s glory appears in Annexure 1). Sanjaya concludes his commentary on
[GITA:19376] the battleground to King Dhrutarashtra in verses 18.74 to 18.78  and
[GITA:19377] indirectly answers the King’s question about the side that won the war by
[GITA:19378] stating that the side that has Lord Krishna and  the warrior Arjuna will
[GITA:19379] always be victorious.
[GITA:19381] && B{V Aï>mXemo@Ü`m`…  &&
