[GITA:19463] Summary: This passage which extols the virtues of the Gita is from the
[GITA:19464] epic Varaha Purana . Go ddess Dharadevi (the governing deity for earth)
[GITA:19465] asks Lord Vishnu how human beings (earth dwellers) can realize the Lord
[GITA:19466] when they are preoccupied with worldly afflictions . The Lord teaches her
[GITA:19467] about the glory of the Gita which helps human beings navigate the river of
[GITA:19478] Annexure 1                                                                                                                                419
[GITA:19481] worldly afflictions. The greatness of the Gita as stated by the Lord  can be
[GITA:19482] summarized as follows.
[GITA:19484] - Those who are engaged in the practice of reciting the Gita will not
[GITA:19485] be entangled by their actions.
[GITA:19486] - The place where one finds books on the Gita or ongoing lectures on
[GITA:19487] the Gita is said to be the home of all great, sacred rivers and
[GITA:19488] pilgrimage centers.
[GITA:19489] - It is also the place where great sages and yogis reside. The Lord also
[GITA:19490] resides there.
[GITA:19491] - The greatness of the Gita derives from the fact that  they are th e
[GITA:19492] words of the Lord Himself in the form of Krishna, who is full of
[GITA:19493] infinite auspicious attributes.
[GITA:19494] - One who recites and studies the Gita daily will attain liberation.
[GITA:19495] - One who utters the word ‘Gita’ at the time of leaving one’s body will
[GITA:19496] reach the Lord.
[GITA:19497] - Even those who have sinned will be rid of their sins if they have
[GITA:19498] read, analyze d, and underst ood the true meaning of the Gita. They
[GITA:19499] too achieve salvation.
[GITA:19500] - Great emperors such as Janaka reached higher destination s due to
[GITA:19501] their study of the Gita.
[GITA:19503] One must study  the glory of the Gita after completing the study of the
[GITA:19504] Gita for maximum benefit.
[GITA:19506] && lr JrVm‘mhmËå¶‘² g§nyU©‘² &&
[GITA:19507] End of Glory of the Gita
[GITA:19519] 420                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19520] Annexure 2 – The Bhagavad Gita: Philosophical
[GITA:19521] Interpretation
[GITA:19523] The verses in the Gita have multiple meanings, each o f them being
[GITA:19524] consistent with the overall narrative. The first and the obvious
[GITA:19525] interpretation is based on the historical meaning of the verses. Another
[GITA:19526] subtle interpretation is based on the philosophical meaning of the verses.
[GITA:19527] Sri Madhwacharya places a lot of importance o n the philosophical aspects
[GITA:19528] of the Gita by stating in his Mahabharata Tatparya Nirnaya  (MBTN
[GITA:19529] 2.146) that the Mahabharata is not just a historical account of the lives of
[GITA:19530] the Pandavas and the Kauravas; it also is a deeply philosophical work .  Sri
[GITA:19531] Pangari Sreenivasacharya’s Gita Vivruti Adhyatma Artha  [GVAA] has
[GITA:19532] examples of multiple interpretations of the verses in the Gita.
[GITA:19534] It is said that the Bhagavad Gita is an embodiment of dharma (the
[GITA:19535] righteous way of living). This is further confirmed by  reviewing the first
[GITA:19536] letter of the first verse (1.1) – dhar and the  last letter of the last verse
[GITA:19537] 18.78 – ma. Thus, the Gita, which is encapsulated between the letters, dhar
[GITA:19538] and ma, is an embodiment of dharma.
[GITA:19540] To illustrate the philosophical interpretat ion of the Gita, Sri
[GITA:19541] Vidyasagara Madhava Teertha provides an interesting interpretation of the
[GITA:19542] first MTNP and last verses which is summarized below -
[GITA:19544] Y¥Vamï´> CdmM Ÿ-
[GITA:19545] Y_©joÌo Hw$éjoÌo g_doVm `w`wËgd… &
[GITA:19546] _m_H$m… nmÊS>dmü¡d {H$_Hw$d©V g§ÄO` Ÿ&& 1.1&&
[GITA:19548] The w ord dhṛtarāṣṭra is comprised of the words dhṛta and rāṣṭra,
[GITA:19549] where rāṣṭra = worldly miseries and dhṛta = the one bearing.  Hence, the
[GITA:19550] name dhṛtarāṣṭra represents a student, and indeed,  all of us who are
[GITA:19551] immersed in worldly afflictions. The name sañjaya is m ade up of root
[GITA:19552] words samyak and jayati (the one who has soundly conquered worldly
[GITA:19553] miseries) and represents a teacher who has overcome worldly miseries .
[GITA:19565] Annexure 2                                                                                                                                         421
[GITA:19567] Thus, this verse represents a conversation between a student and a teacher.
[GITA:19568] dharmakṣetra is based on the  word dharma (derived from the word
[GITA:19569] dharana, the one who protects, in other words the Lord Almighty).
[GITA:19570] kurukṣetra refers to kṣetra with the qualifier kuru which refers to the one
[GITA:19571] who is duty bound (as derived from the root word kru which indicates
[GITA:19572] action). Hence kurukṣetra can mean a person’s physical body. The word
[GITA:19573] māmakā is used by Dhrutarashtra to mean ‘my clan’ where ‘my’ signifies
[GITA:19574] ego which represents the demoni ac forces in our bod ies. In another
[GITA:19575] interpretation, the word ‘ ma’ represents knowledge and mamaka means
[GITA:19576] knowledge that is not evolved ( or ignorance). The word pāṇḍavā is derived
[GITA:19577] from root words  padi and gati which means moving towards knowledge ,
[GITA:19578] and hence is a representation of the angelic forces in our bodies  who
[GITA:19579] embody knowledge ( jnana). Thus, the Kauravas represent ignorance
[GITA:19580] (ajnana) and the Pandavas embody knowledge (jnana).
[GITA:19582] With these interpretations, the first verse can now be translated as
[GITA:19583] follows:
[GITA:19585] Dhrutarashtra (one who is enmeshed in worldly affliction) said -
[GITA:19587] O Sanjaya (the one who has soundly conquered worldly miseries)! In
[GITA:19588] Kurukshetra ( the physical body ) which houses dharmakṣetra (the Lord
[GITA:19589] Almighty), what was the outcome of the struggle (internal struggle)
[GITA:19590] between my clan (demoniac forces represented by ignorance) and the
[GITA:19591] Pandavas (angelic forces representing the knowledge)?
[GITA:19593] The central concept in the philosophical int erpretation of verse (1.1)
[GITA:19594] is about the internal struggle between the angelic and demoni ac forces and
[GITA:19595] its impact on one’s activities.
[GITA:19597] Now, the philosophical interpretation of the last verse follows -
[GITA:19599] `Ì `moJoœa… H¥$îUmo `Ì nmWm} YZwY©a… Ÿ&
[GITA:19600] VÌ lr{d©O`mo ^y{VY«w©dm Zr{V_©{V_©_ Ÿ&& 18. 78 &&
[GITA:19612] 422                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19614] This verse is the concluding response by Sanjaya to King
[GITA:19615] Dhrutarashtra’s question in verse (1.1).  Here, Lord Krishna is described as
[GITA:19616] yogeśvaraḥ (the one who controls all paths and ways to achieve liberation)
[GITA:19617] since He has  described various paths such as karma yoga, jnana yoga,
[GITA:19618] dhyana yoga, and bhakti yoga for a seeker to achieve liberation. Arjuna, an
[GITA:19619] incarnation of the deity Indra with an  instance of the serpent deity Sesha
[GITA:19620] (nara) in him is knowledgeable about performing prescribed duties and
[GITA:19621] represents living beings. With these interpretations, verse 18.78 can now be
[GITA:19622] translated as follows -
[GITA:19624] All actions, where there is the presence of Lor d Almighty Krishna
[GITA:19625] (the Lord of all yogas), and Arjuna (a representative of all living beings),
[GITA:19626] will through the Lord’s grace result in great riches and success, eventually
[GITA:19627] leading to liberation.
[GITA:19629] In summary, the first verse posed a question about the outc ome of
[GITA:19630] the internal struggle between demoniac forces ( ignorance) and angelic
[GITA:19631] forces (knowledge) within all living beings , and the last verse answers by
[GITA:19632] stating that all actions where there is the presence of the Lord and Arjuna
[GITA:19633] (one who is aware of prescribed duties) will succeed fully.
[GITA:19645] Annexure 3                                                                                                                                      423
[GITA:19648] Annexure 3 – The Bhagavad Gita and Dvaita Vedanta
[GITA:19650] Sri Madhwacharya, the great saint, and philosopher of the 12 th
[GITA:19651] century was a proponent of Dvaita Vedanta (philosophy of theistic dualism)
[GITA:19652] built on the foundational premise of the difference between individual souls
[GITA:19653] and the Supreme Soul (the Lord Almighty). Sri Madhwacharya has
[GITA:19654] composed over 37 works with seminal commentaries on the Gita, the
[GITA:19655] Vedas, the Upanishads, the Brahma Sutras , and epics such as the
[GITA:19656] Ramayana and the Mahabharata. In all his works, he quotes extensively
[GITA:19657] from these scriptures. In fact, his very first literary work was his
[GITA:19658] commentary on the Gita (Gita Bhashya). Sri Vyasa Teertha (16th century),
[GITA:19659] a great philosopher  and scholar from Sri Madhwa’s lineage has
[GITA:19660] summarized the philosophy of Sri Madhwacharya in a single verse,
[GITA:19661] popularly known as nava prameya  (the 9 tenets). In this section, the
[GITA:19662] relationship between these nine tenets and the teachings from the Gita are
[GITA:19663] described to emphasize the scriptural basis for Dvaita Vedanta.
[GITA:19665] Sri Vyasa Teertha’s Nava Prameya
[GITA:19667] lr‘Ý‘Üd‘Vo h[a… naVa… gË¶§ OJV² VÎdVmo
[GITA:19668] ^oXmo OrdJUm… haoaZwMam… ZrMmoƒ^md“Vm… &
[GITA:19669] ‘w{³VZ£OgwImZw^y{Va‘bm^{³Vü VËgmYZ§
[GITA:19670] øjm{X{ÌV¶§ à‘mU‘{IbmåZm¶¡H$doÚmo h[a… &&
[GITA:19672] The Nine Tenets of Sri Madhwa’s Philosophy
[GITA:19674] 1. Lord Sri Hari is the Supreme Being
[GITA:19675] 2. This world is real
[GITA:19676] 3. The differences (between the Lord, the individual souls, and inert
[GITA:19677] objects) are real
[GITA:19678] 4. Individual souls are under the control of Lord Sri Hari
[GITA:19679] 5. Individual souls have gradation in attributes
[GITA:19680] 6. Liberation is the ultimate experience of innate happiness
[GITA:19681] 7. Pure devotion to the Lord leads to liberation
[GITA:19693] 424                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19694] 8. Direct knowledge, inference and scriptures are the evidence to
[GITA:19695] establish the truth
[GITA:19696] 9. The Lord is knowable through the Vedas
[GITA:19698] As will be  seen, these nine principles are woven throughout the
[GITA:19699] verses in the Gita. Following are some selected verses from the Gita to
[GITA:19700] establish their correspondence with these nine tenets.
[GITA:19702] 1. Supremacy of the Lord Almighty: Lord Sri Hari is the
[GITA:19703] Supreme Entity
[GITA:19705] (i) Verse 7.7: The Lord states mattaḥ parataraṁ nānyat kiṁcid asti –
[GITA:19706] there is no entity in the universe that is superior to Me.
[GITA:19707] (ii) Verse 8.20 : The Lord states paras tasmāt tu bhāvonyo  – The
[GITA:19708] Lord is the entity that is independent, superior to and different from
[GITA:19709] everything in the universe.
[GITA:19710] (iii) Verse 15.16 : The Lord states uttamaḥ puruṣastvanyaḥ
[GITA:19711] paramātmety udāhṛtaḥ - the entity known as Paramatma is superior
[GITA:19712] to and different from all other entities.
[GITA:19713] (iv) Verse 11.43: Arjuna states na tvatsamosty abhyadhika ḥ kutonyo
[GITA:19714] – there is no o ne equal to You (Krishna) in this universe. How can
[GITA:19715] there be any one more superior?
[GITA:19717] 2. Realism of the world: The world is real
[GITA:19719] (i) Verse 9.10 : The Lord states mayādhyakṣeṇa prakṛtiḥ s ūyate
[GITA:19720] sacarācaram – under My direct supervision, Mother Nature creates
[GITA:19721] this world made of movable and immovable objects  (The Lord uses
[GITA:19722] the term ādhyakṣa which is derived from the word akṣa which means
[GITA:19723] seeing. The Lord physically oversees the process of creation of the
[GITA:19724] universe. As the Lord is real, so is the universe).
[GITA:19725] (ii) Verse 11.7: The Lord states ihaikastham jagat kṛtsnaṁ paśyādya
[GITA:19726] sacarācaram – look at the entire universe (jagat) situated in Me (The
[GITA:19727] Lord grants Arjuna divine  vision to view the entire universe within
[GITA:19728] Him).
[GITA:19739] Annexure 3                                                                                                                                      425
[GITA:19742] (iii) Verse 16.8 : The Lord states asatyam aprati ṣṭhaṁ te jagad āhur
[GITA:19743] anīśvaram. They say that the world is unreal and is not dependent on
[GITA:19744] the Lord Almighty  (The Lord describes the characteristics of those
[GITA:19745] with demoniac nature and states that they view the world ( jagat) as
[GITA:19746] unreal, thereby clarifying the principle of the reality of the world).
[GITA:19748] 3. The fivefold differences (Pancha Bheda) are real
[GITA:19750] The three entities in the universe, namely, the Lord Almighty, the
[GITA:19751] individual souls, and inert objects are different from one another.
[GITA:19752] (i) Verse 13.22 : puruṣaḥ prakṛtistho  hi bhu ṅkte prakṛtij ān gu ṇān.
[GITA:19753] Individual souls residing in the body, comprised of the elements of
[GITA:19754] nature, experience emotions through contact with the three attributes
[GITA:19755] of nature which are inert objects. This establishes the difference
[GITA:19756] between individual souls and inert objects.
[GITA:19757] (ii) Verse 13.31 : yadā bhūtap ṛthagbhāvam ekastham anupaśyati .
[GITA:19758] The same Lord resides in multitudes of different ( pṛthak) living
[GITA:19759] beings. The entire 17 th chapter is about the three types of intrinsic
[GITA:19760] faith in living beings as indicated by the Lord in verse (17.2) trividhā
[GITA:19761] bhavati śraddhā dehinā ṁ s ā svabhāvajā  - Living beings are
[GITA:19762] predisposed based on their innate nature into one of three qualities -
[GITA:19763] sattvic, rajasic or tamasic. This establishes the difference s among
[GITA:19764] individual souls.
[GITA:19765] (iii) Verses 13.6 and 13.7  enumerated the different components of
[GITA:19766] nature that impact an individual’s personality. This establishes the
[GITA:19767] differences  among inert objects.
[GITA:19768] (iv) Verse 7.4 : bhūmir āponalo vāyu ḥ khaṁ mano buddhir eva ca|
[GITA:19769] ahaṁkāra itīya ṁ me bhinn ā pr akṛtir aṣṭadh ā||. The Lord states -
[GITA:19770] Earth, water, fire, wind, space, mind, intellect, and individuation are
[GITA:19771] the eight different parts of inert nature that are under My control.
[GITA:19772] This establishes the difference between the Lord and inert objects ,
[GITA:19773] and among inert objects.
[GITA:19774] (v) Verse 15.16 : The Lord states uttamaḥ puruṣastvanyaḥ
[GITA:19775] paramātmety udāhṛtaḥ - the entity known as Paramatma is superior
[GITA:19787] 426                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19788] to and different from all other entities. This establishes the difference
[GITA:19789] between the Lord and individual souls.
[GITA:19791] 4. Individual souls are dependent on the Lord (they do not have
[GITA:19792] independent doership - kartṛtva)
[GITA:19794] (i) Verse 5.14 : The Lord states na kart ṛtvaṁ na karm āṇi – living
[GITA:19795] beings cannot act independently.
[GITA:19796] (ii) Verse 15.9 : The Lord states śrotraṁ cakṣuḥ sparśanaṁ ca
[GITA:19797] rasanaṁ ghrāṇam eva ca| adhiṣṭh āya manaś cāya ṁ viṣay ān
[GITA:19798] upasevate|| - The Lord resides in the sense organs - ears, eyes, skin,
[GITA:19799] tongue, nose, and mind and verily consumes the (righteous) objects
[GITA:19800] of sense pursuits. This clarifies that living beings are dependent on
[GITA:19801] the independent Lord Almighty.
[GITA:19802] (iii) Verse 18.61 : The Lord states īśvara ḥ sarvabh ūtānāṁ
[GITA:19803] hṛddeśerjuna tiṣṭhati|  bhrāmayan sarvabhūtāni yantrārū ḍhāni
[GITA:19804] māyayā|| - O Arjuna! The omnipotent Lord, residing in the hearts of
[GITA:19805] all living beings, propels them to perfo rm various activities through
[GITA:19806] His own free will. This further conf irms that living beings are
[GITA:19807] dependent on the independent Lord Almighty.
[GITA:19809] 5. Individual souls have gradations
[GITA:19811] Individual souls have different innate capabilities and eventually
[GITA:19812] attain different states.
[GITA:19813] (i) Verse 16.5 : The Lord states daivī sa ṁpad vimokṣ āya - Divine
[GITA:19814] nature paves the way for levels of liberation. vimokṣā is derived as
[GITA:19815] vividha + mokṣā, meaning different levels of bliss in liberation based
[GITA:19816] on the innate abilities (yogyata) and efforts (sadhana) of souls.
[GITA:19817] (ii) Verse 17.2: The Lord states trividhā bhavati śraddhā dehinā ṁ sā
[GITA:19818] svabhāvajā - Living beings are predisposed based on their innate
[GITA:19819] nature into one of three qualities - sattvic, rajasic or tamasic.
[GITA:19820] (iii) Verse 3.42: The Lord states indriyāṇi parāṇy āhur indriyebhyaḥ
[GITA:19821] paraṁ manaḥ| manasas tu parā buddhir yo buddheḥ paratas tu saḥ||
[GITA:19822] - It is said that the sense organs are superior, and the mind is more
[GITA:19833] Annexure 3                                                                                                                                      427
[GITA:19836] superior to them. The i ntellect is superior to the mind and ultimate
[GITA:19837] consciousness is even more superior to the intellect. Her e the entities
[GITA:19838] of the sense organs, the mind and the intellect refer to the respective
[GITA:19839] governing deities. This establishes gradation among the deities.
[GITA:19841] 6. Liberation is the ultimate state of innate happiness
[GITA:19843] (i) Verse 14.27 : The Lord states śāśvatasya ca dh armasya
[GITA:19844] sukhasyaikāntikasya ca. Moksha  is defined as the state of pure ,
[GITA:19845] unending bliss.
[GITA:19846] (ii) Verse 18.71 : The Lord states sopi mukta ḥ śubh āṁl lok ān
[GITA:19847] prāpnuyāt pu ṇyakarmaṇām – (the one who listens to our
[GITA:19848] conversations) will be liberated and will be in the wo rld of exalted,
[GITA:19849] virtuous souls.
[GITA:19851] 7. Pure devotion leads to liberation
[GITA:19853] (i) Verse 8.22  – The Lord states puruṣaḥ sa paraḥ p ārtha bhaktyā
[GITA:19854] labhyas tv ananyayā   - The Supreme One is reachable only by pure,
[GITA:19855] unadulterated devotion.
[GITA:19856] (ii) Verse 11.54  – the Lord state s bhaktyā tv ananyayā śakya aham
[GITA:19857] evaṁvidhorjuna - Only by single minded devotion can one
[GITA:19858] understand Me.
[GITA:19859] (iii) Verse 12.20 – the Lord states śraddadhānā matparamā bhaktās
[GITA:19860] tetīva me priyā ḥ - One who observes these methods sincerely, with
[GITA:19861] deep faith and devotion in Me, is indeed very dear to Me.
[GITA:19862] (iv) Verse 18.68  – the Lord states ya ima ṁ paramaṁ guhyaṁ
[GITA:19863] madbhakteṣv abhidh āsyati| bhakti ṁ mayi par āṁ kṛtv ā mām
[GITA:19864] evaiṣyaty asaṁśayaḥ|| - One who imparts this highly secretive
[GITA:19865] knowledge to My devotees will develop deep devotion to Me and
[GITA:19866] will reach My abode. Let there not be any doubt in this.
[GITA:19867] (v) Verse 14.26  – The Lord states māṁ ca yovyabhic āreṇa
[GITA:19868] bhaktiyogena sevate| sa gu ṇān samatītyaitān brahmabhūyāya
[GITA:19869] kalpate|| - One who worships Me with pure, un alloyed devotion will
[GITA:19870] indeed be able to reach beyond the three qualities and attain the
[GITA:19882] 428                                                                                                                             The Bhagavad Gita
[GITA:19883] abode of Mother Nature - Goddess Mahalakshmi (which is also My
[GITA:19884] abode).
[GITA:19886] 8. The three types of evidence are the sources of knowledge
[GITA:19888] The methods of obtaining true knowledge constitute a fundam ental
[GITA:19889] part of epistemology. Sri Madhwacharya defines the means of
[GITA:19890] knowledge ( pramanas) as pratyaksha (sense perception), anumana
[GITA:19891] (inference) and agama (scriptural). Pratyaksha is the contact of a
[GITA:19892] defectless sense organ with a defectless object. Anumana is
[GITA:19893] defectless syllogism. Aagama is defectless verbal composition
[GITA:19894] (ex: Vedas).
[GITA:19896] (i) Verse 11.5 : The Lord states paśya me pārtha rūpā ṇi śataśotha
[GITA:19897] sahastraśaḥ| n ānāvidhāni divyāni nānāvar ṇākṛtīni ca||  The Lord
[GITA:19898] asks Arjuna to see His infinite forms. The Lord had given Arjuna
[GITA:19899] Divine Vision (which is defectless) with which Arjuna is able to see
[GITA:19900] the Lord (who is defectless). This is an example of pratyaksha
[GITA:19901] pramana.
[GITA:19902] (ii) Verse 7.7 : The Lord states mayi sarvam ida ṁ protaṁ s ūtre
[GITA:19903] maṇigaṇā iva - Everything in the unive rse is supported by Me, just
[GITA:19904] like a garland of pearls is supported by a string. When one sees a
[GITA:19905] garland of pearls, the string which holds the pearls together is
[GITA:19906] normally not visible. But one can infer the presence of the string as
[GITA:19907] the pearls cannot hold th emselves together. This is like inferring the
[GITA:19908] presence of fire on a hill just by watching the smoke from a distance,
[GITA:19909] as smoke will be visible only when there is fire. This is an example
[GITA:19910] of anumana pramana.
[GITA:19911] (iii) Verse 16.24 : The Lord states tasmāc chāstra ṁ pram āṇaṁ te
[GITA:19912] kāryākāryavyavasthitau - Therefore, scriptures are your guide in
[GITA:19913] performing right  deeds and avoiding wrong  deeds. The Lord states
[GITA:19914] that shastram (scriptures) are the pramanas (means) to understand
[GITA:19915] right and wrong deeds. This is an example of agama pramana.
[GITA:19928] Annexure 3                                                                                                                                      429
[GITA:19931] 9. The Lord is knowable through the Vedas
[GITA:19933] (i) Verse 7.8: The Lord states praṇavaḥ sarvavedeṣu - I am the
[GITA:19934] primordial syllable Om in the Vedas.
[GITA:19935] (ii) Verse 15.15: The Lord states vedaiś ca sarvair aham eva vedyo  -
[GITA:19936] I am the one exclusively described in all Vedas.
[GITA:19937] (iii)) Verse (15.18): The Lord states atosmi loke vede ca prathita ḥ
[GITA:19938] puruṣottamaḥ - I am known as the Supreme Being and described as
[GITA:19939] such in scriptures that are composed (loka) and revealed (the Vedas).
